Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
The Validity of a Judge's Letter When the Writing Judge Loses Qualification
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kitab al-qadi validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on kitab al-qadi when the writing judge becomes disqualified before the letter is read, and distinguish it from the position of Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is void if the writing judge loses qualification before the receiving judge reads it in court.

In Islamic judicial procedure, a judge may write to another judge to transfer testimony or a ruling. But what happens if the writing judge dies or loses his position before the letter is read? This lesson explores the Hanafi position and its reasoning, contrasting it with the view of Imam Abu Yusuf, who considers the letter valid once written and sealed. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi emphasis on the completion of the transfer of testimony.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Condition
Identify the condition that the writing judge must be qualified at the time the receiving judge reads the letter to the defendant. If the writing judge dies, is dismissed, or becomes insane before that point, the letter becomes void.
This condition is unique to the Hanafi school and is derived from the analogy to testimony.
2
Identify the Opposing View
Recognize that Imam Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school), along with Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, hold the letter valid even if the writing judge dies after writing and sealing. Their proof is based on analogy (qiyas) to shahadah ala al-shahadah.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; Abu Yusuf's view is recorded but not taken as mufta bihi.
3
Analyse the Opponent's Qiyas
The opposing view argues that writing and sealing the letter completes the transfer of testimony, just as secondary witnesses complete their testimony by speaking. Therefore, the death of the writing judge after that point does not invalidate the letter.
The key illa (effective cause) is the completion of the transfer by writing.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response refutes the analogy: the transfer of testimony is not complete until the letter reaches the receiving judge and is read in court. The death of the writing judge before reading is like the death of secondary witnesses before they perform their testimony, which nullifies the testimony.
The Hanafi school thus distinguishes the moment of completion: it is the reading, not the writing, that finalizes the transfer.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
Under the Hanafi mufta bihi (Abu Hanifa's view), if the writing judge loses qualification before the letter is read, the receiving judge must not accept or act on the letter. Under Abu Yusuf's view, he would act. This difference affects judicial procedure in practice.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: action vs. no action.

صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ قاضی مکتوب الیہ مذکورہ خط اس وقت قبول کرے گا جب کہ قاضی کا تب، منصب قضاء پر فائز ہو ۔ چنانچہ اگر قاضی کا تب مر گیا یا معزول کر دیا گیا یا جنون یا بیہوشی یا مرتد ہونے یا دار الحرب میں چلے جانے یا بعض حضرات کے نزدیک فسق کی وجہ سے اہمیت قضا سے خارج ہو گیا۔ حالانکہ ابھی تک خط قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے پاس نہیں پہنچا یا خط پہنچ تو گیا مگر قاضی مکتوب الیہ مدعی الیہ کو پڑھ کر نہیں سنایا تو یہ خط باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اور قاضی مکتوب الیہ اس کو قبول نہیں کرے گا۔ اور اس کے مطابق مدعی علیہ کے خلاف کوئی فیصلہ نہیں کرے گا حضرت امام ابو یوسف امام شافعی اور امام احمد نے فرمایا کہ قاضی مکتوب الیہ اس حال میں بھی خط کو قبول کر کے اُسی کے مطابق عمل کرے گا۔ ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کتاب القاضی الی القاضی ، شہادت علی الشہادت کے مانند ہے۔ کیونکہ کتاب القاضی کے ذریعہ مکتوب الیہ کی طرف اُن گواہوں کی شہادت کو منتقل کیا جاتا ہے جن گواہوں نے قاضی کا تب کے پاس گواہی دی ہے اور گواہی نقل کرنا، کتاب لیے لکھنے سے مکمل ہو گیا ہے۔ پس خط پہنچنے سے پہلے قاضی کا تب کا مرنا یا اہمیت قضاء سے خارج ہونا ایسا ہے جیسے شہود فرع ادائے شہادت کے بعد فیصلہ سے پہلے مر گئے ہوں اور شہود فرع کا ادائے شہادت کے بعد قاضی کے فیصلہ دینے سے پہلے مر جانا قضائے قاضی کے لئے مانع نہیں ہوتا ، بلکہ قاضی ان کے مرنے کے بعد بھی ان کی شہادت علی الشہادت کی بنیاد پر فیصلہ دے گا۔ اسی طرح خط تحریر کر کے مہر وغیرہ لگانے کے بعد اگر قاضی کا تب مر گیا تو بھی قاضی مکتوب الیہ اس خط کو قبول کرے گا اور اس پر عمل کرے گا۔ لیکن ہماری طرف سے اس دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ محض کتابت اور تحریر سے شہادت کو نقل کر نا مکمل نہیں ہوتا۔ بلکہ نقل شہادت اس وقت پورا ہوگا جب خط قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے پاس پہنچ جائے گا ۔ اور قاضی مکتوب الیہ اس کو مدعی علیہ کے سامنے پڑھ کر سنا دے ہیں قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے خط کو پڑھ کر سنانے سے پہلے قاضی کا تب کا مرجانا ایسا ہے جیسے شہود فرع ادائے شہادت سے پہلے مرجائیں۔ اور شہود فرع اگر ادائے شہادت سے پہلے مرجائیں تو قاضی کوئی فیصلہ نہیں دے گا۔ پس اسی طرح قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے خط پڑھ کر سنانے سے پہلے قاضی کا تب مر گیا یا قضاء کا اہل نہ رہا تو بھی قاضی مکتوب الیہ اس خط پر عمل نہیں کرے گا اور کوئی فیصلہ نہ دے گا۔ خط قبول نہ ہونے پر طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے خط پڑھ کر سنانے سے پہلے اگر قاضی کا تب مر گیا یا معزول ہو گیا یا جنون وغیرہ کی وجہ سے اہلیت قضاء سے خارج ہو گیا تو وہ رعایا میں سے ایک شخص ہو گیا یعنی عام آدمی کی طرح ہو گیا اور جب قاضی کا تب حاکم نہ رہا بلکہ عام آدمی ہو گیا تو خط کے ذریعہ اس کا فیصلہ اور حکم بھی نافذ نہ ہوگا کیونکہ عام آدمی کا کوئی فیصلہ نافذ نہیں ہوتا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر ایک قاضی نے دوسرے قاضی کو اپنے ولایت قضاء کے علاوہ دوسرے شہر میں کوئی خبر دی مثلاً یہ کہا کہ فلاں شخص کا فلاں شخص پر حق ثابت ہے تو اُس دوسرے شہر کا قاضی محض اس خبر پر فیصلہ نہ دے گا۔ کیونکہ خبر دینے والا قاضی اپنی ولایت قضاء کے علاوہ دوسرے شہر میں ایک عام آدمی کی طرح ہے اور محض ایک عام آدمی کی خبر پر فیصلہ نہیں دیا جا تا۔ لہذ امذ کورہ قاضی کی خبر پر بھی فیصلہ نہ دیا جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر دو قاضی ایسے شہر میں جمع ہو گئے جو دونوں کی ولایت قضاء سے باہر ہے اور ان میں سے ایک نے دوسرے کو خبر دی کہ میرے نزدیک فلاں کا فلاں پر حق ثابت ہے تو وہ اس خبر پر عمل نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ دونوں حضرات اس شہر میں عام آدمیوں کی طرح ہیں اور عام آدمیوں کا فیصلہ شرعاً نافذ نہیں ہوتا ۔ لہذا ان کا فیصلہ بھی اپنی ولایت قضاء کے علاوہ میں نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ اس دلیل پر آپ کا اشکال ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ آپ نے فرمایا کہ اگر قاضی کا تب مر گیا یا معزول ہو گیا یا جنون وغیرہ کی وجہ سے اہلیت قضاء سے خارج ہو گیا تو وہ رعایا میں سے ایک شخص ہو گیا یعنی عام آدمی کی طرح ہو گیا۔ حالانکہ معزول ہونے کی صورت میں تو قاضی کا عام آدمی کی طرح ہونا ظاہر ہے۔ لیکن موت اور جنون کی صورت میں اس کو عام آدمی کے ساتھ کیسے لاحق کیا جا سکتا ہے؟ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ فاضل مصنف کا کلام ترقى من الادنى الىی الاعلی کے قبیل سے ہے۔ یعنی اگر قاضی کا تب زندہ ہو اور قضاء کا اہل بھی ہو مگر قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے پاس خطا پہنچنے سے پہلے معزول ہو گیا تو اس کا کلام حجت نہیں ہو گا ۔ پس جس صورت میں قاضی کا تب زندہ ہی نہ رہا یا زندہ تو ہے مگر جنون وغیرہ کی وجہ سے قضاء کا اہل نہ رہا تو اس صورت میں اس کا کلام بدرجہ اولیٰ حجت نہیں ہوگا۔ اس تقریر کے بعد کوئی اشکال واقع نہ ہوگا۔
The author of Hidayah said: The judge to whom a letter is sent will accept the mentioned letter only when the writing judge is qualified for the position of judgment. So if the writing judge died, or was dismissed, or due to insanity, unconsciousness, apostasy, going to Dar al-Harb, or according to some, due to sin (fisq), he left the importance of judgment; while the letter has not yet reached the judge to whom it is sent, or it reached but the judge to whom it is sent has not read it to the defendant, then this letter becomes void, and the judge to whom it is sent will not accept it, and will not pass any judgment against the defendant accordingly. Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad said: The judge to whom it is sent will in this situation also accept the letter and act accordingly. Their proof is that the book of a judge to a judge is like testimony upon testimony (shahadah ala al-shahadah), because through the judge's book, the testimony of those witnesses who testified before the writing judge is transferred to the judge to whom it is sent, and the transfer of testimony is completed by writing the book. So the death of the writing judge before the letter reaches or his leaving the importance of judgment is like when the secondary witnesses die after performing testimony but before the verdict, and the death of secondary witnesses after performing testimony before the judge passes verdict does not prevent the judge's verdict; rather the judge will pass verdict on the basis of their shahadah ala al-shahadah even after their death. Similarly, after writing the letter and affixing the seal, if the writing judge dies, the judge to whom it is sent will accept the letter and act accordingly. But our response to this proof is that merely writing and composing does not complete the transfer of testimony. Rather, the transfer of testimony is completed only when the letter reaches the judge to whom it is sent, and the judge to whom it is sent reads it to the defendant. The death of the writing judge before the judge to whom it is sent reads the letter is like when secondary witnesses die before performing testimony. And if secondary witnesses die before performing testimony, the judge does not pass any verdict. So similarly, if the writing judge died or became unfit for judgment before the judge to whom it is sent reads the letter, then the judge to whom it is sent will not act upon this letter and will not pass any verdict. The proof for non-acceptance by both parties is that if before the judge to whom it is sent reads the letter, the writing judge died, was dismissed, or due to insanity etc. left eligibility for judgment, then he becomes one of the subjects, i.e., like an ordinary person. And when the writing judge is no longer a ruler but became an ordinary person, his judgment and command through the letter are also not effective, because the judgment of an ordinary person is not enforced. This is why if one judge gives news to another judge in a city outside his jurisdiction of judgment, for example he said that a certain person has a right against another, the judge of that other city will not pass judgment merely on this news, because the giving judge outside his jurisdiction is like an ordinary person, and judgment is not passed merely on the news of an ordinary person. So similarly, judgment is not passed on the news of said judge. Likewise, if two judges gather in a city that is outside the jurisdiction of both, and one of them informs the other that in my view such and such has a right against such and such, he cannot act on this information, because both persons in that city are like ordinary people, and the judgment of ordinary people is not enforceable in Shari'ah. So their judgment is also not effective outside their jurisdiction. Upon this proof, there is an objection: you said that if the writing judge died or was dismissed or due to insanity etc. left eligibility for judgment, he becomes one of the subjects, i.e., like an ordinary person; whereas in the case of dismissal it is obvious that the judge becomes like an ordinary person, but how can death and insanity be attached to an ordinary person? The answer is that the author's statement is from the category of ascending from the lower to the higher (taraqqi min al-adna ila al-a'la), i.e., if the writing judge is alive and eligible for judgment, but before the letter reaches the judge to whom it is sent, he is dismissed, then his word is not valid. So in the case where the writing judge did not remain alive, or is alive but due to insanity etc. is not eligible for judgment, then his word is a fortiori not valid. After this clarification, no objection remains.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi) when the writing judge loses his qualification before the letter is read in court. The author of Hidayah states the Hanafi position: the letter is only accepted if the writing judge is still qualified at the time the receiving judge reads it to the defendant. If the writing judge dies, is dismissed, or becomes insane, apostate, etc., before the letter is read, the letter becomes void. However, Imam Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school), along with Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, hold that the letter remains valid even if the writing judge dies after writing and sealing it. They analogize this to testimony upon testimony (shahadah ala al-shahadah), where the transfer of testimony is completed by writing, and the death of secondary witnesses after the testimony does not nullify the verdict. The Hanafi response refutes this by distinguishing that the transfer of testimony is not complete until the letter reaches the receiving judge and is read. The death of the writing judge before that is like the death of secondary witnesses before they perform their testimony, which would nullify the testimony. Therefore, the Hanafi position is that the letter is void. The passage also provides an additional rational argument: if the writing judge loses qualification, he becomes like an ordinary person, and an ordinary person's judgment is not enforceable. The author addresses an objection that death and insanity are not comparable to dismissal, explaining that the reasoning is a fortiori (taraqqi min al-adna ila al-a'la).

Key Terms
کتاب القاضی الی القاضی (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written letter from one judge to another regarding a case, transferring information or a ruling.
شہادت علی الشہادت (shahadah ala al-shahadah): Testimony based on the testimony of primary witnesses; secondary witnesses testify that they heard the primary witnesses testify.
من معلوم الی معلوم (min ma'lum ila ma'lum): From a known person to a known person; a condition for the validity of the judge's letter that both parties are known.
ترقى من الادنى الى الاعلى (taraqqi min al-adna ila al-a'la): Ascending from the lower to the higher; a logical argument (a fortiori) that if a weaker case is invalid, a stronger case is even more invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when does a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi) become void?
A) If the writing judge dies before writing the letter.
B) If the writing judge loses qualification (e.g., dies) before the receiving judge reads it to the defendant.
C) If the seal is broken during transit.
D) If the receiving judge is also dismissed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a judge's letter is void if the writing judge loses qualification before the receiving judge reads it in court; the transfer of testimony is not complete until the reading.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
12 min
Acceptance of a Judge's Letter When the Recipient Dies
Hanafi ruling on judge's letter validity after recipient's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a judge's letter when the named recipient dies before delivery, and explain the condition of 'from known to known' that governs acceptance by a successor.

Core Idea
Trust is personal: the writing judge's reliance on a named judge cannot be transferred to an unknown successor.

When a judge sends a letter to another judge regarding a case, the validity of that letter upon the death of the receiving judge depends on how the letter is addressed. The Hanafi school imposes a strict condition that both the sender and recipient must be known. In this lesson, we examine the inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is on whether a successor can accept the letter when the original recipient dies.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules: if the named receiving judge dies before the letter reaches, the letter becomes void and the replacement judge cannot accept it.
This is the starting point of the dispute.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State that Imam Shafi'i (and Imam Ahmad) hold that the replacement judge can accept and act upon the letter, even if the original recipient died.
The opposing school uses analogy from the case of a general address.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain the Shafi'i argument: if the letter is addressed to 'the judge of the city' or 'every judge it reaches,' the replacement can accept by agreement. By qiyas, a specific address should also allow acceptance because the letter is still relevant to the court.
The opponent relies on the continuity of the judicial office.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the writing judge relied specifically on the knowledge and trustworthiness of the named individual. Since judges vary in reliability, trust is personal and cannot be transferred to an unknown successor.
The Hanafi proof is based on the principle of personal trust (amanah).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: under Hanafi, if the receiving judge dies, the case must be retried; under Shafi'i, the replacement can proceed with the letter without restarting.
This difference affects judicial efficiency and workload.

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر خط پہنچنے سے پہلے قاضی مکتوب الیہ مر گیا تو بھی یہ خط بے فائدہ ہو جائے گا اور دوسرا قاضی جو اس کی جگہ فائز ہو گا وہ اس خط کو قبول نہیں کرے گا ۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قاضی مکتوب الیہ کی وفات کے بعد جو قاضی اس کی جگہ آئے گا وہ اس خط کو قبول کر کے اس پر عمل کرے گا ۔ یہی قول امام احمد کا ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر قاضی کاتب نے یہ لکھا کہ فلاں شہر کے قاضی فلاں بن فلاں کی طرف مسلمان قاضیوں میں سے ہر اُس قاضی کی طرف جس کو یہ خط ملے اور پھر قاضی مکتوب الیہ خط پہنچنے سے پہلے مر جائے تو جو قاضی اس کی جگہ فائز ہو گا وہ بالا تفاق اس خط کو قبول کریگا ۔ پس اسی طرح اگر والى كل من يصل اليه من قضاة المسلمين تلکھا ہو تو اس صورت میں بھی قاضی مکتوب الیہ (میت) کا قائم مقام اس کو قبول کرے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی کاتب نے قاضی مکتوب الیہ (میت) کے علم اور امانت پر اعتماد کیا ہے۔ اور دوسرے کے علم و امانت پر اعتاد نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور قاضی لوگ ادائے امانت میں متفاوت بھی ہوتے ہیں۔ پس جس پر قاضی کا تب نے اعتماد کیا ہے وہ تو خط قبول کر سکتا ہے مگر دوسرا جو اس کا قائم مقام ہے وہ اس خط کو قبول نہیں کر سکتا۔ ہاں اگر قاضی کا تب نے یوں لکھا کہ فلاں شہر کے قاضی فلاں بن فلاں کی طرف اور ہر ایسے قاضی کی طرف جس کو مسلمان قاضیوں میں سے یہ خط پہنچے تو قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے مرنے سے یہ خط لغو نہ ہوگا بلکہ جس قاضی کو پہنچا اور مدعی علیہ اس کی ولایت میں ہے تو وہ قاضی عمل کرے گا کیونکہ مکتوب الیہ میت کے علاوہ جو بھی اس کا قائم مقام ہوگا وہ مکتوب الیہ کا تابع ہوگا ۔ حالانکہ یہ قاضی بھی مکتوب الیہ کا قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے معلوم ہے۔ پس من معلوم الی معلوم کی شرط پائی گئی اور جب شرط پائی گئی تو خط کو قبول کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ اور قاضی کا تب نے ابتداء یہ لکھا کہ ہر ایسے قاضی کی طرف جس کو یہ خط پہنچے تو یہ خط لغو ہو گا۔ اس کو کوئی قاضی بھی قبول نہ کرے گا۔ یہی ہمارے مشائخ کا مذہب ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں قاضی مکتوب الیہ مجہول ہے اور جب قاضی مکتوب الیہ مجهول ہے تو من معلوم الی معلوم کی شرط نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے یہ خط قبول نہ ہوگا۔ اور اس پر عمل نہ ہو گا۔
The author of Hidayah says: If the judge to whom the letter is sent dies before the letter reaches, then this letter also becomes useless, and the other judge who will be appointed in his place will not accept this letter. Imam Shafi'i said: After the death of the judge to whom it is sent, the judge who comes in his place will accept the letter and act upon it. This is also the saying of Imam Ahmad. Imam Shafi'i says: If the writing judge wrote: 'To the judge of such-and-such city, so-and-so son of so-and-so, and to every judge among the Muslim judges whom this letter reaches,' and then the judge to whom it is sent dies before the letter reaches, then the judge who is appointed in his place will accept the letter by agreement. So similarly, if he wrote 'to every one of the Muslim judges whom it reaches,' then in that case also the successor of the deceased judge will accept it. Our proof is that the writing judge relied on the knowledge and trustworthiness of the judge to whom he wrote (the deceased), and did not rely on the knowledge and trustworthiness of another. And judges differ in the performance of trust. So the one on whom the writing judge relied can accept the letter, but another who is his successor cannot accept it. Yes, if the writing judge wrote: 'To the judge of such-and-such city, so-and-so son of so-and-so, and to every such judge among the Muslim judges whom this letter reaches,' then on the death of the judge to whom it is sent, this letter does not become void; rather, whichever judge it reaches and the defendant is in his jurisdiction, that judge will act because whoever is the successor of the deceased judge is subordinate to him. Although this judge is known as the successor of the judge to whom it is sent, so the condition of 'from known to known' is met, and when the condition is met, accepting the letter is permissible. And if the writing judge initially wrote: 'To every judge whom this letter reaches,' then this letter is void; no judge will accept it. This is the madhhab of our scholars, because in this case the judge to whom it is sent is unknown, and when the judge to whom it is sent is unknown, due to the condition of 'from known to known' not being met, this letter will not be accepted and will not be acted upon.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when the receiving judge (al-maktub ilayh) dies before the letter reaches. The Hanafi position, as stated by the author of Hidayah, is that the letter becomes void and the new judge who replaces the deceased cannot accept it. Imam Shafi'i (and Imam Ahmad) disagree, holding that the replacement judge should accept and act upon it. Shafi'i argues that if the letter is addressed broadly (e.g., 'to every judge it reaches'), then the replacement can accept by agreement. The Hanafi proof is that the writing judge specifically relied on the knowledge and trustworthiness of the named judge; another judge does not have that reliance. However, if the writing judge explicitly writes 'to the judge of the city and to every Muslim judge it reaches,' then the condition of 'from known to known' is satisfied because the replacement judge is known as a successor, so the letter is valid. If the letter is addressed vaguely (e.g., 'to every judge'), it is void because the recipient is unknown. The passage ends by noting the madhhab of the Hanafi scholars that such a letter is not accepted.

Key Terms
قاضی مکتوب الیہ (qadi maktub ilayh): The judge to whom a letter is sent by another judge; the recipient judge.
قائم مقام (qa'im maqam): Successor or deputy; the judge who replaces a deceased judge.
من معلوم الی معلوم (min ma'lum ila ma'lum): From a known person to a known person; a condition for the validity of a judge's letter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, when may a replacement judge accept a letter addressed to his predecessor?
A) Always, because the letter is a document of the court.
B) Never, because the writing judge only trusted the deceased.
C) Only if the writing judge addressed the letter to 'the judge of the city and every Muslim judge it reaches.'
D) Only if the seal is intact.

Key Takeaway
A judge's letter is only valid for the named recipient; his death voids it unless the address is general enough to make any successor a known recipient.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate

Effect of Death or Dismissal of Recipient Judge on Judicial Letter
Ruling on judicial letter when recipient judge dies or is dismissed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a judicial letter when the recipient judge dies before receipt, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and apply the condition 'min ma'lum ila ma'lum'.

Core Idea
A judicial letter is a personal trust; the successor judge cannot enforce it unless the letter was written to the office generally.

In the Hanafi school, a written communication from one judge to another (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi) is held to strict conditions. One critical condition is that both the sender and recipient must be specifically known. But what happens when the recipient judge dies or is dismissed before the letter arrives? This passage from Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi presents the Hanafi view and contrasts it with the Shafi'i and Hanbali positions. Understanding this dispute sharpens your appreciation for how personal trust and institutional continuity interact in Islamic judicial procedure.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: if the recipient judge dies, is dismissed, or loses capacity before the letter arrives, the letter becomes void and the new judge cannot act upon it.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that the successor judge can accept the letter if it was addressed generally (to 'every judge') or specifically named, based on consensus (ittifaq).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent argues that the successor judge inherits the office and thus can accept letters addressed to the office, especially if addressed generally.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that the scribe judge relied on the specific knowledge and trustworthiness of the named recipient; the successor does not inherit that personal trust. However, an exception exists if the letter is written 'to the judge of such a city and to every Muslim judge who receives it', then it is valid because the recipient is known by his office.
This exception shows that 'min ma'lum ila ma'lum' can be satisfied by addressing a known office.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis would not allow a new judge to execute a deceased predecessor's letter; Shafi'is and Hanbalis would allow it under certain conditions, affecting the continuity of judicial orders.

کتاب الادب القاضي

نے دوسرے کو خبر دی کہ میرے نزدیک فلاں کا فلاں پر حق ثابت ہے تو وہ اس خبر پر عمل نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ دونوں حضرات اس شہر میں عام آدمیوں کی طرح ہیں اور عام آدمیوں کا فیصلہ شرعاً نافذ نہیں ہوتا ۔ لہذا ان کا فیصلہ بھی اپنی ولایت قضاء کے علاوہ میں نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ اس دلیل پر آپ کا اشکال ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ آپ نے فرمایا کہ اگر قاضی کا تب مر گیا یا معزول ہو گیا یا جنون وغیرہ کی وجہ سے اہلیت قضاء سے خارج ہو گیا تو وہ رعایا میں سے ایک شخص ہو گیا یعنی عام آدمی کی طرح ہو گیا۔ حالانکہ معزول ہونے کی صورت میں تو قاضی کا عام آدمی کی طرح ہونا ظاہر ہے۔ لیکن موت اور جنون کی صورت میں اس کو عام آدمی کے ساتھ کیسے لاحق کیا جا سکتا ہے؟ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ فاضل مصنف کا کلام ترقى من الادنى الىی الاعلی کے قبیل سے ہے۔ یعنی اگر قاضی کا تب زندہ ہو اور قضاء کا اہل بھی ہو مگر قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے پاس خطا پہنچنے سے پہلے معزول ہو گیا تو اس کا کلام حجت نہیں ہو گا ۔ پس جس صورت میں قاضی کا تب زندہ ہی نہ رہا یا زندہ تو ہے مگر جنون وغیرہ کی وجہ سے قضاء کا اہل نہ رہا تو اس صورت میں اس کا کلام بدرجہ اولیٰ حجت نہیں ہوگا۔ اس تقریر کے بعد کوئی اشکال واقع نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر خط پہنچنے سے پہلے قاضی مکتوب الیہ مر گیا تو بھی یہ خط بے فائدہ ہو جائے گا اور دوسرا قاضی جو اس کی جگہ فائز ہو گا وہ اس خط کو قبول نہیں کرے گا ۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قاضی مکتوب الیہ کی وفات کے بعد جو قاضی اس کی جگہ آئے گا وہ اس خط کو قبول کر کے اس پر عمل کرے گا ۔ یہی قول امام احمد کا ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر قاضی کاتب نے یہ لکھا کہ فلاں شہر کے قاضی فلاں بن فلاں کی طرف مسلمان قاضیوں میں سے ہر اُس قاضی کی طرف جس کو یہ خط ملے اور پھر قاضی مکتوب الیہ خط پہنچنے سے پہلے مر جائے تو جو قاضی اس کی جگہ فائز ہو گا وہ بالا تفاق اس خط کو قبول کریگا ۔ پس اسی طرح اگر والى كل من يصل اليه من قضاة المسلمين تلکھا ہو تو اس صورت میں بھی قاضی مکتوب الیہ (میت) کا قائم مقام اس کو قبول کرے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی کاتب نے قاضی مکتوب الیہ (میت) کے علم اور امانت پر اعتماد کیا ہے۔ اور دوسرے کے علم و امانت پر اعتاد نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور قاضی لوگ ادائے امانت میں متفاوت بھی ہوتے ہیں۔ پس جس پر قاضی کا تب نے اعتماد کیا ہے وہ تو خط قبول کر سکتا ہے مگر دوسرا جو اس کا قائم مقام ہے وہ اس خط کو قبول نہیں کر سکتا۔

ہاں اگر قاضی کا تب نے یوں لکھا کہ فلاں شہر کے قاضی فلاں بن فلاں کی طرف اور ہر ایسے قاضی کی طرف جس کو مسلمان قاضیوں میں سے یہ خط پہنچے تو قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے مرنے سے یہ خط لغو نہ ہوگا بلکہ جس قاضی کو پہنچا اور مدعی علیہ اس کی ولایت میں ہے تو وہ قاضی عمل کرے گا کیونکہ مکتوب الیہ میت کے علاوہ جو بھی اس کا قائم مقام ہوگا وہ مکتوب الیہ کا تابع ہوگا ۔ حالانکہ یہ قاضی بھی مکتوب الیہ کا قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے معلوم ہے۔ پس من معلوم الی معلوم کی شرط پائی گئی اور جب شرط پائی گئی تو خط کو قبول کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ اور قاضی کا تب نے ابتداء یہ لکھا کہ ہر ایسے قاضی کی طرف جس کو یہ خط پہنچے تو یہ خط لغو ہو گا۔ اس کو کوئی قاضی بھی قبول نہ کرے گا۔ یہی ہمارے مشائخ کا مذہب ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں قاضی مکتوب الیہ مجہول ہے اور جب قاضی مکتوب الیہ مجہول ہے تو من معلوم الی معلوم کی شرط نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے یہ خط قبول نہ ہوگا۔ اور اس پر عمل نہ ہو گا۔

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے پاس خط پہنچنے سے پہلے مدعی علیہ مر گیا تو قاضی مکتوب الیہ اس خط کو اس کے وارثوں پر نافذ کرے گا کیونکہ وارث اس کا قائم مقام ہے۔
He informed another that near me such-and-such has a right upon such-and-such, then he cannot act upon that news. Because both persons in this city are like common people, and the judgment of common people is not enforceable by Shariah. Therefore their judgment will not be enforceable outside their jurisdiction of qada. There is an objection to this proof. It is that you said that if the scribe judge dies, or is dismissed, or becomes incompetent due to insanity etc., then he becomes one of the subjects, i.e., like a common person. But in the case of dismissal, it is obvious that the judge becomes like a common person. However, in the case of death and insanity, how can he be attached to a common person? The answer is that the speech of the author is of the type 'ascending from lower to higher'. That is, if the scribe judge is alive and qualified for qada, but before the letter reaches the recipient judge, he becomes dismissed, then his speech is not proof. Then in the case where the scribe judge is not alive, or is alive but not qualified for qada due to insanity etc., then his speech is even more not proof. After this explanation, no objection remains. Sahib al-Hidayah says that if the recipient judge dies before the letter arrives, then this letter becomes useless, and the other judge who takes his place will not accept this letter. Imam Shafi'i said that after the death of the recipient judge, the judge who comes in his place will accept this letter and act upon it. This is also the saying of Imam Ahmad. Imam Shafi'i says that if the scribe judge wrote: 'To the judge of such a city, son of so-and-so, and to every judge among the Muslim judges who receives this letter,' and then the recipient judge dies before the letter arrives, then the judge who takes his place will, by consensus, accept this letter. So similarly, if he wrote 'To every one of the Muslim judges who receives it,' then also the successor of the deceased judge will accept it. Our proof is that the scribe judge relied on the knowledge and trustworthiness of the recipient judge, and did not rely on the knowledge and trustworthiness of the other. And judges differ in the performance of trust. Therefore, the one on whom the scribe judge relied can accept the letter, but the other who is his successor cannot accept it.

Yes, if the scribe judge wrote thus: 'To the judge of such a city, son of so-and-so, and to every judge among the Muslim judges whom this letter reaches,' then the death of the recipient judge will not make this letter void; rather, whichever judge it reaches and the defendant is under his jurisdiction, that judge will act upon it, because whoever is the successor of the deceased recipient judge is subordinate to him. And this judge is also known by virtue of being the successor of the recipient judge. So the condition of 'from known to known' is found, and when the condition is found, accepting the letter is permissible. And if the scribe judge wrote initially: 'To every judge whom this letter reaches,' then this letter will be void; no judge will accept it. This is the madhhab of our mashayikh, because in this case the recipient judge is unknown, and when the recipient judge is unknown, due to the condition of 'from known to known' not being met, this letter will not be accepted and will not be acted upon.

Sahib al-Hidayah says that if the defendant dies before the letter reaches the recipient judge, then the recipient judge will enforce this letter upon his heirs, because the heir is his successor.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi addresses the validity of a judge's written communication to another judge (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi). The Hanafi position, as stated by Sahib al-Hidayah, is that if the recipient judge dies, is dismissed, or loses capacity (e.g., insanity) before the letter arrives, the letter becomes void and the new judge cannot act upon it. The text first clarifies a potential objection: the author's statement that a disqualified judge is like a common person seems problematic for death and insanity, but the answer explains that the argument follows logically from the lesser (dismissal) to the greater (death/insanity) – if a dismissed judge's letter is invalid, even more so a dead or insane one. Then the passage presents the dispute: Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that the successor judge can accept the letter if the scribe judge wrote it generally to 'every judge' or specifically named, based on consensus. The Hanafi rebuttal relies on the principle that the scribe judge specifically relied on the knowledge and reliability of the named recipient; a successor does not inherit that trust. An exception is made if the scribe judge writes 'to the judge of such a city and to every Muslim judge who receives it,' then the letter is valid for any judge who gets it, because it is written to a known jurisdiction. But if written only generally to 'every judge', the recipient is unknown, so the letter is void. Finally, if the defendant dies before the letter arrives, the letter is enforced on his heirs because they stand in his place. This ruling highlights the importance of the relationship of trust between judges and the strict conditions for written evidence in judicial proceedings.

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written communication from one judge to another regarding a case or legal fact.
قائم مقام (qa'im maqam): Successor or representative who takes the place of another; here, the judge who replaces the deceased recipient.
من معلوم الى معلوم (min ma'lum ila ma'lum): The condition that both the sender and the recipient of a judicial letter must be known (specifically identified).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what happens if a judge writes a letter to another judge, but the recipient dies before the letter arrives?
A) The letter becomes void and the new judge cannot act upon it.
B) The letter is still valid and the new judge must enforce it.
C) The letter is only valid if it was written generally to 'every judge'.
D) The letter is valid but only if the new judge is also named.

Key Takeaway
A judicial letter is a personal trust; the successor judge cannot enforce it unless the letter was written to the office generally, satisfying the condition 'min ma'lum ila ma'lum'.

Why a Judge's Letter is Rejected in Hudud and Qisas: A Hanafi–Maliki/Hanbali Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on evidentiary value of judicial letters in serious penalties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on accepting a judge's letter in hudud and qisas, explain the two Hanafi proofs, and evaluate the opposing school's argument.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is rejected in hudud and qisas because it resembles testimony upon testimony and contradicts the principle of avoidance.

This passage from Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi addresses a critical inter-madhhab dispute: whether a written letter from one judge to another can be used as evidence in hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). The Hanafis, following Sahib al-Quduri, firmly reject it, while Malikis and Hanbalis accept it. Understanding the reasoning behind each position sharpens your ability to apply evidentiary principles in serious cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contested Ruling
What exactly is the legal question? It is whether a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi) is accepted as valid evidence in hudud and qisas cases.
The dispute is specific to these categories; outside hudud and qisas, the letter may be accepted in other matters.
2
State the Hanafi Position and its Authority
The Hanafi school, as stated by Sahib al-Quduri, holds that the letter is not accepted (la yuqbal). This is a well-established position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The passage cites Sahib al-Quduri, indicating the reliability of this view.
3
Analyze the First Hanafi Proof: Analogy to Testimony upon Testimony
The letter involves shubhat al-badaliyya (suspicion of substitution) because the second judge relies on the first judge's writing, not the original witnesses. This is likened to shahada 'ala al-shahada (testimony upon testimony), which is not accepted in hudud and qisas.
The analogy is based on the shared illa: both involve indirect reliance on testimony.
4
Analyze the Second Hanafi Proof: Principle of Isqat (Dropping)
Hudud and qisas are built on the principle of isqat—the law encourages avoiding these punishments where possible. Accepting the letter would work to establish them, which contradicts this objective.
This reflects the broader Hanafi tendency to restrict the application of severe penalties.
5
Examine the Opposing School's Argument and the Hanafi Rebuttal
The opposing school (Maliki, Hanbali, and one qawl of Shafi'i) argues that since witnesses have already testified before the first judge, and the letter's authenticity is attested, the testimony is complete. The Hanafi rebuttal reiterates the substitution issue and the isqat principle.
The Hanafi response shows that the letter is a substitute, not the original testimony.
6
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi judge will not act on a written letter from another judge in hudud/qisas; he requires direct testimony. A Maliki or Hanbali judge would accept the letter and execute the punishment.
This difference can have serious real-world implications for defendants.

قاضی کا دوسرے قاضی کی طرف خط حدود و قصاص میں قابل قبول نہیں

ولا يقبل كتاب القاضى الى القاضى فى الحدود والقصاص لان فيه شبهة البدلية فصار كالشهادة على الشهادة ولان مبناهما على الاسقاط و فی قبوله سعـى فـي اثــــاتهــمـــا ترجمہ اور حدود و قصاص میں خط قاضی الی القاضی قبول نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں بدل کا شبہ ہے۔ پس شہادت علی الشہادۃ کے مانند ہو گیا۔ اور اس لئے کہ ان دونوں کی بنیا د ساقط کرنے پر ہے۔ اور خط قاضی قبول ہونے میں ان کو ثابت کرنے میں کوشش کرتا ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ حدود اور قصاص میں کتاب القاضی الی القاضی مقبول نہ ہوگا ۔ یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے اور امام مالک اور امام احمد نے فرمایا کہ حدود و قصاص میں بھی کتاب القاضی الی القاضی مقبول ہو گا ۔ یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔

امام مالک اور امام احمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعتماد گواہوں پر ہوتا ہے اور گواہ قاضی کا تب کے پاس گواہی دے چکے اور اس خط کو لانے والے گواہوں نے قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے پاس اس کی صحت کی گواہی دیدی ہے۔ پس جب فیصلہ کا دارو مدار شہادت پر ہے۔ اور شہادت دی جاچکی ہے۔ تو حدود و قصاص میں بھی خط قاضی قبول کر کے قاضی مکتوب الیہ فیصلہ دیدے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ خط قاضی میں بدلیت کا شبہ موجود ہے بایں طور کہ اصلی گواہوں نے قاضی کا تب کے سامنے گواہی دی ہے اور قاضی کا تب نے اس کو قلم بند کر کے قاضی مکتوب الیہ کی طرف منتقل کر دیا ہے تو یہ شہادت علی الشہادت کے قبیل سے ہو گیا اور حدود و قصاص میں چونکہ شہادت علی الشہادۃ کو قبول نہیں کیا جاتا اس لئے خط قاضی الی القاضی بھی قبول نہ ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حدود و قصاص کی بنیاد ساقط کرنے پر ہے یعنی امکانی کوشش یہ ہونی چاہیے کہ ان کو ساقط کر دیا جائے۔ حالانکہ خطہ قاضی قبول کرنے میں ان کو ثابت کرنا لازم آتا ہے اس لئے حدود و قصاص میں خط قاضی قبول نہ ہوگا۔

جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
The letter of a judge to another judge is not accepted in hudud and qisas, because in it there is a suspicion of substitution (badal), so it becomes like testimony upon testimony (shahada ala al-shahada), and because their basis (hudud and qisas) is upon dropping (isqat), and in accepting it there is effort in establishing them. Translation: The letter of a judge to a judge is not accepted in hudud and qisas because there is a suspicion of substitution in it. So it becomes like testimony upon testimony. And because the foundation of both is upon dropping, and in accepting the judge's letter, there is effort in establishing them. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that the book (letter) of a judge to a judge is not accepted in hudud and qisas. This is one saying of Imam Shafi'i. And Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad said that in hudud and qisas, the book of a judge to a judge is accepted. This is also one saying of Imam Shafi'i.

Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad's proof is that reliance is upon witnesses, and the witnesses have already testified before the scribe judge, and the witnesses who bring this letter have testified before the recipient judge as to its authenticity. So when the decision depends on testimony, and testimony has been given, then in hudud and qisas also, the recipient judge should accept the judge's letter and pass judgement. Our proof is that in the judge's letter there is a suspicion of substitution, in that the original witnesses testified before the scribe judge, and the scribe judge wrote it down and transferred it to the recipient judge, so it becomes from the category of testimony upon testimony, and since testimony upon testimony is not accepted in hudud and qisas, therefore the judge's letter to a judge is also not accepted. The second proof is that hudud and qisas are based on dropping (isqat), i.e., the effort should be to drop them. But in accepting the judge's letter, establishing them becomes necessary, therefore in hudud and qisas, the judge's letter is not accepted.

Jamil Ahmad, forgiven (may Allah forgive him).
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi deals with a clear inter-madhhab dispute regarding the acceptance of a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi) in cases of hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). The Hanafi school, as stated by Sahib al-Quduri, holds that such a letter is not accepted. The primary reason is shubhat al-badaliyya (suspicion of substitution): the letter is analogous to shahada 'ala al-shahada (testimony upon testimony), which itself is not accepted in hudud and qisas because the original witnesses do not directly testify before the executing judge. The second reason is that the foundation of hudud and qisas is isqat (dropping or averting) — the law encourages avoiding these punishments where possible. Accepting a written letter tends to establish them, which contradicts the principle of isqat. The opposing position is held by Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and also one qawl of Imam Shafi'i: they argue that since the witnesses have already testified before the first judge, and the letter's validity is attested by witnesses before the second judge, the testimony is complete, so the letter should be accepted. The Hanafi rebuttal reiterates the analogy to testimony upon testimony and the principle of isqat. Note that the signature at the end 'Jamil Ahmad, forgiven' is likely a scribe or author's note, not part of the original text.

Key Terms
حدود (hudud): Fixed punishments prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes (e.g., theft, fornication).
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation or retribution, typically for murder or bodily harm, where the victim or heirs have the right to demand equivalent punishment.
شبهة البدلية (shubhat al-badaliyya): Suspicion of substitution or replacement; here, the idea that the letter is a substitute for direct testimony.
شهادة على الشهادة (shahada 'ala al-shahada): Testimony upon testimony, where a witness testifies about another witness's testimony.
إسقاط (isqat): Dropping or averting (of punishment); the principle that hudud and qisas should be avoided where possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Why does the Hanafi school reject a judge's letter in hudud and qisas according to this passage?
A) Because the letter lacks a seal.
B) Because it involves a suspicion of substitution and goes against the principle of dropping (isqat).
C) Because the witnesses are not Muslim.
D) Because the first judge was not reliable.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rejection of a judicial letter in hudud and qisas rests on the analogical similarity to testimony upon testimony and the fundamental principle of aversion (isqat) in these penalties.

Acceptance of Judge's Letter in Hudud and Qisas
Inter-madhhab dispute on judge's letter in hudud and qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the acceptance of a judge's letter in hudud and qisas, explain the two Hanafi proofs, and compare the opposing view of the Maliki school.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is not accepted in hudud and qisas because it is second-hand testimony and punishments must be avoided.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya presents an important inter-madhhab dispute about the validity of a judge's written communication in cases of hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). The Hanafi school firmly holds that such a letter is unacceptable, while other schools disagree. The reasoning hinges on two key principles: the nature of the letter as second-hand testimony and the fundamental rule of avoiding punishments. Understanding this dispute will sharpen your ability to apply Hanafi principles of evidence and procedural law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
The issue is whether a written communication (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi) from one judge to another can be used as valid proof to enforce hudud and qisas penalties.
This is a procedural question, not a question about the original guilt or innocence.
2
State the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi school, as stated by al-Quduri and al-Marghinani, holds that the judge's letter is not accepted in hudud and qisas.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position in the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the First Proof: Shubhat al-Badal
The letter involves shubhat al-badal (semblance of substitution), making it analogous to shahadat 'ala al-shahadat (testimony upon testimony), which is not accepted in hudud and qisas.
Testimony upon testimony is weaker than direct testimony and is rejected in these severe penalties.
4
Analyze the Second Proof: Isqat (Dropping)
Hudud and qisas are built on the principle of isqat—every effort should be made to drop these punishments due to doubts. Accepting the letter would be a positive effort to establish them, contradicting this principle.
This proof is unique to Hanafi reasoning and reflects the school's cautious approach.
5
Compare with Opposing School
Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and one view of Imam al-Shafi'i accept the letter. Their proof: the original witnesses testified, and the bearers confirm authenticity, so the decision rests on testimony, which is valid even in hudud and qisas.
The Hanafi response counters that the chain makes it second-hand testimony, which is unacceptable.

Chapter on the Conduct of the Judge. The author of al-Hidayah says: If the defendant dies before the letter reaches the addressed judge, then the addressed judge will execute the letter upon his heirs because the heir is his representative. The judge's letter to another judge is not acceptable in hudud and qisas. Arabic: 'And the letter of a judge to a judge is not accepted in hudud and qisas because it contains a semblance of substitution, so it becomes like testimony upon testimony, and because their foundation is upon dropping (isqat), and accepting it involves effort in establishing them.' Translation: And in hudud and qisas, a judge's letter to another judge will not be accepted because it has the semblance of substitution. Thus it becomes like testimony upon testimony. And because the basis of both is on dropping. And in accepting the judge's letter, there is effort in establishing them. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that in hudud and qisas, the letter of a judge to a judge will not be accepted. This is one view of Imam Shafi'i. And Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad said that in hudud and qisas, the letter of a judge to a judge is accepted. This is also one view of Imam Shafi'i. The proof of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad is that reliance is upon witnesses, and the witnesses have already testified before the first judge, and the witnesses who bring the letter have testified to its correctness before the addressed judge. So when the decision depends on testimony, and testimony has already been given, then even in hudud and qisas the judge should accept the letter and decide. Our proof is that the judge's letter contains a semblance of agency; in that the original witnesses testified before the first judge, and the first judge wrote it down and transferred it to the addressed judge, so it becomes of the category of testimony upon testimony. And since testimony upon testimony is not accepted in hudud and qisas, therefore the judge's letter to a judge is also not accepted. The second proof is that the foundation of hudud and qisas is on dropping; meaning every possible effort should be made to drop them. While accepting the judge's letter necessitates establishing them, therefore the judge's letter is not accepted in hudud and qisas. Jamil Ahmad, may Allah forgive him.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya presents an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of a judge's written communication (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi) in cases of hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). The Hanafi school, represented here by the author of al-Hidayah and al-Quduri, holds that such a letter is not acceptable as evidence in these cases. The passage provides two primary proofs. First, the letter carries a shubhat al-badal (semblance of substitution), analogous to shahadat 'ala al-shahadat (testimony upon testimony), which is uniformly rejected in hudud and qisas because these severe penalties require the highest level of certainty and direct testimony. Second, the very nature of hudud and qisas is built upon isqat (dropping or avoidance); the Shari'ah encourages dropping these punishments wherever doubt exists. Accepting the letter would be a positive effort to establish them, contradicting this principle. The opposing view is attributed to Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and one reported position of Imam al-Shafi'i, who argue that since the witnesses testified before the sending judge and the letter's bearers confirm its authenticity, the decision rests on valid testimony, so the letter should be accepted. The Hanafi response reiterates that the chain of transmission turns the letter into second-hand testimony, which is unacceptable in these matters. Thus, the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that hudud and qisas cannot be enforced based on a judge's letter; direct testimony before the presiding judge is required.

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written communication from one judge to another, containing a judicial finding or testimony, intended to be acted upon by the recipient judge.
شبهة البدلية (shubhat al-badal): A semblance of substitution or agency; the letter stands in place of direct testimony, creating a secondary level of evidence.
إسقاط (isqat): Dropping or waiving; the legal principle that hudud and qisas should be avoided and dropped whenever possible due to doubts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the sending judge may not be trustworthy.
D) Because the witnesses are not present before the second judge.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a judge's letter is not accepted as proof in hudud and qisas because it is second-hand testimony and contradicts the principle of dropping punishments.

Women as Judges: Hanafi Position vs. Three Imams
Inter-madhhab dispute with qiyas argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on women judges, explain the qiyas to testimony, and evaluate the opposing schools' hadith-based argument.

Core Idea
A woman's judgement is valid in all matters except hudud and qisas, by analogy to her testimony.

This passage presents a classic Hanafi departure from the majority: while Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad prohibit women from judging altogether, the Hanafi school permits it except in the most severe criminal punishments. The reasoning hinges on a powerful analogy to women's testimony in court. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi prioritization of qiyas over a general hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling as per al-Quduri: women can be judges in all matters except hudud and qisas.
This is a ruling of permissibility (ja'iz), not obligation.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) hold that women cannot be judges in any matter.
Their position is based on a hadith and the claim of deficient intellect.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the hadith: 'A people who entrust their affairs to a woman will never succeed' (Sahih al-Bukhari). They interpret it broadly to include judgeship.
Also they argue that women are not fit due to intellectual deficiency.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis restrict the hadith to supreme political leadership (imamah al-kubra), not the specific function of a judge. They prioritize qiyas to testimony, which is explicitly accepted in the Quran for women.
The claim of deficient intellect is not a legal impediment since women give testimony, issue fatwas, and narrate hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi jurisdictions allow women judges in most cases; Shafi'i jurisdictions prohibit them entirely.
The dispute hinges on how to interpret the hadith and the weight given to qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حدود و قصاص کے علاوہ عورت کے قضا کا حکم
ويجوز قضاء المرأة فى كل شئ الافى الحدود والقصاص اعتبارا بشهادتها فيهما وقد مر الوجه
ترجمہ اور عورت کا حکم قضاء ہر چیز میں جائز ہے علاوہ حدود و قصاص کے۔ ان دونوں میں عورت کی شہادت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور وجہ گذر چکی ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ حدود و قصاص کے علاوہ ہر معاملہ میں عورت کو قاضی بنانا جائز ہے۔ اور حدود و قصاص کے علاوہ ہر معاملہ میں اس کا فیصلہ نافذ ہوگا۔ احناف اسی کے قائل ہیں لیکن امام مالک، امام شافعی اور امام احمد نے فرمایا کہ عورت کو کسی بھی معاملہ میں قاضی بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور اس کا فیصلہ حدود و قصاص میں نافذ ہوگا نہ کسی دوسرے معاملہ میں ائمہ ثلاثہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت ناقص العقل ہونے کی وجہ سے مقدمات کا فیصلہ کرنے اور بحیثیت قاضی، عدالت میں حاضر ہونے کی اہل نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو قاضی بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ بخاری شریف کی حدیث سے بھی اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔ چنانچہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایالـن يـفـلـح قوم ولوا امر هم امرأة، یعنی ایسی قوم ہرگز فلاح یاب نہ ہو سکے گی جس نے اپنے معاملات کا والی کسی عورت کو مقر رکیا ہو ۔ عورت کو والی بنانے پر آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا عدم فلاح کی خبر دینا، اس بات کی تین دلیل ہے کہ عورت کو قاضی اور حاکم بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہماری دلیل ... عورت کے حکم قضاء کو اس کی شہادت پر قیاس کیا گیا ہے۔ یعنی حکم قضاء شہادت کے حکم سے مستفاد ہے۔ پس جو شخص شہادت کا اہل ہے وہ قضاء کا بھی اہل ہوگا ۔ اور جو شہادت کا اہل نہیں وہ قضاء کا اہل بھی نہ ہو گا۔ پس عورت کی شہادت چونکہ حدود و قصاص کے علاوہ میں جائز ہے اس لئے حدود و قصاص کے علاوہ میں اس کا حکم قضاء بھی جائز ہوگا۔ اور حدود و قصاص میں عورت کی شہادت چونکہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے حدود و قصاص میں اس کا حکم قضاء بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔
Ruling on a woman's judgement except in hudud and qisas. And a woman's judgement is permissible in every thing except in hudud and qisas, based on her testimony in them, and the reasoning has passed. Translation: And the ruling of a woman's judgement is permissible in every thing except hudud and qisas, by analogy to her testimony in them, and the reasoning has passed. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: It is permissible to appoint a woman as a judge in every matter except hudud and qisas. And her judgement will be enforced in every matter except hudud and qisas. The Hanafis adhere to this. But Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad said that it is not permissible to appoint a woman as a judge in any matter. And her judgement will not be enforced in hudud and qisas nor in any other matter. The proof of the three Imams is that a woman, due to deficiency of intellect, is not capable of deciding cases and presenting herself in court as a judge. Therefore, it is not permissible to appoint her as a judge. The hadith in Sahih Bukhari also supports this. Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'A people who entrust their affairs to a woman will never succeed.' That is, a people who appoint a woman as their ruler over their affairs will never achieve success. The Prophet's informing of failure due to appointing a woman as ruler is clear proof that it is not permissible to appoint a woman as a judge and ruler. Our proof is that a woman's judgement is analogized to her testimony. That is, the ruling of judgement is derived from the ruling of testimony. So whoever is qualified for testimony will also be qualified for judgement. And whoever is not qualified for testimony will not be qualified for judgement. Since a woman's testimony is permissible except in hudud and qisas, therefore her judgement is also permissible except in hudud and qisas. And since her testimony is not permissible in hudud and qisas, therefore her judgement is not permissible in hudud and qisas.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning women serving as judges. The Hanafi school, as stated by al-Quduri, holds that women can be judges in all matters except hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliatory punishments). The ruling is derived by analogy (qiyas) to the acceptance of women's testimony: women are accepted as witnesses in all cases except hudud and qisas, so similarly their judgment is valid except in those areas. The opposing view of the three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) is that women cannot be judges at all. They argue that women have deficient intellect and are not fit for the responsibility, and they cite the hadith 'A people who entrust their affairs to a woman will never succeed.' The Hanafi response distinguishes between general leadership (which the hadith condemns) and the specific function of a judge in a courtroom. The Hanafi position relies on the analogy to testimony, which is established in the Quran and Sunnah, and they consider the analogy to be the stronger evidence. The text concludes by reaffirming the Hanafi ruling based on this analogy.

Key Terms
حدود (hudud): Fixed punishments prescribed for specific crimes (e.g., theft, adultery).
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for murder or injury; equal retribution.
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony given in court.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; deriving a ruling for a new case based on a similar case with an established ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only hudud and qisas
B) All matters, including hudud and qisas
C) All matters except hudud and qisas
D) Only financial disputes

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits women judges in all matters except hudud and qisas, based on a strong analogy to women's testimony.

Judge Cannot Appoint a Deputy Without Delegation
States the prohibition on a judge appointing a deputy unless delegated authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge appointing a deputy, identify the qiyas used as proof, and distinguish the exception for the Friday prayer leader.

Core Idea
A judge's authority is personal; delegation requires explicit permission.

This lesson examines the principle that a judge cannot delegate his judicial authority to a deputy unless specifically authorized. The Hanafi school uses a qiyas (analogy) to the case of an agent (wakil) who cannot appoint a sub-agent without permission. However, an exception exists for the Friday prayer leader due to the fixed time constraint. Understanding this ruling is essential for ensuring the validity of judgments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its category
Locate the explicit statement 'ليس للقاضي' which establishes a prohibition. Determine the hukm level (haram) and the condition (explicit delegation).
The ruling is a prohibition unless the judge has been delegated the authority to appoint deputies.
2
Analyze the qiyas (analogy)
Identify the asl (original case: agent appointing sub-agent), its hukm (prohibition without permission), and the far' (judge appointing deputy). Establish the illa (common effective cause: authority is personal).
The illa is that both positions involve delegated authority that does not include the power to further delegate unless expressly given.
3
Examine the exception for Friday prayer
Note the contrast: the person ordered to lead Friday prayer may appoint a deputy. Understand the rationale: the prayer has a fixed time and may be missed, so the command implies permission to delegate.
This exception is based on necessity (time constraint) and does not apply to judgment, which can be delayed.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a judge who appoints a deputy without delegation. Conclude that the deputy's judgments are invalid. Then consider a case where the judge has been given explicit delegation; then the deputy's judgments are valid.
The text also hints at ratification: if the original judge ratifies the deputy's judgment, it may become valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی کے لئے نائب مقرر کرنے کا حکم
وليس للقاضى ان يستخلف على القضاء الا ان يفوّض اليه ذلك لانه قلد القضاء دون التقليد به فصار كتوكيل الوكيل بخلاف المامور باقامة الجمعة حيث يستخلف لانه على شرف الفوات لتوقته فكان الامر به اذنافي الاستخلاف دلالة ولا كذلك القضاء ولو قضى الثانى بمحضر من الاول او قضى الثانى فاجاز
Ruling on the judge appointing a deputy: It is not permissible for the judge to appoint a deputy for judgment unless he has delegated that authority to him. Because he was appointed to judge, not to appoint others, so it becomes like a deputy appointing a deputy. Contrary to the one ordered to establish the Friday prayer, who can appoint a deputy because it is on the verge of being missed due to its fixed time, so the command to establish it is an implicit permission to appoint a deputy. This is not the case with judgement. And if the second judge passes a judgement in the presence of the first, or the second judge passes a judgement and the first ratifies it...
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof regarding a judge's ability to appoint a deputy. The ruling is that a judge cannot appoint someone else to act as a judge in his place unless he has been expressly delegated the authority to do so by the original appointing authority (e.g., the caliph). The reasoning is that the judge has been appointed to perform the act of judging itself, not to delegate that task to others. This is analogous to a principal-agent relationship: an agent (وكيل) cannot appoint another agent without explicit permission. The proof is based on qiyas to the case of agency. The text contrasts this with the case of a person ordered to lead the Friday prayer: that person can appoint a deputy because the Friday prayer has a fixed time (Friday noon) and may be missed if the appointed person is unavailable. Therefore, the command to establish the prayer implies by indication (dalalah) the permission to appoint a deputy. However, judgment (qada) does not have the same time constraint; a case can be delayed. Therefore, the same implicit permission does not exist for a judge. The passage ends with a discussion of what happens if the second judge (the deputy) passes a judgement in the presence of the original judge, or if the original judge ratifies it, which likely deals with the validity of such judgements. This ruling is derived from the general principles of agency and delegation in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhlaaf): Appointing a deputy or successor.
توكيل الوكيل (tawkeel al-wakeel): An agent appointing another agent (sub-agency).
مامور باقامة الجمعة (ma'moor bi iqamat al-jumu'ah): The person appointed to lead the Friday prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because prayer is more important than judgment
B) Because the Friday prayer has a fixed time and may be missed, so permission is implied
C) Because judges are more knowledgeable
D) Because the judge's role is more complex

Key Takeaway
A judge cannot delegate his judicial authority to a deputy unless explicitly authorized, based on qiyas to agency and contrasted with the exceptional case of Friday prayer.

Women's Judgeship: Hanafi Exception for Hudud and Qisas
Inter-madhhab dispute on women's capacity for judgeship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on women's judgeship and evaluate the opposing schools' arguments using the analogy to testimony.

Core Idea
Women may judge all cases except hudud and qisas — the same scope as their testimony.

The role of a judge (qadi) is a position of authority requiring legal capacity. The Hanafi school, based on the principle of qiyas (analogy) to a woman's testimony, allows women to serve as judges in all matters except hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning and contrasts it with the view of the majority of other schools that completely prohibit women from judging.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to the Hanafi school: a woman may be appointed as judge in all matters except hudud and qisas. Her verdict is effective in those areas.
The ruling is based on the authority of Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
The Maliki, Shafi'i, and Hanbali schools hold that women cannot be judges in any matter. Their primary evidence is the hadith, 'A people who entrust their affairs to a woman will never succeed,' and the claim that women are deficient in intellect.
This hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis distinguish the hadith: it applies to supreme political leadership (imamah al-kubra), not to ordinary judgeship. They argue that qiyas on testimony is a more specific and appropriate analogy.
The Hanafis accept that women are capable of sound judgment in non-hudud matters, as evidenced by their accepted testimony.
4
Understand the qiyas reasoning
The key analogy: women's testimony is accepted in all matters except hudud and qisas. Since judgeship requires similar capacity, the same scope applies. Therefore, women may judge except in hudud and qisas.
This is a clear qiyas jali (manifest analogy) with the illa being legal capacity for testimony.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis allow women judges in all civil and criminal matters except hudud/qisas. Other schools do not allow women judges at all.
In modern contexts, Hanafis may permit women to serve as judges in family or commercial courts, but not in cases involving fixed penalties.

Source Text

It is permissible for a woman to be a judge in everything except hudud and qisas, by analogy to her testimony in those two matters, and the reasoning has passed. Translation: And the ruling of a woman's judgeship is permissible in everything except hudud and qisas. In both of these, by analogy to her testimony, and the reasoning has passed. Elaboration: Sahib al-Quduri said that it is permissible to appoint a woman as judge in every matter except hudud and qisas. And her verdict will be effective in every matter except hudud and qisas. The Hanafis hold this view. But Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad said that it is not permissible to appoint a woman as judge in any matter. And her verdict will not be effective in hudud and qisas nor in any other matter. The proof of the three Imams is that a woman, due to being deficient in intellect, is not capable of deciding cases and appearing in court as a judge. Therefore, it is not permissible to appoint her as judge. The hadith in Sahih al-Bukhari also supports this: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'A people who entrust their affairs to a woman will never succeed.' This report of the Prophet (peace be upon him) of lack of success for appointing a woman as ruler indicates that it is impermissible to appoint a woman as judge and ruler. Our proof: The ruling of a woman's judgeship is analogized to her testimony. That is, the ruling of judgeship is derived from the ruling of testimony. So whoever is capable of testimony is also capable of judgeship, and whoever is not capable of testimony is not capable of judgeship. Since a woman's testimony is permissible in matters other than hudud and qisas, her judgeship is also permissible in matters other than hudud and qisas. And since a woman's testimony is not permissible in hudud and qisas, her judgeship is also not permissible in hudud and qisas.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on whether a woman can serve as a judge. The Hanafi school, following Imam al-Quduri, holds that a woman may be appointed a judge in all matters except hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). The ruling is based on qiyas (analogy) to a woman's testimony: since her testimony is accepted in financial and other transactions but not in hudud and qisas, the same applies to her judicial authority. The three other schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) argue that women are inherently deficient in intellect and cannot handle the responsibilities of judging, citing the hadith 'A people who entrust their affairs to a woman will never succeed.' The Hanafi response is that this hadith refers to supreme political leadership (imamah al-kubra), not to ordinary judgeship. They maintain that analogy to testimony provides a sound basis, and since women are accepted as witnesses in most matters, they are also fit to adjudicate those matters. The passage thus establishes the Hanafi position and refutes the opposing view.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍā'): The office of judge; adjudication of legal disputes.
حدود (ḥudūd): Fixed punishments prescribed by Shari'ah for certain crimes (e.g., theft, zina).
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retaliatory punishment for intentional homicide or injury.
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony as a witness in court.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning to derive a ruling for a new case based on an existing ruling with a common 'illa.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits women to serve as judges in all matters except hudud and qisas, by analogy to their testimony in those matters.

Judge Appointing a Deputy: Conditions and Rulings
Ruling on a judge's authority to appoint a deputy without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on a judge appointing a deputy without permission and distinguish it from the Jumu'ah imam's authority using the concept of dalala.

Core Idea
A judge cannot delegate his authority without the ruler's permission; Jumu'ah is an exception due to its time sensitivity.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies a critical distinction in delegation of judicial authority. You will learn that a judge, unlike an imam leading Jumu'ah, cannot appoint a deputy unless explicitly authorized by the ruler. The reasoning hinges on the nature of the original appointment: a judge is given authority to adjudicate, not to delegate that authority. The narrow time frame of Jumu'ah creates an implied permission (dalala) that does not apply to the judiciary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the legal act: a judge appointing a deputy (khalifa) over judiciary. The matn states: 'It is not for the judge to appoint a deputy unless entrusted.' This means it is impermissible without the ruler's permission.
The Arabic phrase 'ليس للقاضي' indicates legal prohibition.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The evidence is a qiyas (analogy) to a wakil (agent): just as an agent cannot appoint another agent without the principal's permission, a judge cannot appoint a deputy without the ruler's permission. This is because the judge was appointed (qulida) to judge, not to delegate (taqlid).
The key text: 'لانه قلد القضاء دون التقليد به فصار كتوكيل الوكيل'.
3
Analyze the exception for Jumu'ah
Unlike the judge, the person appointed to lead Jumu'ah can appoint a deputy even without explicit permission. Why? Because Jumu'ah has a fixed, narrow time; if the imam becomes unable, waiting for permission from the ruler would cause the prayer to be missed. So the command to establish Jumu'ah implies (dalala) permission to appoint a deputy when necessary.
This exception is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and the principle of avoiding loss of the obligation.
4
Discuss scenarios of ratification and full delegation
The passage addresses two additional cases: (1) If a second judge gives a ruling in the presence of the first, or the first later validates it, it is valid – like ratification in agency. (2) If the ruler grants the judge full authority to appoint deputies, the second judge becomes a deputy of the ruler, not the first judge, and the first judge cannot remove him unless given that power.
These scenarios show that the ruler's permission is the key condition.
5
Note cross-madhhab disagreement
The commentary mentions that the three other schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) agree with the Hanafi position, except for one opinion from a Shafi'i disciple that permits a judge to appoint a deputy without permission if he is incapable of handling the matter himself. This remains a minority view.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the prohibition without permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس للقاضى ان يستخلف على القضاء الا ان يفوّض اليه ذلك لانه قلد القضاء دون التقليد به فصار كتوكيل الوكيل بخلاف المامور باقامة الجمعة حيث يستخلف لانه على شرف الفوات لتوقته فكان الامر به اذنافي
