It is not for the judge to appoint a deputy over judiciary unless that is entrusted to him, because he was entrusted with adjudication, not with the authority to entrust it to others. So it is like a wakil (agent) appointing another wakil. Unlike the one appointed to establish the Friday prayer, who can appoint a deputy because Friday prayer is on the verge of being missed due to its fixed time. So the command to establish it implies permission to appoint a deputy by indication (dalala), and this is not the case for judiciary. If the second judge gives a ruling in the presence of the first, or the second gives a ruling and then the first validates it, it is permissible, as in agency. This is because the first judge's opinion was present, and that is the condition. And if [the ruler] has entrusted him with the authority to [appoint a deputy], he possesses it, and the second becomes a deputy of the original (the ruler), such that the first judge does not have the power to remove him, unless the power of removal was also entrusted to him. This is the correct view. Elaboration: Sahib al-Quduri says that the judge does not have the authority to appoint anyone as his deputy or khalifa in judiciary due to an excuse or without an excuse, unless the sultan or supreme ruler has given him this authority. If so, then appointing a deputy is permissible. Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad hold the same view. It is reported from one disciple of Imam Shafi'i that if a judge appoints a deputy in a matter he himself is incapable of, it is permissible even without the sultan's permission. This difference occurs when the sultan remained silent at the time of appointment, neither permitting nor prohibiting appointment of a deputy. If the sultan permits, the judge is unanimously allowed to appoint a deputy, and if the sultan prohibits, it is unanimously impermissible. In any case, without the sultan's permission, the judge cannot appoint his representative because he was only made a judge, not given the authority to make others judges. So it is like a wakil appointing another wakil: just as a wakil without permission from the principal cannot appoint another in his place, likewise a judge without the sultan's permission cannot appoint his deputy or khalifa. In contrast, if someone is appointed to lead the Friday prayer, he can appoint his khalifa and deputy even if the sultan did not give permission, because the time for Friday is very limited. If the one appointed to establish Friday prayer becomes unable to perform it due to an excuse and he does not have permission to appoint a deputy, by the time he informs the sultan and leader of the Muslims, the time for Friday prayer would pass, even though he was appointed to perform it. So the sultan's and leader's permission to establish Friday prayer implies by indication (dalala) permission to appoint a deputy when necessary to perform it. But it should be remembered that the one appointed to establish Friday prayer can only appoint as his deputy someone who has heard the Friday sermon (khutba), because the sermon is among the conditions for commencing Friday prayer. And this ruling is...
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on whether a judge can appoint a deputy (khalifa/na'ib) to act in his place. The matn states that a judge cannot appoint a deputy unless specifically authorized to do so by the ruler. The reasoning is that the judge was given the authority to judge, not the authority to delegate that authority to others. This is analogous to an agent (wakil) who cannot appoint another agent without the principal's permission. An exception is made for the person appointed to lead the Friday prayer (Jumu'ah): he can appoint a deputy even without explicit permission, because the time for Jumu'ah is limited and the purpose (establishing the prayer) would otherwise be defeated. This exception is based on dalala (implied permission from the context). The passage also discusses two scenarios: (1) if a second judge gives a ruling in the presence of the first, or the first subsequently validates the second's ruling, it is valid—this is similar to agency where ratification works. (2) If the ruler has given the judge full authority to appoint deputies, the second judge becomes a deputy of the ruler, not of the first judge, so the first judge cannot remove him unless also given that power. The commentary by al-Quduri emphasizes that without the ruler's permission, the judge cannot appoint a deputy, and this is agreed upon by the three other schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) except for one opinion from a Shafi'i disciple allowing it when the judge is incapable. The distinction from Jumu'ah is crucial: because of the narrow time window, the authority to lead Jumu'ah implies the authority to appoint a substitute when necessary.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhlāf): Appointing a deputy or successor (khalifa) for the judiciary.
تقليد (taqlīd): The act of appointing someone to a position; here, the authority to delegate.
وكيل (wakīl): Agent or representative.
دلالة (dalāla): Implication or indication; a method of deriving rulings from context.
نائب (nā'ib): Deputy or substitute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can the person appointed to lead Jumu'ah prayer appoint a deputy without explicit permission, unlike a judge?
A) Because Jumu'ah is more important than judiciary
B) Because the time for Jumu'ah is limited and might be missed
C) Because the Jumu'ah imam has more authority than a judge
D) Because judiciary is not a religious duty

Key Takeaway
A judge's authority is limited to adjudication; delegation requires explicit authorization from the ruler, unlike the Jumu'ah imam whose implied authority to delegate arises from time sensitivity.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Judge's Authority to Appoint a Deputy: Permission Required
Ruling on judge's inability to appoint deputy without ruler's permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge appointing a deputy without the ruler's permission, explain the qiyas to agency, and identify the exception for the Friday prayer imam.

Core Idea
A judge cannot appoint a deputy without the ruler’s permission, just as an agent cannot appoint another agent without the client’s permission.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a key limitation on a judge's authority: he is not automatically empowered to deputize others. The ruling is derived by analogy to agency and contrasted with the special case of the Friday prayer imam. The Hanafi position, shared by other major schools, is that explicit permission from the ruler is required. However, a minority view from a student of Imam al-Shafi'i allows deputization in cases of necessity. Understanding this ruling is crucial for ensuring the validity of judicial appointments and verdicts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
Read the passage and find the explicit statement that a judge cannot appoint a deputy without the ruler's permission.
Look for phrases like 'لا يملك أن يولي خليفة'.
2
Understand the Qiyas to Agency
The analogy: judge is like an agent (wakil) of the ruler. An agent cannot appoint another agent without permission. Similarly, the judge cannot appoint another judge without permission.
This is qiyas jali.
3
Contrast with the Friday Prayer Imam
The imam for Jumu'ah can appoint a deputy even without explicit permission because the time is tight and missing the prayer would cause loss.
This is an exception due to necessity and implied permission.
4
Examine the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
The Hanafi position (shared by Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) requires permission. A student of Shafi'i allows it if the judge cannot handle the matter.
The dispute is only when the ruler remained silent.
5
Note the Practical Consequences
If a judge appoints without permission, the judgment is not valid unless the judge later approves it. If the ruler gives permission, the deputy becomes a deputy of the ruler, not of the judge.
This affects removal authority.

کام باقی نماز کو پورا کرنا اور جو حصہ مامور با قامۃ الجمعہ ادا کر چکا ہے اس پر بنا کرنا ہے۔ نماز جمعہ کا افتتاح کرنا اس کا کام نہیں ہے بلکہ افتتاح مامور با قامتہ الجمعہ کر چکا ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ خطبہ افتتاح جمعہ کے شرائط میں سے ہے نہ کہ بنائے جمعہ کے شرائط میں سے۔ بہر حال خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ نماز جمعہ کا وقت چونکہ تنگ ہوتا ہے اس میں اتنی گنجائش نہیں ہوتی کہ عذر پیش آجانے پر سلطان کو مطلع کرے اس لئے جو شخص نماز جمعہ قائم کرنے پر مامور ہو گا اس کو سلطان کی طرف سے دلالہ اس کی بھی اجازت ہوگی کہ ضرورت پڑنے پر وہ کسی کو بھی اپنا خلیفہ مقرر کر دے۔ برخلاف حکم قضاء کے کہ اس کے واسطے کوئی وقت متعین نہیں ہے۔ اور جب کوئی وقت متعین نہیں ہے تو عذر پیش آنے پر تاخیر کی وجہ سے اس کے فوت ہونے کا امکان بھی باقی نہیں رہا۔ اور جب تاخیر کی وجہ سے حکم قضاء کے فوت ہونے کا امکان نہیں رہا۔ تو قاضی حکم قضاء میں اگر کسی کو اپنا خلیفہ مقرر کرنا چاہے تو اس کے لئے سلطان اور حاکم اعلیٰ کی طرف سے اجازت درکار ہوگی بغیر صریحی اجازت کے قاضی اپنا خلیفہ مقرر کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔
Book of the Etiquette of the Judge: Page 294 of Ashraf al-Bidaya Volume Nine. First: It is permissible as in agency. And this is because his opinion (the first judge's) is present, which is the condition. And when authority is delegated to him, he possesses it, so the second becomes a deputy of the original, so that the first cannot remove him unless removal is delegated to him. That is correct. Translation: And the judge does not have the authority to appoint his deputy over the judiciary unless this authority has been given to him. Because he was entrusted with the office of judiciary, not given the authority to appoint a judge. So this is like a agent appointing another agent. Contrary to the one who is appointed to establish the Friday prayer, for he can appoint his deputy. Because the time for Friday prayer is limited and it is at risk of being missed. So the command to perform Friday prayer implies permission to appoint a deputy. And the case of judiciary is not like this. And if another judge gave a judgment in the presence of the first judge, or another judge gave a judgment, and then the first permitted it, it is valid, as in agency. And this validity is because the first judge's opinion is present in that judgment, and that was the condition. And when the king delegated to the judge the authority to appoint a deputy, the judge becomes its owner, and the second judge becomes a deputy of the original (the king), so that the first judge cannot remove him unless he was also given the authority to remove. That is correct. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says that the judge does not have the authority to appoint a deputy for the judiciary, whether due to an excuse or without an excuse. Yes, if the sultan and supreme ruler has given him this authority, then appointing a deputy is permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad are also of this view. From a student of Imam al-Shafi'i, it is narrated that if a judge appoints a deputy for a matter he cannot handle himself, it is permissible even without the sultan's permission. This difference arises when the sultan remained silent at the time of appointing the judge, neither permitting nor prohibiting. Otherwise, if the sultan permitted the judge to deputize, the judge is unanimously authorized to appoint his deputy. And if the sultan prohibits, then it is unanimously impermissible. In any case, without the sultan's permission, the judge cannot appoint his deputy, because he was only made a judge, and he was not given the authority to make judges. So this is like an agent appointing another agent in his place, i.e., just as an agent does not have the authority to appoint another agent without the client's permission, similarly the judge cannot appoint a deputy or caliph without the sultan's permission. In contrast, if someone is appointed to lead the Friday prayer, he can appoint his deputy even if the sultan did not give him permission. Because the time for Friday prayer is very tight. So if the one appointed to establish the Friday prayer becomes unable to perform it due to an excuse, and he does not have permission to appoint a deputy, by the time he notifies the sultan and leader of the Muslims, the time for Friday prayer would have passed, whereas he was appointed to perform it. So the sultan and leader of the Muslims giving someone permission to perform the Friday prayer implies permission to appoint a deputy for the Friday prayer when needed. But it should be remembered that the one appointed to establish the Friday prayer can appoint as his deputy only one who has heard the Friday sermon. Because the sermon is among the conditions for commencing the Friday prayer. This ruling applies when an excuse occurs after the sermon but before starting the prayer. If the one appointed becomes excused before the sermon, the one he appoints will give the sermon and lead the prayer. And if he started the prayer after the sermon and then becomes hadith (ritually impure), he can appoint any of the followers as deputy, whether they heard the sermon or not. Because in this case, the deputy's job is only to complete the remaining prayer and build on what the original imam has already done. He is not opening the Friday prayer; the opening was done by the original imam, and it is established that the sermon is a condition for commencing the Friday prayer, not for its continuation. In any case, the summary is that since the time for Friday prayer is tight, there is no room to inform the sultan when an excuse occurs, so the one appointed to establish the Friday prayer is implicitly permitted by the sultan to appoint a deputy when needed. This is contrary to the judiciary, for which no specific time is set. And when no specific time is set, there is no possibility of it being missed due to delay. So if the judge wishes to appoint a deputy in judicial matters, he needs explicit permission from the sultan and supreme ruler; without explicit permission, the judge is not authorized to appoint his deputy.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute. It establishes the general rule that a judge cannot appoint a deputy unless the ruler (sultan) gives him explicit permission. The proof is an analogy to agency (wakalah): just as an agent cannot appoint another agent without the client's permission, the judge cannot appoint another judge without the ruler's permission. The exception is the person appointed to lead the Friday prayer; because the time is tight, the appointment implies permission to deputize when necessary. The passage also notes that if the judge appoints a deputy without permission, and then the judge later approves the deputy's judgment, it is valid because the judge's opinion is then present. An inter-madhhab dispute is mentioned: Imam Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad agree with the Hanafi view that permission is needed, but a student of Shafi'i holds that if the judge cannot handle the matter himself, he can appoint a deputy without permission. The preferred Hanafi position is that the judge is not authorized without explicit permission.

Key Terms
خلیفہ (khalīfah): Deputy or representative appointed by the judge to perform judicial functions.
نائب (nā'ib): A deputy appointed by the judge to act in his place in judicial matters.
مأمور بإقامة الجمعة (ma'mūr bi-iqāmat al-jumu'ah): The person appointed by the ruler to lead the Friday prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a judge appoints a deputy without the ruler's permission?
A) It is valid if the deputy is qualified.
B) It is invalid unless the judge later approves the deputy's actions.
C) It is valid only for matters the judge cannot handle himself.
D) It is valid because the judge has inherent authority.

Key Takeaway
A judge cannot appoint a deputy without the ruler's permission, analogous to agency; the Friday prayer imam is an exception due to time constraints.

Validity of Deputy's Judgment with Later Approval
Ruling that a deputy's judgment becomes valid with later approval

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a deputy's judgment when the judge later approves, and explain the analogy to agency that supports it.

Core Idea
A deputy's judgment becomes valid when the judge later approves it, because the judge's opinion is now present.

This passage from the Hidayah and Bada'i clarifies that a deputy's judgment, even if given without prior permission, can be made valid by subsequent approval. The key is that the judge's opinion, which is the condition for a valid judgment, is fulfilled at the time of approval. The proof is drawn from the analogy of an agent's approval of a sub-agent's actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a deputy judge giving a judgment without the original judge's prior permission. The ruling is that the judgment becomes valid (sahih) if the judge later approves it.
This applies whether the judgment was given in the judge's presence or absence.
2
Determine the condition for validity
The condition is that the judge's opinion must be present in the judgment. Later approval supplies this condition.
The passage explicitly states that the judge's opinion is the condition (shart) for validity.
3
Analyze the analogy to agency
The ruling is derived via qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) to the case of an agent who appoints a sub-agent without permission, but later approves the sub-agent's action. Both become valid with subsequent approval.
Sahib al-Hidayah uses this analogy to demonstrate that the same reasoning applies in judiciary.
4
Apply the ruling to both scenarios
The passage states that the ruling holds whether the deputy acted in the judge's presence or absence. In both cases, later approval validates the judgment.
Presence alone is insufficient; approval is required. However, approval can be implicit if the judge was present and did not object, though the text mentions explicit permission.
5
Conclude with the Hanafi position
The mufta bihi position is that the deputy's judgment is valid with subsequent approval, provided the deputy is qualified. This is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
No intra-Hanafi disagreement is recorded on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب بدائیہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر قاضی نے امام المسلمین کی اجازت کے بغیر اپنا خلیفہ اور نائب مقرر کیا اور اس نے کسی مقدمہ میں اصل قاضی کی موجودگی میں کوئی فیصلہ دیا یا قاضی کی عدم موجودگی میں فیصلہ دیا مگر جب قاضی کو معلوم ہوا تو قاضی نے اجازت دیدی تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں نائب کا فیصلہ جائز اور قابل عمل ہوگا۔ بشرطیکہ نائب صاحب میں اہلیت قضا موجود ہو۔ اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے کسی وکیل نے اپنے مؤکل کی اجازت کے بغیر کسی دوسرے آدمی کو اپنی طرف سے وکیل مقرر کر دیا اور وکیل ثانی نے وکیل اول کی موجودگی میں تصرف کیا یا وکیل اول کی عدم موجودگی میں تصرف کیا۔ مگر وکیل اول نے اجازت دیدی تو دونوں صورتوں میں وکیل ثانی کا تصرف جائز ہوتا ہے۔ پس اسی طرح مذکورہ دونوں صورتوں میں نائب قاضی کا حکم بھی جائز اور نافذ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے مسئلہ قضاء اور مسئلہ وکالت میں جواز کی دلیل دیتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ جب خلیفہ اور نائب نے اصل قاضی کی موجودگی میں حکم دیا ، یا اصل قاضی کی عدم موجودگی میں حکم دیا تھا مگر اصل قاضی نے اس کو جائز کر دیا تو اس حکم میں اصل قاضی کی رائے موجود ہوگئی اور یہی جو از حکم کی شرط ہے۔ پس جب اصل قاضی کی رائے ( جو جو از حکم کے لئے شری تھی وہ پائی گئی تو یہ حکم نافذ ہو گا۔ یہی تقریر مسئلہ وکالت میں کی جائے گی۔
Sahib al-Bada'i says: If a judge appointed his deputy and caliph without the permission of the leader of the Muslims, and that deputy gave a judgment in a case in the presence of the original judge, or gave a judgment in the absence of the judge, but when the judge found out, he gave permission, then in both cases the deputy's judgment is valid and enforceable, provided that the deputy possesses the qualifications for being a judge. Its example is like when an agent appoints another agent on his behalf without the client's permission, and the second agent performs a transaction in the presence of the first agent, or in the absence of the first agent, but the first agent gave permission; then in both cases the transaction of the second agent is valid. So similarly, in the two mentioned cases, the judgment of the deputy judge is also valid and effective. Sahib al-Hidayah, while giving the proof for validity in the case of judiciary and agency, said: When the deputy and caliph gave judgment in the presence of the original judge, or gave judgment in the absence of the original judge, but the original judge validated it, then the opinion of the original judge is present in that judgment, and that is the condition for the validity of the judgment. So when the opinion of the original judge (which was the condition for validity) is found, this judgment becomes effective. This same reasoning is applied in the case of agency.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, expanding on the validity of a deputy's judgment when the judge later approves. Sahib al-Bada'i and Sahib al-Hidayah both state that if a judge appoints a deputy without permission, but the deputy gives a judgment either in the judge's presence or absence, and the judge later gives permission, the judgment is valid and enforceable. The condition is that the deputy must be qualified to be a judge. The proof is an analogy to agency: if an agent appoints a sub-agent without permission, but later approves the sub-agent's action, it is valid. The key reason is that the judge's opinion becomes present in the judgment, which is the condition for validity. This ruling applies whether the deputy acted in the judge's presence or absence, as long as the judge subsequently approves.

Key Terms
اجازت (ijāzat): Permission or approval granted by the judge after the fact, making the deputy's judgment valid.
حکم (hukm): The judgment or decision given by the deputy in a case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect when a judge later approves a deputy's judgment given without permission?
A) The judgment becomes valid only if it was given in the judge's presence.
B) The judgment becomes valid only if it was given in the judge's absence.
C) The judgment becomes valid in both cases, as the judge's opinion is now present.
D) The judgment remains invalid unless the ruler also approves.

Key Takeaway
A deputy's judgment without prior permission is valid if the judge later approves it, because the judge's opinion becomes present.

When Ruler Gives Judge Authority to Appoint Deputy
Ruling that the deputy becomes the ruler's deputy, not the judge's

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a ruler gives a judge authority to appoint a deputy and identify who has the power to remove the deputy.

Core Idea
The judge's appointed deputy is the ruler's deputy, not the judge's — removal power stays with the ruler unless delegated.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key question in judicial delegation: When the ruler tells a judge, 'Appoint whomever you wish,' and the judge appoints a deputy, who really appointed that deputy? The ruling clarifies that the deputy becomes the ruler's deputy, and thus the judge cannot remove him without separate permission. This distinction preserves the ruler's ultimate authority over judicial appointments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is the ruler explicitly giving the judge permission to appoint a deputy (e.g., 'Appoint whomever you wish'). Note that the ruler is delegating his own authority to appoint, not transferring ownership of the appointment power.
The ruler's phrase 'ولّ من شئت' is key.
2
Determine the legal nature of the deputy's appointment
The deputy appointed by the judge is legally considered the deputy of the ruler (Imam al-Muslimin), not the judge. This is because the appointment authority ultimately flows from the ruler.
3
Identify the consequence for the judge
Since the deputy is the ruler's deputy, the judge does not have the authority to remove him. The power of removal remains with the ruler.
The text states: 'يہی وجہ ہے کہ قاضی اول اس کو معزول کرنے کے کا مجاز نہیں ہوتا'
4
Note the exception when removal authority is also delegated
If the ruler explicitly gives the judge the authority to remove (e.g., 'and replace whomever you wish'), then the judge can remove the deputy. This is the correct view (sahih qawl).
The condition is explicit delegation of removal power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر سلطان اور امام المسلمین نے قاضی کو نائب اور خلیفہ بنانے کا اختیار دیا مثلاً سلطان نے قاضی سے کہا کہ ” ولّ من شئت ، تو جس کو چاہے اپنا والی اور نائب مقرر کر ” قاضی کو یہ اختیار حاصل ہوگا۔ لیکن یہ خیال رہے کہ دوسرا قاضی جس کو قاضی اول نے منتخب کیا ہے وہ امام مسلمین اور سلطان وقت کا نائب ہوگا ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ قاضی اول اس کو معزول کرنے کے کا مجاز نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ اس کا تقر ر امام المسلمین کی جانب سے ہوا ہے۔ لہذا اس کو معزول کرنے کا اختیار بھی امام المسلمین ہی کو حاصل ہو گا۔ ہاں اگر امام المسلمین نے قاضی کو معزول کرنے کا اختیار بھی دیدیا ہو۔ مثلاً یہ کہا ہو و استبدِل مَنْ شئتَ ۔ یعنی جس کو چاہے تبدیل کر تو صحیح قول کے مطابق اس صورت میں قاضی اول نائب کو معزول کرنے کا بھی مجاز ہو گا۔ اور اگر سلطان نے کسی کو قاضی القضاۃ کا
Sahib al-Hidayah says: If the sultan and leader of the Muslims gave the judge the authority to appoint a deputy and caliph, for example the sultan said to the judge, 'Appoint whomever you wish,' meaning, appoint whomever you want as your governor and deputy, then the judge will have that authority. But it should be noted that the second judge whom the first judge selects will be the deputy of the leader of the Muslims and the sultan of the time. This is why the first judge is not authorized to remove him. Because his appointment is from the leader of the Muslims. Therefore, the authority to remove him also belongs only to the leader of the Muslims. Yes, if the leader of the Muslims also gave the judge the authority to remove, for example he said, 'And replace whomever you wish,' meaning change whomever you want, then according to the correct view, in that case the first judge is also authorized to remove the deputy. And if the sultan appoints someone as the Qadi al-Qudat... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the consequence when the ruler explicitly gives the judge authority to appoint a deputy. If the ruler says 'Appoint whomever you wish,' the judge can appoint a deputy, but the appointed deputy becomes the deputy of the ruler, not the judge. Therefore, the judge cannot remove him; only the ruler can. However, if the ruler also gives the judge authority to remove (e.g., 'and replace whomever you wish'), then the judge can remove the deputy. This is the correct view (sahih qawl). The text ends mid-sentence referring to the case of Qadi al-Qudat, but the page is cut off.

Key Terms
تولية (tawliyah): The act of appointing someone as a deputy or governor; here it refers to the judge's authority to appoint a deputy.
معزول (ma'zūl): Removed from office; the judge cannot remove the deputy appointed with the ruler's authority unless given that power.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The deputy appointed by a judge with the ruler's permission is the ruler's deputy; only the ruler can remove unless he delegates removal authority.

Enforcement of a Previous Judge's Ruling
Ruling on enforcement of judicial decisions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a higher judge must enforce a lower judge's decision and identify the exceptions based on clear textual contradictions.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling on a matter of ijtihad is binding on all subsequent judges unless it violates a definitive text or consensus.

Judicial finality and respect for prior decisions are crucial for legal stability. This lesson explains the Hanafi position that a judge presented with another judge's ruling (ḥukm ḥākim) must enforce it, except when it clearly contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma. The principle rests on the equality of ijtihad and the strength given by the actual execution of the first ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
State the default obligation: a judge must enforce a previous judicial ruling.
From al-Quduri: 'amḍāhu' – he enforces it.
2
List the exceptions
Identify the three overriding sources: contradiction with Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma. Also note the variant 'or an opinion with no evidence'.
These are definitive (qaṭʿī) sources that override ijtihad.
3
Understand the rationale from al-Jami' al-Saghir
When jurists differ, and a judge rules on one view, a later judge with a different view must uphold the first ruling because both ijtihads are equal, but the first is reinforced by the judicial decision.
Key phrase: 'lā yarudduhu ghayruhu' – no other can reject it.
4
Apply the examples
Work through the four examples: (a) ruling allowing eating without tasmiyah, (b) ruling based on one witness + oath, (c) ruling making a triple-divorced woman halal via invalid marriage, (d) ruling allowing mutʿah marriage. Confirm each contradicts a clear dalīl.
These illustrate when the exception applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا رفع الى القاضي حكم حاكم امضاه الا ان يخالف الكتاب او السنة او الاجماع بان يكون قولاً لا دليل عليه. و في الجامع الصغير: وما اختلف فيه الفقهاء فقضى به القاضى ثم جاء قاض آخر بغير ذلك امضاه. والاصل ان القضاء متى لاقى فصلا مجتهداً فيه ينفذ ولا يرده غيره لان اجتهاد الثاني كاجتهاد الاول وقد ترجح الاول باتصال القضاء به فلا ينقص بما هو دونه. ترجمہ: اور اگر کسی حاکم کے حکم کا کسی قاضی کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا تو قاضی اس حکم کو نافذ کرے گا۔ مگر یہ کہ وہ حکم کتاب یا سنت یا اجماع کے خلاف ہو۔ بایں طور کہ ایسا قول ہو جس پر کوئی دلیل موجود نہ ہو۔ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ جس مسئلہ میں فقہا نے اختلاف کیا پھر کسی قاضی نے اس میں حکم دیا پھر دوسرا قاضی آیا جس کی رائے اس کے خلاف ہے تو وہ بھی حکم اول کو نافذ کرے اور قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ جب کسی مختلف فیہ صورت میں حکم قضاء لاحق ہوتا ہے تو وہ نافذ ہو جاتا ہے اور دوسرا حاکم اس کو رد نہیں کر سکتا اس لئے کہ دوسرے کا اجتہاد اول کے اجتہاد کے مانند ہے۔ اور اجتہاد اول کے ساتھ حکم قضاء متصل ہو کر اس کو ترجیح ہو گئی تو وہ ایسے اجتہاد سے نہیں ٹوٹے گا جو اس سے کمتر ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ اگر کسی قاضی کی عدالت میں کسی حاکم کے حکم کا مرافعہ کیا گیا یعنی اپیل کی ہے تو قاضی اسی سابقہ حکم کو نافذ کرے گا بشرطیکہ حاکم کا یہ حکم کتاب اللہ سنت رسول اور اجماع کے خلاف نہ ہو۔ چنانچہ اگر حاکم کا حکم مذکورہ ادلہ میں سے کسی کے خلاف ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے وہ اس حکم کو نافذ نہ کرے گا ۔ مثلا ما تحت قاضی نے متروک التسمیہ عامداً کے حلال ہونے کا حکم دیا۔ حالانکہ یہ حکم باری تعالیٰ کے قول ولا تأكلوا ممالم يذكر اسم الله علیہ کے خلاف ہے یا مثلا ما تحت قاضی نے ایک گواہ اور مدعی کی قسم کی بنیاد پر فیصلہ دیدیا حالانکہ یہ حکم باری تعالیٰ کے قول فاستشهدوا شهيدين من رجالكم فان لم يكونا رجلين فرجل وامراتان کے خلاف ہے۔ یا مثلا ما تحت قاضی نے یہ حکم دیا کہ مطلقہ ثلاث بغیر ولی کے محض زوج ثانی کے ساتھ نکاح کرنے سے زوج اول کے لئے حلال ہوگئی ہے حالانکہ یہ حکم حدیث رفاعہ لا حتى تذوقي من عسيلته و يذوق من عسیلتک کے خلاف ہے۔ یا مثلاً ما تحت قاضی نے نکاح متعہ کے حلال ہونے کا حکم دیا۔ حالانکہ یہ حکم اجماع صحابہ کے خلاف ہے۔ پس ان صورتوں میں اگر قاضی اعلیٰ کی عدالت میں اپیل کی گئی تو قاضی اعلیٰ ماتحت قاضی کے اُس حکم کو نافذ نہ کرے جو کتاب یا سنت یا اجماع کے خلاف ہے۔ قدوری کی عبارت بان يكون قولا لا دليل عليه میں ایک نسخہ کے مطابق تو یہی عبارت ہے۔ اور تندوری کے بعض نسخوں میں ۔ او يكون قولاً لا دلیل علیہ کی عبارت ہے۔ پس'' او يـكـون قولا لا دليل علیہ نسخہ کے مطابق عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ اگر قاضی اعلیٰ کی عدالت میں ماتحت قاضی کے کسی فیصلہ کا اپیل کیا گیا تو قاضی اعلیٰ اُسی فیصلہ کو نافذ کرے گا۔ لیکن اگر ماتحت قاضی کا فیصلہ قرآن حدیث یا سنت کے خلاف ہوا جیسا کہ سابق میں مثالیں گذر چکیں یا
He said: And when the ruling of a ruler is presented to a judge, he enforces it, unless it contradicts the Book, the Sunnah, or the Consensus, such that it is an opinion for which there is no evidence. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: In a matter over which the jurists differed, and a judge gave a ruling, then another judge came with a different opinion, he enforces it. The principle is that whenever a judicial decision meets an issue open to ijtihad, it takes effect and no other can reject it, because the ijtihad of the second is like the ijtihad of the first, and the first has been strengthened by being connected to the judicial decision, so it is not weakened by something that is inferior to it. Translation: And if the ruling of a ruler is referred to a judge, the judge will enforce it, unless that ruling contradicts the Book, the Sunnah, or the Consensus, such that it is an opinion for which there is no evidence. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: In a matter over which the jurists differed, then a judge gave a ruling, then another judge came whose opinion is contrary to it, he also enforces the first ruling. The general rule is that when a judicial decision is attached to a matter that is subject to ijtihad, it takes effect and another ruler cannot reject it, because the ijtihad of the second is like the ijtihad of the first, and the first has been strengthened by the connection of the judicial decision, so it will not be broken by an ijtihad that is inferior to it. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: If the ruling of a ruler is referred to a judge, i.e., an appeal is made, then the judge will enforce that previous ruling, provided that the ruler's ruling does not contradict the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger, or the Consensus. Thus, if the ruler's ruling contradicts any of these evidences, then the higher judge to whom the appeal is made will not enforce it. For example, a subordinate judge ruled that intentionally omitting the tasmiyah is permissible, although this ruling contradicts the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And do not eat of that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' (Quran 6:121). Or for example, a subordinate judge decided based on one witness and the plaintiff's oath, although this ruling contradicts the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And call to witness two witnesses from among your men; and if there are not two men, then one man and two women' (Quran 2:282). Or for example, a subordinate judge ruled that a thrice-divorced woman becomes permissible to her first husband by merely marrying a second husband without a guardian, although this ruling contradicts the hadith of Rifa'ah: 'Not until you taste his honey and he tastes your honey.' Or for example, a subordinate judge ruled that temporary marriage (nikah mut'ah) is permissible, although this ruling contradicts the consensus of the Companions. So in these cases, if an appeal is made to the higher judge, the higher judge will not enforce that ruling of the subordinate judge which contradicts the Book, the Sunnah, or the Consensus. In al-Quduri's phrase 'بأن يكون قولا لا دليل عليه' according to one version, it is this phrase. And in some copies of al-Tanduri, there is the phrase 'أو يكون قولا لا دليل عليه'. So according to the version with 'أو', the meaning of the phrase would be: If the ruling of a subordinate judge is appealed to the higher judge, the higher judge will enforce that ruling, unless the subordinate judge's ruling contradicts the Quran, the Hadith, or the Sunnah, as examples have passed before, or
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a key principle in Hanafi judicial procedure: the respect for previously rendered judicial decisions. It begins by quoting from al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir (both Zahir al-Riwayah sources). The ruling is that when a judge is presented with a ruling from another judge (حكم حاكم), he must enforce it (يمضيه) unless it contradicts the Quran, the Sunnah, or the Consensus (الإجماع). The phrase 'بان يكون قولا لا دليل عليه' clarifies that if the ruling is based on an opinion that has no evidence, it is equivalent to contradicting the primary sources. The passage then cites al-Jami' al-Saghir, establishing a principle: if jurists have differed on a matter, and a judge gives a ruling based on one opinion, a subsequent judge with a different view must still enforce the first ruling if it is brought before him. The reasoning is that the first ruling has been 'connected to the judicial decision' (اتصل به القضاء), giving it precedence. The ijtihad of the second judge is not superior to that of the first, so he cannot overturn it. This principle is often expressed as 'اجتهاد لا ينقض بمثله' (ijtihad is not overturned by similar ijtihad). The passage then gives examples of rulings that are against clear texts: (1) declaring permissible eating without saying Bismillah intentionally (against Quran 6:121), (2) deciding on the basis of one witness plus oath (against Quran 2:282), (3) allowing a thrice-divorced woman to remarry the first husband without a proper second marriage with guardian (against the hadith of Rifa'ah), and (4) allowing temporary marriage (against Ijma of the Companions). In each case, the higher judge must not enforce such a ruling. The passage also notes a textual variant in al-Quduri's phrasing: some copies have 'أو يكون قولا لا دليل عليه' (or it is an opinion without evidence) instead of 'بان يكون'. This variant broadens the scope: the higher judge enforces the ruling unless it is either against Quran/Sunnah/Ijma OR is an opinion without evidence. The commentary ends mid-sentence but the essential ruling is clear.

Key Terms
حكم حاكم (ḥukm ḥākim): A ruling or decision issued by a judge or ruler (ḥākim).
امضى (amḍā): To enforce or execute a previous ruling; to uphold it.
اجتهاد (ijtihād): Independent legal reasoning by a qualified jurist to derive a ruling from the sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir, when must a higher judge refuse to enforce a lower judge's ruling?
A) Whenever the higher judge has a different opinion based on ijtihad.
B) Only if the ruling contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma.
C) Only if the ruling is clearly unjust.
D) Whenever the higher judge thinks the lower judge was incompetent.

Key Takeaway
A prior judicial decision on a matter of ijtihad is binding on subsequent judges unless it directly contradicts a definitive source (Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma).

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
12 min
Enforcement of a Prior Judge's Ruling by a Higher Judge
Ruling with proof on judicial enforcement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when a higher judge must enforce a prior judge's decision, identify the exceptions (contradiction to Quran/Sunnah/Ijma or baseless opinion), and apply the nuance regarding the first judge's awareness of ijtihad.

Core Idea
A valid ijtihad-based ruling is binding on the higher judge unless it clearly contradicts a definitive text.

In this passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya, we examine a key principle of Hanafi judicial procedure: the binding force of a prior judge's decision on a higher judge. The rule is straightforward—enforce unless contradictory—but the commentary introduces a critical nuance about the first judge's knowledge of juristic disagreement. By the end, you will understand both the core rule and its essential refinement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule from al-Quduri
Extract the basic ruling: a higher judge must enforce the prior judge's ruling unless it contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, or if it is an opinion with no evidence.
This is the default position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Recognize the types of contradictions
Review the examples: rulings that permit eating without tasmiyah (contradicts Quran 6:121), accept one witness and oath (contradicts Quran 2:282), allow remarriage without halalah (contradicts hadith), or permit mut'ah marriage (contradicts Ijma). Also, rulings that have no basis in Shariah, like dropping a debt after 12 years.
Contradictions to clear texts make the ruling invalid (batil) and unenforceable.
3
Understand the extra benefit from al-Jami' al-Saghir
Al-Jami' al-Saghir adds two points: (1) The first judge's awareness of juristic ikhtilaf matters—if he was unaware, the majority of later scholars say enforcement is not wajib; if aware, it is wajib. (2) Enforcement is required regardless of whether the higher judge agrees or disagrees with the ruling, as long as it does not contradict clear texts.
These nuances refine al-Quduri's statement and are essential for correct application.
4
Grasp the underlying principle
The text states: 'the ijtihad of the second is like the ijtihad of the first, and the first has been strengthened by the connection of the judgment to it.' This means both judges have equal authority in ijtihad, and once a ruling is passed, it gains a binding force that cannot be undone by another ijtihad.
This principle ensures stability and finality in judicial decisions.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical
Consider a scenario: A first judge, aware of khilaf, rules in favor of a creditor in a disputed loan case. The higher judge disagrees with the ruling. Must he enforce? Yes, because it is a valid ijtihad-based ruling not contradicting clear texts. Now, if the first judge was unaware of the khilaf and ruled coincidentally according to a minority view, the higher judge is not obliged to enforce according to the majority.
This illustrates the practical difference the awareness condition makes.

قال القدوري: واذا رفع الى القاضي حكم حاكم امضاه الا ان يخالف الكتاب او السنة او الاجماع بان يكون قولا لا دليل عليه. و في الجامع الصغير: و ما اختلف فيه الفقهاء فقضى به القاضي ثم جاء قاضي آخر يرى غير ذلك امضاه. و الاصل ان القضاء متى لاقى فصلا مجتهدا فيه ينفذ و لا يرده غيره لان اجتهاد الثاني كاجتهاد الاول و قد ترجح الاول باتصال القضاء به فلا ينقص بما هو دونه۔ تشریح: صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ اگر کسی قاضی کی عدالت میں کسی حاکم کے حکم کا مرافعہ کیا گیا یعنی اپیل کی ہے تو قاضی اسی سابقہ حکم کو نافذ کرے گا بشرطیکہ حاکم کا یہ حکم کتاب اللہ سنت رسول اور اجماع کے خلاف نہ ہو۔ چنانچہ اگر حاکم کا حکم مذکورہ ادلہ میں سے کسی کے خلاف ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے وہ اس حکم کو نافذ نہ کرے گا ۔ مثلا ما تحت قاضی نے متروک التسمیۃ عامداً کے حلال ہونے کا حکم دیا حالانکہ یہ حکم باری تعالیٰ کے قول ولا تأكلوا ممالم يذكر اسم الله عليه کے خلاف ہے۔ یا مثلا ما تحت قاضی نے ایک گواہ اور مدعی کی قسم کی بنیاد پر فیصلہ دیدیا حالانکہ یہ حکم باری تعالیٰ کے قول فاستشهدوا شهيدين من رجالكم فان لم يكونا رجلين فرجل وامراتان کے خلاف ہے۔ یا مثلا ما تحت قاضی نے یہ حکم دیا کہ مطلقۃ ثلاث بغیر ولی کے محض زوج ثانی کے ساتھ نکاح کرنے سے زوج اول کے لئے حلال ہوگئی ہے حالانکہ یہ حکم حدیث رفاعہ: لا حتى تذوقي من عسيلته و يذوق من عسيلتك کے خلاف ہے۔ یا مثلاً ما تحت قاضی نے نکاح متعہ کے حلال ہونے کا حکم دیا، حالانکہ یہ حکم اجماع صحابہ کے خلاف ہے۔ پس ان صورتوں میں اگر قاضی اعلیٰ کی عدالت میں اپیل کی گئی تو قاضی اعلیٰ ماتحت قاضی کے اُس حکم کو نافذ نہ کرے جو کتاب یا سنت یا اجماع کے خلاف ہے۔ قدوری کی عبارت "بان يكون قولا لا دليل عليه" میں ایک نسخہ کے مطابق تو یہی عبارت ہے۔ اور بعض نسخوں میں "او يكون قولا لا دليل عليه" عبارت ہے۔ پس "او يكون قولا لا دليل عليه" نسخہ کے مطابق عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ اگر قاضی اعلیٰ کی عدالت میں ماتحت قاضی کے کسی فیصلہ کا اپیل کیا گیا تو قاضی اعلیٰ اُسی فیصلہ کو نافذ کرے گا۔ لیکن اگر ماتحت قاضی کا فیصلہ قرآن حدیث یا سنت کے خلاف ہوا جیسا کہ سابق میں مثالیں گذر چکیں یا ماتحت قاضی کا حکم ایسا قول ہو جس پر کوئی دلیل نہ ہو (مثلاً ماتحت قاضی نے بارہ سال گذر جانے پر مطالبہ میں تاخیر کی وجہ سے قرضدار کے ذمہ سے قرضہ ساقط ہونے کا حکم دیا اور یہ ایسا قول ہے جس پر کوئی دلیل شرعی نہیں ہے) تو ان صورتوں میں قاضی اعلیٰ ماتحت قاضی کا فیصلہ نافذ نہ کرے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ جامع صغیر میں یہ مسئلہ اس طرح مذکور ہے کہ اگر کسی مسئلہ میں فقہا کا اختلاف ہو اور ایک قاضی نے اس میں حکم دیا پھر دوسرا قاضی آیا جس کی رائے اس کے خلاف ہے تو دوسرا قاضی اسی فیصلہ کو نافذ کرے گا جو فیصلہ قاضی اول نے دیا ہے بشرطیکہ قاضی اول کا دیا ہوا فیصلہ کتاب یا حدیث یا اجماع کے خلاف نہ ہو۔ سوال: یہاں ایک سوال ہو سکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ جب جامع صغیر کی عبارت میں وہی مسئلہ مذکور ہے جو مسئلہ قدوری کی عبارت میں ذکر کیا گیا ہے تو قدوری کی عبارت کے مذکور ہونے کے بعد جامع صغیر کی عبارت ذکر کرنے کی کیا ضرورت تھی؟ جواب: اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جامع صغیر کی عبارت میں ایسے دو فائدے مذکور ہیں جن سے قدوری کی عبارت خالی ہے۔ پہلا فائدہ تو یہ ہے کہ جامع صغیر کی عبارت میں فقہا کی قید سے اس طرف اشارہ ہے کہ اگر قاضی اول موضع اجتہاد سے واقف نہ ہو بلکہ اُس کا فیصلہ اتفاقاً موضع اجتہاد کے موافق ہو گیا یعنی کسی فقیہ کے قول کے موافق ہو گیا تو عامۃ المشائخ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ قاضی اعلیٰ جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے اس پر اس فیصلہ کا نافذ کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر قاضی اول موضع اجتہاد سے واقف ہو یعنی اختلاف فقہا کا علم رکھتے ہوئے کسی فقیہ کے قول کے موافق فیصلہ دیا تو قاضی اعلیٰ پر اس کا نافذ کرنا واجب ہوگا اگر چہ یہ فیصلہ قاضی اعلیٰ کی رائے کے خلاف ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔ دوسرا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ جامع صغیر کی عبارت "يرى غير ذلك" اس طرف مشیر ہے کہ قاضی اول کا دیا ہوا فیصلہ اگر کتاب یا سنت یا اجماع کے خلاف نہ ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ جس کی عدالت میں مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے وہ اُسی کو نافذ کرے گا خواہ وہ فیصلہ قاضی اعلیٰ کی رائے کے مخالف ہو یا موافق ہو کیونکہ جس صورت میں قاضی اول کا دیا ہوا فیصلہ قاضی اعلیٰ کی رائے کے خلاف ہے جب اُس صورت میں اُس کو نافذ کرنا ضروری ہے تو جس صورت میں قاضی اول کا فیصلہ قاضی اعلیٰ کی رائے کے موافق ہوگا اُس صورت میں اس کو نافذ کرنا بدرجہ اولیٰ ضروری ہوگا۔ ملاحظہ فرمائیے مذکورہ جن فائدوں کی طرف جامع صغیر کی عبارت میں اشارہ کیا گیا ہے قدوری کی عبارت ان دو فائدوں سے ساکت ہے پس انھیں دو فائدوں کی وجہ سے قدوری کی عبارت کے بعد جامع صغیر کی عبارت کا ذکر کرنا ضروری سمجھا گیا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ قاضی اول کا فیصلہ اگر کتاب یا سنت یا اجماع کے خلاف نہ ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ کے اس فیصلے کو نافذ کرنے اور نہ کرنے کے سلسلہ میں قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی مختلف فیہ مسئلہ میں قاضی نے کوئی حکم دیا ہو تو وہ نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ قاضی اعلیٰ (جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے) اس کو رد کرنے یا باطل کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا کیونکہ قاضی اعلیٰ کا اجتہاد قاضی اول کے اجتہاد کے مانند ہے۔
Al-Quduri said: When a judge is presented with the ruling of a ruler, he enforces it unless it contradicts the Book, the Sunnah, or Ijma, provided it is an opinion with no evidence for it. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Whatever the jurists have differed about, and a judge gave a ruling on it, then another judge comes who holds a different opinion, he enforces it. The principle is that when a judgment meets a matter open to ijtihad, it is executed and no one else can reject it, because the ijtihad of the second is like the ijtihad of the first, and the first has been strengthened by the connection of the judgment to it, so it is not invalidated by what is inferior to it. Commentary: The author of al-Quduri said: If the ruling of a ruler is appealed to a judge, the judge enforces the previous ruling provided it does not contradict the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger, or Ijma. Thus if the ruler's ruling contradicts any of these, the higher judge to whom the appeal is made does not enforce it. For example, if a subordinate judge ruled that intentionally omitting the tasmiyah is permissible, while this contradicts Allah's statement: 'And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' (6:121). Or if he ruled based on one witness and the plaintiff's oath, contradicting 'And bring to witness two witnesses from among your men; and if there are not two men, then one man and two women' (2:282). Or if he ruled that a woman divorced three times becomes lawful to the first husband by merely marrying a second husband without a guardian, contradicting the hadith of Rifa'ah: 'not until you taste his sweetness and he tastes your sweetness.' Or if he ruled that mut'ah marriage is lawful, contradicting the Ijma of the Companions. In these cases, if appealed to a higher judge, he does not enforce the subordinate judge's ruling that contradicts the Book, Sunnah, or Ijma. In al-Quduri's phrase 'provided it is an opinion with no evidence for it,' according to one manuscript it is this. In some manuscripts it is 'or it is an opinion with no evidence for it.' According to the latter, the meaning is that if the subordinate judge's ruling is appealed, the higher judge enforces it unless it contradicts Quran, Hadith, or Sunnah, or it is an opinion with no evidence (e.g., the subordinate judge ruled that a debt is dropped after twelve years due to delay in claiming, which has no legal evidence). In those cases the higher judge does not enforce it. The author of al-Hidayah said: In al-Jami' al-Saghir, this issue is mentioned as: If jurists differ on a matter and a judge gives a ruling, then another judge comes who holds a contrary opinion, the second judge enforces the first judge's ruling provided it does not contradict the Book, Hadith, or Ijma. Question: Why repeat the same issue from al-Jami' al-Saghir after al-Quduri? Answer: Because al-Jami' al-Saghir's wording contains two benefits absent from al-Quduri. First, the mention of 'jurists' indicates that if the first judge was unaware of the field of ijtihad and his ruling coincidentally agreed with a jurist's opinion, the majority of mashayikh hold that the higher judge is not obliged to enforce it. But if he was aware of the juristic difference and ruled in accordance with a jurist, then enforcement is obligatory even if contrary to the higher judge's view. Second, the phrase 'he holds a different opinion' indicates that if the first judge's ruling does not contradict Book, Sunnah, or Ijma, the higher judge enforces it whether it agrees with his view or not, because if enforcement is necessary when contrary, it is even more necessary when agreeable. Observe these two benefits are absent from al-Quduri's wording, so it was deemed necessary to cite al-Jami' al-Saghir afterward. The author of al-Hidayah said: The general principle concerning whether a higher judge enforces the first judge's ruling (if not contradicting Book, Sunnah, or Ijma) is that if a judge gave a ruling on a matter open to ijtihad, it becomes executed. The higher judge (to whom appeal is made) is not authorized to reject or nullify it, because the ijtihad of the higher judge is like the ijtihad of the first judge.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya, commenting on the chapter of Adab al-Qadi (Etiquette of the Judge), deals with the authority of a prior judge's ruling when it is brought before a higher judge. The ruling is taken from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, a foundational Hanafi text: the higher judge must enforce the lower judge's ruling unless it contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma (consensus), or if it is an opinion with no evidence. The author then cites al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani to add two important nuances. First, the lower judge must be aware of the differing juristic opinions (i.e., he must know that he is ruling in a matter open to ijtihad); if he rules without such awareness, even if his ruling coincidentally matches a jurist's view, the higher judge is not obliged to enforce it. Second, the wording 'يرى غير ذلك' (he holds a different opinion) shows that enforcement is required regardless of whether the higher judge agrees or disagrees with the ruling, as long as it does not contradict clear texts. The passage then gives examples of rulings that clearly contradict Quran (e.g., permitting meat without tasmiyah, accepting one witness and oath), Sunnah (e.g., allowing remarriage after triple divorce without proper halalah), and Ijma (e.g., allowing mut'ah marriage). These are batil (invalid) and must not be enforced. The key principle is that a valid ijtihad-based ruling, once passed and connected to execution, gains a binding force that another judge cannot undo because both judges' ijtihad are equal in authority. This ensures stability in judicial decisions.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): The ruling/decision issued by a judge or ruler; in this context, the prior judgment brought for appeal.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Independent legal reasoning in matters where no clear text exists; the field of ikhtilaf among jurists.
اختلاف الفقهاء (ikhtilaf al-fuqaha): Disagreement among jurists on a legal issue within the scope of ijtihad; the passage treats such cases as subject to enforcement unless contradicting clear texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when must a higher judge enforce a prior judge's decision?
A) Always, regardless of any error
B) Only if the higher judge agrees with the ruling
C) Unless it contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, or is an opinion with no evidence
D) Only if the first judge was aware of juristic differences

Key Takeaway
A higher judge must enforce a prior ijtihad-based ruling unless it contradicts a definitive text or is baseless; the first judge's awareness of ikhtilaf is a necessary condition for obligation.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Enforceability of a Subordinate Judge's Judgment
Explaining when a higher judge must enforce a subordinate's ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a higher judge must enforce a subordinate judge's judgment, distinguish between matters of ijtihad and matters with clear texts, and apply this principle to given scenarios.

Core Idea
A subordinate judge's ruling in a matter of ijtihad is binding on the higher judge, unless it contradicts the Qur'an, Sunnah, or Ijma'.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the crucial distinction between enforceable and unenforceable judgments of subordinate judges in the Hanafi judicial system. It clarifies that a higher judge must respect the ijtihad of a lower judge, even if his own ijtihad differs, as long as the ruling does not violate definitive texts. The practice of Caliph Umar provides strong backing for this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of judgments
Recognize that some judgments are based on clear legal evidence (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma') and others are mere opinions without evidence. The passage gives the example of a debt dropped after twelve years without textual support.
2
Understand the condition for non-enforcement
A higher judge must not enforce a subordinate's judgment if it contradicts the Qur'an, Sunnah, or Ijma'. Such a judgment is considered a statement without evidence and is void.
3
Apply the rule from al-Jami' al-Saghir
In matters where jurists differ (mujtahad fih), if a judge rules according to a valid opinion, a subsequent judge must enforce it, even if his own opinion differs. The rule applies as long as the ruling does not oppose the primary texts.
4
Recognize the additional condition of awareness
The commentary highlights that the first judge must be aware of the scope of ijtihad (maudi' al-ijtihad) for his ruling to be binding. If he accidentally agrees with a jurist without knowledge, the higher judge is not obligated to enforce.
This condition is derived from al-Jami' al-Saghir, not from al-Quduri.
5
Analyse the proof from Umar's practice
Caliph Umar refused to overturn a ruling of his subordinate judge Abu al-Darda', stating 'There is no text here, and opinion is shared.' This demonstrates that in ijtihad matters, the first ruling is final.
The ijtihad of the first judge is considered stronger because it is accompanied by a judicial ruling.

كتاب الادب القاضي ماتحت قاضی کا حکم ایسا قول ہو جس پر کوئی دلیل نہ ہو۔ ( مثلاً ما تحت قاضی نے بارہ سال گذر جانے پر مطالبہ میں تاخیر کی وجہ سے قرضدار کے ذمہ سے قرضہ ساقط ہونے کا حکم دیا اور یہ انیسا قول ہے جس پر کوئی دلیل شرعی نہیں ہے ) ۔ تو ان صورتوں میں قاضی اعلیٰ، ماتحت قاضی کا فیصلہ نافذ نہ کرے گا۔ اور بان يكون قولاً لا دلیل علیہ نسخہ کے مطابق یہ عبارت الا ان يخالف الكتاب الخ کی علت واقع ہوگی۔ اور مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ ماتحت قاضی کا فیصلہ اگر کتاب یا حدیث یا اجماع کے خلاف ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ اس کو نافذ نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ یہ فیصلہ ایسا قول ہے جس پر کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے۔ اور جس فیصلہ پر دلیل شرعی موجود نہ ہو وہ قابل تنفیذ نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے یہ فیصلہ بھی قابل تنفیذ نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ جامع صغیر میں یہ مسئلہ اس طرح مذکور ہے کہ اگر کسی مسئلہ میں فقہا کا اختلاف ہو اور ایک قاضی نے اس میں لم دیا پھر دوسرا قاضی آیا جس کی رائے اس کے خلاف ہے تو دوسرا قاضی اسی فیصلہ کو نافذ کرے گا جو فیصلہ قاضی اول نے دیا ہے بشرطیکہ قاضی اول کا دیا ہوا فیصلہ کتاب یا حدیث یا اجماع کے خلاف نہ ہو۔ سوال : یہاں ایک سوال ہو سکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ جب جامع صغیر کی عبارت میں وہی مسئلہ مذکور ہے جو مسئلہ قدوری کی عبارت میں ذکر کیا گیا ہے تو قدوری کی عبارت کے مذکور ہونے کے بعد جامع صغیر کی عبارت ذکر کرنے کی کیا ضرورت تھی؟ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جامع صغیر کی عبارت میں ایسے دو فائدے مذکور ہیں جن سے قدوری کی عبارت خالی ہے۔ پہلا فائدہ تو یہ ہے کہ جامع صغیر کی عبارت میں فقہا کی قید سے اس طرف اشارہ ہے کہ اگر قاضی اول موضع اجتہاد سے واقف نہ ہو۔ بلکہ اُس کا فیصلہ اتفاقاً موضع اجتہاد کے موافق ہو گیا یعنی کسی فقیہ کے قول کے موافق ہو گیا تو عامۃ المشائخ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ قاضی اعلیٰ جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے اس پر اس فیصلہ کا نافذ کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر قاضی اول موضع اجتہاد سے واقف ہو یعنی اختلاف فقہا کا علم رکھتے ہوئے کسی فقیہ کے قول کے موافق فیصلہ دیا تو قاضی اعلیٰ پر اس کا نافذ کرنا واجب ہوگا ۔ اگر چہ یہ فیصلہ قاضی اعلیٰ کی رائے کے خلاف ہی کیوں نہ ہو دوسرا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ جامع صغیر کی عبارت " مری غیر ذلک اس طرف مشیر ہے کہ قاضی اول کا دیا ہوا فیصلہ اگر کتاب یا سنت یا اجماع کے خلاف نہ ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ جس کی عدالت میں مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے وہ اُسی کو نافذ کرے گا خواہ وہ فیصلہ قاضی اعلیٰ کی رائے کے مخالف ہو یا موافق ہو کیونکہ جس صورت میں قاضی اول کا دیا ہو فیصلہ، قاضی اعلیٰ کی رائے کے خلاف ہے۔ جب اُس صورت میں اُس کو نافذ کرنا ضروری ہے تو جس صورت میں قاضی اول کا فیصلہ قاضی اعلیٰ کی رائے کے موافق ہوگا۔ اُس صورت میں اس کو نافذ کرنا بدرجہ اولیٰ ضروری ہوگا۔ ملاحظہ فرمائیے مذکورہ جن فائدوں کی طرف جامع صغیر کی عبارت میں اشارہ کیا گیا ہے قدوری کی عبارت ان دو فائدوں سے ساکت ہے پس انھیں دو فائدوں کی وجہ سے قدوری کی عبارت کے بعد جامع صغیر کی عبارت کا ذکر کرنا ضروری سمجھا گیا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ قاضی اول کا فیصلہ اگر کتاب یا سنت یا اجماع کے خلاف نہ ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ کے اس فیصلے کو نافذ کرنے اور نہ کرنے کے سلسلہ میں قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی مختلف فیہ مسئلہ میں قاضی نے کوئی حکم دیا ہو تو وہ نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ قاضی اعلی (جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے ) اس کو رد کرنے یا باطل کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ قاضی اعلیٰ کا اجتہاد قاضی اول کے اجتہاد کے مانند ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح قاضی اول کے اجتہاد میں خطاء کا احتمال ہے یا اسی طرح قاضی اعلیٰ کے اجتہاد میں بھی خطاء کا احتمال ہے۔ کیونکہ کوئی مجہتد حتمی طور پر اپنے اجتہاد کو درست اور دوسرے کے اجتہاد کو غلط نہیں کہہ سکتا۔ پس اس اعتبار سے دونوں قاضیوں کے اجتہاد برابر ہیں۔ لیکن قاضی اول کے اجتہاد کے ساتھ چونکہ حکم قضاء لاحق ہو گیا ہے اور قاضی اعلیٰ کے اجتہاد کے ساتھ حکم قضاء لاحق نہیں ہوا۔ اس لئے قاضی اوّل کا اجتہاد اعلیٰ اور اقویٰ درجہ کا ہوا۔ اور قاضی دوم جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے اس کا اجتہاد ادنی درجہ کا ہوا اور یہ امر مسلم ہے کہ اعلیٰ کو ادنی کی وجہ سے رد نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ اس لئے قاضی اعلیٰ پر قاضی اول کا فیصلہ نافذ کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ اور قاضی اعلیٰ قاضی اول کے فیصلہ کو توڑنے اور زد کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ علامہ بدرالدین مینی صاحب بنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ حضرت عمر کے عمل سے بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ اگر کوئی مسئلہ مجتہد فیہ ہو اور کسی قاضی نے فقیہ کے اجتہاد کے موافق فیصلہ دیدیا ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے وہ اس فیصلہ کو نافذ کرے گا۔ اس کو رد کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ چنانچہ مروی ہے کہ امیر المومنین حضرت عمرؓ جب خلافت کے امور میں زیادہ مصروف ہو گئے تو آپ نے حضرت ابوالدردار کو قاضی مقرر کر دیا۔ حضرت ابوالدرداء کی عدالت میں ایک مقدمہ پیش ہوا آپ نے فریقین میں سے ایک کے حق میں فیصلہ کر دیا۔ پھر حضرت عمر کی اس شخص سے ملاقات ہوئی جس کے خلاف حضرت ابوالدردا نے فیصلہ دیا تھا۔ حضرت عمر نے اس کا حال دریافت کیا۔ اس نے کہا ابو الدردانے میرے خلاف فیصلہ کیا ہے۔ حضرت عمرؓ نے فرمایا لو كنت مكانه لقضیت لک ۔ اگر میں اس کی جگہ ہوتا تو میں تیرے حق میں فیصلہ دیتا۔ اس نے کہا آپ کو فیصلہ دینے سے کیا چیز مانع ہے؟ یعنی آپ ابوالد روا کا فیصلہ تو ڑ کر دوسرا فیصلہ دیجئے ؟ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا ليس هنا نص والرای مشترک یعنی اس مسئلہ میں کوئی نص موجود نہیں ہے اور رائے مشترک ہے یعنی جب کوئی نص موجود نہ ہو تو تمام مجتہدین کی رائے برابر ہے۔ قاضی جس مجتہد کی رائے کے موافق فیصلہ دے گا اس کا نفاذ ضروری ہوگا۔ قاضی اعلیٰ اس کو رد کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا ۔ ملاحظہ فرمائیے امیر المؤمنین نے اپنے ماتحت قاضی حضرت ابوالد روا کے دیئے ہوئے فیصلہ کے خلاف فیصلہ دینے سے کس طرح گریز کیا ہے۔ اسی طرح کا ایک واقعہ اس وقت پیش آیا جب فاروق اعظم نے زید بن ثابت کو قاضی مقرر کیا تھا۔ اور یہ بھی مروی ہے کہ ایک مرتبہ پیش آمدہ حادثہ میں حضرت عمر نے ایک فیصلہ دیا پھر اسی جیسے حادثہ میں اس کے برخلاف فیصلہ دیا تو حضرت عمر سے اس بارے میں لوگوں نے عرض کیا کہ پہلے آپ نے کچھ فیصلہ دیا تھا اور اب اس کے خلاف فیصلہ فرما رہے ہیں؟ یہ سن کر حضرت عمرؓ نے فرمایا تلک کما قضيناه و هذه كما نقضى ۔ یعنی وہ تو اُسی طرح ہے جس طرح ہم نے فیصلہ دیا تھا اور یہ اسی طرح ہے جس طرح ہم فیصلہ دے رہے ہیں۔ مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ بھی درست ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ مسئلہ منصوص نہیں ہے بلکہ مجتہد فیہ ہے۔ لہذا پہلی بار ایک مجتہد کے اجتہاد کے موافق فیصلہ دیا تھا اور دوسری بار دوسرے مجتہد کے اجتہاد کے موافق فیصلہ دیا ہے۔
The subordinate judge's judgment is a statement for which there is no evidence. (For example, the subordinate judge ruled that a debt is dropped from the debtor because of a delay of twelve years in claiming, and this is an opinion with no legal evidence.) So in these cases, the higher judge will not enforce the lower judge's decision. And according to the text ' الا ان يخالف الكتاب الخ ', the phrase 'بان يكون قولاً لا دلیل علیہ' will be the cause. And the meaning is that if the subordinate judge's judgment contradicts the Book, Hadith, or Ijma', the higher judge will not enforce it. Because this judgment is a statement with no evidence. And a judgment that has no legal evidence is not enforceable. Therefore this judgment is also unenforceable. The author of al-Hidayah said that in al-Jami' al-Saghir this issue is mentioned as: if there is a disagreement of jurists in a matter and one judge gave a verdict, then another judge came whose opinion is contrary to it, then the second judge will enforce the verdict of the first judge, provided that the verdict of the first judge does not oppose the Book, Sunnah, or Ijma'. Question: Here a question may arise: when al-Jami' al-Saghir mentions the same issue as Quduri's text, why was it necessary to mention al-Jami' al-Saghir after Quduri's text? Answer: The answer is that al-Jami' al-Saghir's text contains two benefits which Quduri's text lacks. The first benefit is that in al-Jami' al-Saghir's text, the phrase 'فقہا' indicates that if the first judge was not aware of the domain of ijtihad, but his verdict coincidentally agreed with a jurist's opinion, then the majority of the mashayikh hold that the higher judge to whom the case is referred is not obliged to enforce it. But if the first judge was aware of the domain of ijtihad, i.e., knowing the disagreement of jurists, he gave a verdict according to a jurist's opinion, then the higher judge must enforce it, even if that verdict is against the higher judge's own opinion. The second benefit is that al-Jami' al-Saghir's phrase 'میری غیر ذلک' indicates that if the first judge's verdict is not against the Book, Sunnah, or Ijma', then the higher judge in whose court the appeal is made will enforce it, whether the verdict is contrary to or in agreement with the higher judge's opinion. Because when enforcement is necessary in the case where the verdict opposes the higher judge's opinion, then in the case where it agrees, enforcement is even more necessary. Note that these two benefits are alluded to in al-Jami' al-Saghir, while Quduri's text is silent on them. Therefore, it was deemed necessary to mention al-Jami' al-Saghir after Quduri's text for these two benefits. The author of al-Hidayah said: Regarding enforcement or non-enforcement by the higher judge of the first judge's verdict when it does not oppose the Book, Sunnah, or Ijma', the general rule is that if a judge gave a ruling in a matter of disagreement (mukhtalaf fih), it will be enforced. The higher judge (to whom the case is appealed) is not authorized to reject or nullify it. Because the ijtihad of the higher judge is like the ijtihad of the first judge. That is, just as the ijtihad of the first judge is susceptible to error, so also the ijtihad of the higher judge is susceptible to error. No mujtahid can definitively assert that his ijtihad is correct and another's is wrong. So in this respect, the ijtihads of both judges are equal. But since the first judge's ijtihad has been accompanied by a judicial ruling, while the higher judge's ijtihad has not, the first judge's ijtihad is of a higher and stronger degree, and the second judge's ijtihad is of a lower degree. It is accepted that the higher cannot be nullified by the lower. Therefore, it is obligatory for the higher judge to enforce the first judge's verdict, and he is not authorized to break or revoke the first judge's verdict. Allamah Badr al-Din al-'Ayni, author of al-Binayah, wrote that the practice of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) also proves that if a matter is subject to ijtihad and a judge gave a verdict according to a jurist's ijtihad, then the higher judge to whom the case is appealed will enforce it and not be authorized to reject it. For it is narrated that when Amir al-Mu'minin Umar became very busy with affairs of the caliphate, he appointed Abu al-Darda' as judge. A case came before Abu al-Darda', and he decided in favor of one of the two parties. Then Umar met the man against whom Abu al-Darda' had ruled. Umar asked about his situation. He said, 'Abu al-Darda' ruled against me.' Umar replied, 'If I were in his place, I would have ruled in your favor.' The man said, 'What prevents you from giving a verdict?' i.e., overturn Abu al-Darda's verdict and give another? Umar said, 'There is no text here, and opinion is shared.' That is, there is no text in this matter, and all mujtahids' opinions are equal. The judge will enforce the verdict in accordance with whichever mujtahid's opinion he follows, and the higher judge is not authorized to reject it. Note how Amir al-Mu'minin refrained from giving a verdict contrary to that of his subordinate judge Abu al-Darda'. A similar incident occurred when Umar appointed Zayd ibn Thabit as judge. It is also narrated that once, in an incident, Umar gave one verdict, and later in a similar incident he gave the opposite verdict. People asked him, 'Previously you gave such a verdict, and now you are giving the opposite?' Umar replied, 'That is as we ruled, and this is as we rule.' Meaning, that was correct because it was not a text-based matter but a matter of ijtihad. So the first time he ruled according to one mujtahid's ijtihad, and the second time according to another mujtahid's ijtihad.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah on Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi of al-Hidayah. It addresses when a higher judge (qadi a'la) must enforce the judgment of a subordinate judge. The commentary first clarifies the condition from the Hidayah: if the subordinate judge's judgment is a mere opinion without legal evidence, the higher judge should not enforce it. The example given is a ruling that drops a debt due to delay, which lacks support from the Shari'ah. This leads to the general rule that any judgment contradicting the Qur'an, Sunnah, or Ijma' is void and must not be implemented. The commentary then references al-Jami' al-Saghir, which states the opposite case: if jurists differ on a matter and a judge rules according to one view, a subsequent judge must enforce it as long as it does not violate the primary texts. The author explains why al-Jami' al-Saghir is cited after al-Quduri, highlighting two additional benefits: first, it emphasizes the condition that the first judge must be aware of the scope of ijtihad (maudi' al-ijtihad) for his ruling to be binding; if he rules accidentally in agreement with a jurist without knowledge, the majority of scholars say the higher judge is not obligated to enforce it. Second, it clarifies that the higher judge must enforce the ruling regardless of whether it agrees with his own opinion, as long as it doesn't conflict with clear texts. The commentary then establishes the general principle: in a matter subject to ijtihad (mukhtalaf fih), the ruling of the first judge is binding because his ijtihad has been actualized in a verdict, whereas the higher judge's ijtihad is merely potential. Thus, the higher judge cannot overturn it. This is supported by the practice of Caliph Umar, who refused to overturn a judgment of Abu al-Darda' in an ijtihad matter, stating 'There is no text here, and opinion is shared.' This principle demonstrates that in matters of ijtihad, the ruling of a qualified judge is final and cannot be reversed by a higher authority simply because of a difference in ijtihad.

Key Terms
قاضی اعلیٰ (qadi a'la): The superior or higher judge who hears appeals from subordinate judges.
ماتحت قاضی (ma taht al-qadi): The subordinate judge whose decisions are subject to review by a higher judge.
موضع اجتہاد (maudi' al-ijtihad): Domain of ijtihad; matters where there is room for independent reasoning due to absence of clear text.
مجتہد فیہ (mujtahad fih): A matter in which ijtihad is permissible, i.e., not definitively settled by a clear text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition must the higher judge enforce the subordinate judge's judgment?
A) If the higher judge agrees with the judgment.
B) If the judgment is in a matter of ijtihad and does not contradict the Qur'an, Sunnah, or Ijma'.
C) If the subordinate judge was aware of the domain of ijtihad.
D) If the judgment is based on the higher judge's own opinion.

Key Takeaway
A higher judge must enforce a subordinate's judgment in matters of ijtihad, even if he disagrees, because the ijtihad of the first judge is actualized in a ruling and cannot be overturned by a potential ijtihad.

Judge Ruling Contrary to His Own Madhhab in Ijtihad Matters
Intra-Hanafi dispute on judge's ruling contrary to madhhab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the enforceability of a judge's ruling that contradicts his own madhhab in ijtihad matters, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A judge's judgment opposing his own madhhab is not enforceable, even if forgetful, according to the school's fatwa.

This lesson examines a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of a qadi's ruling when he inadvertently or deliberately departs from his own school in a matter open to ijtihad. You will analyze the reasoning behind each view and learn the operative fatwa position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Understand the core question: Is a judge's judgment enforceable when he rules contrary to his own madhhab in an ijtihad matter?
The ruling involves a scenario where the judge's own school has a clear view, but he applies a different school's view.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa distinguishes: if the judge forgot his madhhab (nasiyan), the judgment is enforceable; if deliberate (amidan), there are two narrations (one enforcing, one not).
His reasoning: the error is not certain (laysa bi khata'in bi yaqin).
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the judgment is not enforceable in either case—whether forgetful or deliberate.
Their reasoning: the judge ruled according to what he himself considers an error (qada bima huwa khata'un 'indahu).
4
Compare the reasoning
Contrast the epistemic basis: Abu Hanifa focuses on the objective uncertainty of error; the Sahibayn focus on the judge's subjective certainty of error.
This difference in perspective leads to different rulings.
5
Identify the tarjih
The text states 'alayhi al-fatwa', meaning the fatwa is with the Sahibayn. Thus, the operative ruling is that the judgment is not enforceable.
This is the mufta bihi position for Hanafi fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خادم نے بعض اساتذہ سے سنا ہے کہ اگر کسی مسئلہ میں ائمہ فقہ کا اختلاف ہو تو مفتی ، امت کی سہولت کے لئے جس امام کے قول پر بھی فتوی دے گا درست اور جائز ہوگا۔ قاضی نے مجتہد فیہ مسئلہ میں بھول کر دوسرے مذہب پر فیصلہ صادر کر دیا تو نافذ ہوگا یا نہیں ولو قضى فى المجتهد فيه مخالفاً لرأيه ناسياً لمذهبه نفذ عند ابي حنيفة وان كان عامدا ففيه روايتان ووجه النفاذ انه ليس بخطاً بيقين وعندهما لا ينفذ في الوجهين لانه قضى بما هو خطأ عنده وعليه الفتوى ثم
The servant heard from some teachers that if there is disagreement among the imams of fiqh in a matter, the mufti, for the convenience of the community, can give a fatwa according to any imam's opinion, and it will be valid and permissible. If a judge, in a matter subject to ijtihad, mistakenly ruled contrary to his own madhhab, is it enforced? And if he ruled in a matter of ijtihad contrary to his own opinion, having forgotten his madhhab, it is enforced according to Abu Hanifa. If he was deliberate, there are two narrations. And the justification for enforcement is that it is not definitely an error. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not enforced in both cases because he ruled according to what is, in his view, an error. And the fatwa is on their statement. Then
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage, likely a marginal note or addition by the author of Ashraf al-Hidayah, first mentions a general rule about muftis: in cases where the imams differ, a mufti may choose any opinion for the convenience of the ummah. This is a preliminary point. The main issue is the effect of a judge's ruling in a matter of ijtihad when he goes against his own madhhab. The text presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa holds that if the judge forgets his madhhab and rules according to another view, the judgment is enforceable (nafidh). The reason is that his error is not certain (laysa bi khata'in bi yaqin). If the judge deliberately rules contrary to his madhhab, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa – one supporting enforcement, the other rejecting it. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that in both cases (forgetful or deliberate), the judgment is not enforceable. Their reasoning is that the judge knowingly ruled according to what he himself considers an error (huwa khata'un 'indahu). The fatwa (the relied-upon position) is with the Sahibayn, meaning the judgment is not enforceable if the judge rules contrary to his own madhhab, whether by mistake or intentionally. The word 'thumma' at the end indicates continuation, but the passage ends here in the window.

Key Terms
مجتہد فیہ (mujtahad fih): A matter open to ijtihad, not determined by a definitive text.
ناسیاً (nasiyan): Forgetfully; unintentionally, due to forgetfulness.
عامداً (amidan): Deliberately; intentionally, with knowledge.
روایتان (riwayatan): Two narrations (transmissions) from the imam, indicating a difference of opinion.
علیہ الفتوی (alayhi al-fatwa): The relied-upon position for giving fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) regarding a judge who rules contrary to his own madhhab in a matter of ijtihad?
A) It is enforceable if the judge forgets his madhhab.
B) It is not enforceable in both cases (forgetful or deliberate).
C) It is enforceable if the judge acts deliberately.
D) It is enforceable only if the judgment is in accordance with the higher judge's opinion.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a judge's ruling that contradicts his own madhhab in ijtihad matters is not enforceable, even if he forgot his madhhab.
