Enforceability of a Judge's Verdict Against His Own Ijtihad
Explains the ruling when a judge rules against his own opinion in a matter of ijtihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the enforceability of a judge's verdict in a mujtahad fih matter when it contradicts his own ijtihad, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A judge's verdict against his own ijtihad in a matter of legitimate disagreement is enforceable if forgetful, but the relied-upon fatwa forbids it in all cases.

This passage from Kitab Adab al-Qadi addresses a delicate question: what happens when a judge renders a verdict that goes against his own personal opinion or madhhab in a case where multiple valid opinions exist? This is a matter of ijtihad, and the Hanafi school has nuanced views, supported by the practice of Umar (RA). In this lesson, we will dissect the ruling, the proofs, and the internal debate within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Determine what the passage is about: a judge's verdict in a matter subject to legitimate ijtihad (mujtahad fih) that is contrary to his own opinion or madhhab.
2
Distinguish forgetful vs. intentional
Note that the ruling depends on whether the judge acted forgetfully (nasian) or intentionally (amidan). Abu Hanifa differentiates; the Sahibayn do not.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and rationale
Abu Hanifa holds that if forgetful, the verdict is enforced because it is not definitively wrong. If intentional, there are two narrations.
The rationale: the verdict falls within the scope of valid ijtihad.
4
State the Sahibayn's position and rationale
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the verdict is not enforced in either case because the judge himself believes it is wrong.
Analogized to a person praying opposite his own qibla ijtihad.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon fatwa position is that of the Sahibayn, supported by later authorities like Ibn al-Humam, and it aligns with the other three Sunni schools.
The text states 'وعليه الفتوى' (upon this is the fatwa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الادب القاضي

یعنی جس طرح قاضی اول کے اجتہاد میں خطاء کا احتمال ہے یا اسی طرح قاضی اعلیٰ کے اجتہاد میں بھی خطاء کا احتمال ہے۔ کیونکہ کوئی مجہتد حتمی طور پر اپنے اجتہاد کو درست اور دوسرے کے اجتہاد کو غلط نہیں کہہ سکتا۔ پس اس اعتبار سے دونوں قاضیوں کے اجتہاد برابر ہیں۔ لیکن قاضی اول کے اجتہاد کے ساتھ چونکہ حکم قضاء لاحق ہو گیا ہے اور قاضی اعلیٰ کے اجتہاد کے ساتھ حکم قضاء لاحق نہیں ہوا۔ اس لئے قاضی اوّل کا اجتہاد اعلیٰ اور اقویٰ درجہ کا ہوا۔ اور قاضی دوم جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے اس کا اجتہاد ادنی درجہ کا ہوا اور یہ امر مسلم ہے کہ اعلیٰ کو ادنی کی وجہ سے رد نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ اس لئے قاضی اعلیٰ پر قاضی اول کا فیصلہ نافذ کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ اور قاضی اعلیٰ قاضی اول کے فیصلہ کو توڑنے اور زد کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ علامہ بدرالدین مینی صاحب بنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ حضرت عمر کے عمل سے بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ اگر کوئی مسئلہ مجتہد فیہ ہو اور کسی قاضی نے فقیہ کے اجتہاد کے موافق فیصلہ دیدیا ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے وہ اس فیصلہ کو نافذ کرے گا۔ اس کو رد کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ چنانچہ مروی ہے کہ امیر المومنین حضرت عمرؓ جب خلافت کے امور میں زیادہ مصروف ہو گئے تو آپ نے حضرت ابوالدردار کو قاضی مقرر کر دیا۔ حضرت ابوالدرداء کی عدالت میں ایک مقدمہ پیش ہوا آپ نے فریقین میں سے ایک کے حق میں فیصلہ کر دیا۔ پھر حضرت عمر کی اس شخص سے ملاقات ہوئی جس کے خلاف حضرت ابوالدردا نے فیصلہ دیا تھا۔ حضرت عمر نے اس کا حال دریافت کیا۔ اس نے کہا ابو الدردانے میرے خلاف فیصلہ کیا ہے۔ حضرت عمرؓ نے فرمایا لو كنت مكانه لقضیت لک ۔ اگر میں اس کی جگہ ہوتا تو میں تیرے حق میں فیصلہ دیتا۔ اس نے کہا آپ کو فیصلہ دینے سے کیا چیز مانع ہے؟ یعنی آپ ابوالد روا کا فیصلہ تو ڑ کر دوسرا فیصلہ دیجئے ؟ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا ليس هنا نص والرای مشترک یعنی اس مسئلہ میں کوئی نص موجود نہیں ہے اور رائے مشترک ہے یعنی جب کوئی نص موجود نہ ہو تو تمام مجتہدین کی رائے برابر ہے۔ قاضی جس مجتہد کی رائے کے موافق فیصلہ دے گا اس کا نفاذ ضروری ہوگا۔ قاضی اعلیٰ اس کو رد کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا ۔ ملاحظہ فرمائیے امیر المؤمنین نے اپنے ماتحت قاضی حضرت ابوالد روا کے دیئے ہوئے فیصلہ کے خلاف فیصلہ دینے سے کس طرح گریز کیا ہے۔ اسی طرح کا ایک واقعہ اس وقت پیش آیا جب فاروق اعظم نے زید بن ثابت کو قاضی مقرر کیا تھا۔ اور یہ بھی مروی ہے کہ ایک مرتبہ پیش آمدہ حادثہ میں حضرت عمر نے ایک فیصلہ دیا پھر اسی جیسے حادثہ میں اس کے برخلاف فیصلہ دیا تو حضرت عمر سے اس بارے میں لوگوں نے عرض کیا کہ پہلے آپ نے کچھ فیصلہ دیا تھا اور اب اس کے خلاف فیصلہ فرما رہے ہیں؟ یہ سن کر حضرت عمرؓ نے فرمایا تلک کما قضيناه و هذه كما نقضى ۔ یعنی وہ تو اُسی طرح ہے جس طرح ہم نے فیصلہ دیا تھا اور یہ اسی طرح ہے جس طرح ہم فیصلہ دے رہے ہیں۔ مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ بھی درست ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ مسئلہ منصوص نہیں ہے بلکہ مجتہد فیہ ہے۔ لہذا پہلی بار ایک مجتہد کے اجتہاد کے موافق فیصلہ دیا تھا اور دوسری بار دوسرے مجتہد کے اجتہاد کے موافق فیصلہ دیا ہے۔ خادم نے بعض اساتذہ سے سُنا ہے کہ اگر کسی مسئلہ میں ائمہ فقہ کا اختلاف ہو تو مفتی ، امت کی سہولت کے لئے جس امام کے قول پر بھی فتوی دے گا درست اور جائز ہوگا۔ قاضی نے مجتہد فیہ مسئلہ میں بھول کر دوسرے مذہب پر فیصلہ صادر کر دیا تو نافذ ہوگا یا نہیں

ولو قضى فى المجتهد فيه مخالفاً لرأيه ناسياً لمذهبه نفذ عند ابي حنيفة وان كان عامدا ففيه روايتان ووجه النفاذ انه ليس بخطاً بيقين وعندهما لا ينفذ في الوجهين لانه قضى بما هو خطأ عنده وعليه الفتوى ثم

المجتهد فيه ان لايكون مخالفا لما ذكرنا و المراد بالسنة المشهورة منها و فيما اجتمع عليه الجمهور لا يعتبر مخالفة البعض و ذلك خلاف وليس باختلاف والمعتبر الاختلاف في الصدر الاول

ترجمہ اور قاضی نے کسی مجتہد فیہ مسئلہ میں اپنی رائے کے خلاف اپنا مذہب بھول کر فیصلہ دیدیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کو نافذ کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر عمداً ایسا کیا تو اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔ اور نافذ ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ حکم یقینی طور پر خطا نہیں ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں نافذ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس نے ایسی چیز کے ساتھ فیصلہ دیا ہے جو اس کے نزدیک خطا ہے اور اسی پر فتویٰ ہے۔ پھر مجتہد فیہ وہ ہے جو مذکورہ بالا کے خلاف نہ ہو ۔ اور سنت سے مراد وہ سنت ہے جو مشہور ہو ۔ اور جس امر پر جمہور نے اتفاق کیا ہو اس میں بعض کی مخالفت معتبر نہ ہو گی۔ اور یہ خلاف ہے اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ اور صدر اول کا اختلاف معتبر ہے۔

تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر کسی مجتہد فیہ مسئلہ میں قاضی نے اپنا مذ ہب بھول کر اپنی رائے کے خلاف حکم دیدیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک قاضی کا یہ حکم نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر جان بوجھ کر ایسا کیا تو اس بارے میں حضرت امام اعظم سے دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک روایت کے مطابق اس صورت میں بھی قاضی کا حکم نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اسی روایت کے مطابق صدر الشہید اور شیخ ظهیر الدین فتوی دیتے تھے۔ اور ایک روایت میں قاضی کا یہ حکم نافذ نہ ہو گا۔ اسی روایت پر شمس الائمہ اور جندی فتوی دیتے تھے ۔ نافذ ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قاضی نے اپنے مذہب کے خلاف جو حکم دیا ہے وہ قطعی طور پر غلط نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ قاضی کی رائے اگر چہ اس کے نزد یک بظاہر صواب ہے لیکن احتمال خطا کا بھی ہے اور اس کے علاوہ کی رائے اس کے نزدیک اگر چہ غلط ہے لیکن احتمال صواب کا بھی ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ دونوں میں سے کسی کی رائے یقینی طور پر خطا نہیں ہے۔ اور جب دونوں میں سے کسی کی رائے کو یقینی طور پر نہ خطا کہا جا سکتا ہے اور نہ درست کہا جا سکتا ہے تو قاضی کا حکم مجتہد فیہ صورت میں ہوا اور مجتہد فیہ صورت میں قاضی کا حکم بہر صورت نافذ ہوتا ہے خواہ اس کے مذہب کے خلاف ہو، خواہ موافق ہو اسلئے قاضی کا مذکورہ حکم اگر چہ اس کے مذہب کے خلاف ہے، نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اور نافذ نہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جب قاضی نے عمدا اپنے مذہب کے خلاف فیصلہ دیا ہے تو گویا اس کو اپنے دیئے ہوئے فیصلہ کے غلط اور فاسد ہونے کا گمان ہے اور ہر شخص کے حق میں چونکہ اس کے گمان کے مطابق معاملہ کیا جاتا ہے اسلئے قاضی کے گمان کے مطابق اس کے فیصلہ کو فاسد قرار دیکر اس کو نافذ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ جیسے کسی شخص پر قبلہ مشتبہ ہو گیا اور اس کی تحری کسی ایک جہت کی طرف واقع ہوئی مگر اس نے اس کے خلاف دوسری جہت کی طرف منہ کر کے نماز ادا کی تو اس کی نماز درست نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اسکے اعتقاد میں یہ جہت غلط ہے پس اسی طرح یہاں بھی قاضی کا فیصلہ جو اس کے مذہب کے خلاف ہے۔ اس کے اعتقاد میں غلط ہونے کی وجہ سے نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ قاضی اپنے مذہب کے خلاف بھول کر فیصلہ دے یا جان کر فیصلہ دے دونوں صورتوں میں اُس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہو گا۔ یہی مذہب امام مالک، امام شافعی اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ اور بقول علامہ ابن الہمام کا فتوی بھی اسی پر ہے۔ کیونکہ قاضی نے جو فیصلہ دیا ہے وہ اس کے نزدیک غلط اور خطا ہے اور آدمی سے چونکہ اس کے گمان کے مطابق معاملہ کیا جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے گمان کے مطابق اس کا یہ فیصلہ غلط اور خطا ہوگا اور غلط فیصلہ چونکہ نا قابل تنفیذ ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس فیصلہ کو نافذ کیا جائے گا۔
Book of the Etiquette of the Judge. Meaning: Just as there is a possibility of error in the first judge's ijtihad, similarly there is a possibility of error in the higher judge's ijtihad. Because no mujtahid can definitively say that his ijtihad is correct and another's is wrong. So in this respect, the ijtihad of both judges is equal. However, since a judicial verdict has been attached to the first judge's ijtihad and not to the higher judge's ijtihad, the first judge's ijtihad becomes of a higher and stronger degree, and the ijtihad of the second judge to whom the case was appealed becomes of a lower degree. It is an established matter that the higher cannot be rejected by the lower. Therefore, it is obligatory for the higher judge to enforce the first judge's verdict, and the higher judge is not permitted to break or invalidate the first judge's verdict. Allamah Badr al-Din al-Maini, author of al-Binayah, wrote that the practice of Umar (RA) also proves that if a matter is mujtahad fih and a judge gave a verdict according to the ijtihad of a jurist, the higher judge to whom the case is appealed will enforce that verdict; he is not permitted to reject it. Thus, it is narrated that when the Commander of the Faithful, Umar (RA), became very busy with caliphal affairs, he appointed Abu al-Darda' as judge. A case was presented in Abu al-Darda''s court, and he gave a verdict in favor of one of the parties. Then Umar met the person against whom Abu al-Darda' had given the verdict. Umar asked him about his situation. He said: 'Abu al-Darda' gave a verdict against me.' Umar (RA) said: 'If I were in his place, I would have given the verdict in your favor.' He said: 'What prevents you from giving a verdict?' i.e., break Abu al-Darda''s verdict and give another verdict. Umar said: 'There is no text here, and opinion is shared,' meaning there is no text in this matter, and when there is no text, the opinions of all mujtahids are equal. Whichever mujtahid's opinion the judge follows in his verdict, its enforcement is necessary; the higher judge is not permitted to reject it. Observe how the Commander of the Faithful refrained from giving a verdict against the verdict given by his subordinate judge, Abu al-Darda'. A similar incident occurred when Umar appointed Zayd ibn Thabit as judge. It is also narrated that once in an incident, Umar gave a verdict, then in a similar incident he gave a contrary verdict. People asked him: 'You gave a verdict before, and now you give a contrary verdict?' Hearing this, Umar (RA) said: 'That is as we judged it, and this is as we judge.' The meaning is that that too is correct, because this matter is not textual but is mujtahad fih. So the first time he gave a verdict according to the ijtihad of one mujtahid, and the second time according to the ijtihad of another mujtahid. The servant heard from some teachers that if there is a difference among the imams of fiqh on a matter, the mufti, for the convenience of the ummah, may give a fatwa according to any imam's opinion, and it will be correct and permissible. If a judge, in a mujtahad fih matter, forgetfully gave a verdict according to another madhhab contrary to his own opinion, will it be enforced? The text: 'And if he judges in a matter of ijtihad contrary to his own opinion, forgetful of his madhhab, it is enforced according to Abu Hanifah. And if he did so intentionally, there are two narrations. The reason for enforcement is that it is not definitely wrong. According to them (the Sahibayn), it is not enforced in both cases because he judged by something that is wrong in his view, and upon this is the fatwa. Then: A matter of ijtihad is that which is not contrary to what we have mentioned. The intended meaning of Sunnah is the well-known one. In what the majority have agreed upon, the opposition of some is not considered. That is khilaf, not ikhtilaf. What is considered is the ikhtilaf of the early generation.' Translation: If a judge, in a matter of ijtihad, gave a verdict contrary to his own opinion, forgetful of his madhhab, then according to Imam Abu Hanifah, his verdict will be enforced. And if he did so intentionally, there are two narrations on this. The reason for enforcement is that this ruling is not definitely wrong. According to the Sahibayn, it is not enforced in either case, because he gave a verdict with something that is wrong in his view, and upon this is the fatwa. Then a matter of ijtihad is that which is not contrary to what was mentioned. The intended meaning of Sunnah is the well-known one. In what the majority have agreed upon, the opposition of some is not considered. That is khilaf, not ikhtilaf. What is considered is the ikhtilaf of the early generation. Commentary: The author of al-Quduri said: If in a matter of ijtihad, a judge forgetfully gave a ruling contrary to his madhhab and against his own opinion, then according to Imam Abu Hanifah, this ruling will be enforced. And if he did so intentionally, there are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifah. According to one narration, even in this case the judge's ruling will be enforced; and according to this narration, Sadr al-Shahid and Shaykh Zahir al-Din gave fatwa. According to another narration, the judge's ruling will not be enforced; and according to this narration, Shams al-Aimmah and al-Jundi gave fatwa. The reason for enforcement is that the ruling he gave contrary to his madhhab is not absolutely wrong. Because the judge's opinion, though apparently correct in his view, has a possibility of error; and the other opinion, though wrong in his view, has a possibility of correctness. So it becomes clear that neither of the two opinions is definitively wrong. And when neither opinion can be definitively called wrong nor definitively correct, the judge's ruling was in a mujtahad fih situation, and in a mujtahad fih situation, the judge's ruling is enforced in all cases, whether it is contrary to his madhhab or in agreement. Therefore, the aforementioned ruling of the judge, even if it is contrary to his madhhab, will be enforced. The reason for non-enforcement is that when the judge intentionally gave a verdict contrary to his madhhab, he has a suspicion that his own verdict is wrong and invalid. Since a person's actions are based on his suspicion, according to the judge's suspicion, his verdict will be deemed invalid and not enforced. For example, if a person is confused about the qibla and his ijtihad leads to one direction, but he prays facing another direction contrary to his ijtihad, his prayer is not valid. Because in his belief, that direction is wrong. Similarly, here the judge's verdict which is against his madhhab, due to being wrong in his belief, will not be enforced. The Sahibayn said: Regardless of whether the judge gives a verdict contrary to his madhhab forgetfully or intentionally, his verdict will not be enforced. This is also the madhhab of Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. According to Allamah Ibn al-Humam, the fatwa is also upon this. Because the judge gave a verdict that is wrong and erroneous in his view. Since a person is treated according to his suspicion, according to his suspicion this verdict is wrong and erroneous, and since a wrong verdict is unenforceable, therefore this verdict will not be enforced.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage from the Book of the Etiquette of the Judge (Kitab Adab al-Qadi) discusses a critical issue in Islamic judicial procedure: the validity of a judge's verdict when it contradicts his own ijtihad or madhhab in a matter subject to legitimate scholarly disagreement (mujtahad fih). The commentary begins by establishing a foundational principle: in matters of ijtihad, no mujtahid can claim absolute certainty for his opinion over another's. This equal probability means that a higher judge cannot overturn a lower judge's verdict simply because it differs from his own view. The author supports this with the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA), who refused to reverse Abu al-Darda''s verdict, stating 'There is no text here, and opinion is shared.' Umar's statement is a direct proof that in the absence of a definitive textual ruling, all valid ijtihad is equally legitimate, and once a verdict is rendered, it becomes binding and cannot be retracted simply because another mujtahid holds a different view. The passage then presents the core legal question: if a judge (qadi) renders a verdict in a mujtahad fih matter that is contrary to his own opinion or madhhab, is that verdict enforceable? The answer differs by circumstance and among Hanafi authorities. According to Imam Abu Hanifah, if the judge was forgetful (nasiyan) of his own madhhab when he issued the verdict, the verdict is enforced. The rationale is that the verdict is not definitively wrong; it falls within the range of valid ijtihad. If the judge acted intentionally (amid), there are two narrations from Abu Hanifah: one narration holds the verdict enforceable, another says it is not. The reason for non-enforcement in the intentional case is that the judge's own conviction is that the verdict is wrong; a person's actions are judged by his intent and belief, so the verdict is considered invalid in his own eyes and thus unenforceable. This is analogized to a person who, after performing ijtihad to determine the qibla, deliberately prays facing a different direction; the prayer is invalid because he acted against his own ijtihad. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that in both forgetful and intentional cases, the verdict is not enforced. Their view is that since the verdict is wrong in the judge's own estimation, it cannot be considered a valid judgment. This is the position adopted by the majority of later Hanafi scholars (mufta bihi), and it aligns with the views of Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. The passage then defines what constitutes a 'mujtahad fih' matter: it is an issue not directly covered by a clear, well-known Sunnah (sunnah mashhurah) or consensus of the majority (ijma' al-jumhur). Matters of khilaf (mere opposition) are not considered true ikhtilaf; only the differences of the early generations (sadr al-awwal) are considered legitimate grounds for ijtihad. In summary, the passage teaches that while judicial rulings based on ijtihad are generally binding and should be respected by higher courts, a judge's own ruling contrary to his personal conviction may not stand if it contradicts his own ijtihad, especially if done intentionally. The Hanafi school has internal differences, with the preferred position being that of the Sahibayn: the verdict is not enforceable.

Key Terms
مُجْتَهَد فِيه (mujtahad fih): A matter in which no clear textual ruling exists from Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, and thus legitimate ijtihad is allowed. The passage specifies it excludes matters established by well-known Sunnah or majority consensus.
خِلاف (khilaf): Opposition to a matter agreed upon by the majority; this is not considered legitimate ikhtilaf and is not a basis for ijtihad.
اخْتِلاف (ikhtilaf): Legitimate difference of opinion among qualified scholars of the early generation (sadr al-awwal) that forms the basis of ijtihad in mujtahad fih matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a judge intentionally gives a verdict in a mujtahad fih matter contrary to his own ijtihad?
A) Enforceable in all cases.
B) Not enforceable.
C) Enforceable only if the judge was forgetful.
D) Enforceable but the judge is sinful.

Key Takeaway
In matters of ijtihad, a judge's verdict contrary to his own conviction is not enforceable according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, reflecting the principle that judicial rulings are judged by the judge's own ijtihad.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Qadi's Verdict Against His Own Madhhab in Mujtahad Fih
Hanafi ruling with proof and intra-madhhab dispute on qadi's verdict enforcement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the enforceability of a qadi's verdict when he rules against his own madhhab in a mujtahad fih matter and identify the mufta bihi position with its reasoning.

Core Idea
A judge's verdict against his own madhhab in a mujtahad fih issue may be valid but is not enforced according to the relied-upon position.

The Islamic judiciary requires a qadi to adjudicate according to his own ijtihad. But what if he deliberately or forgetfully rules against his own madhhab in an issue open to ijtihad? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on the enforceability of such a verdict, exploring the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two distinguished disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The qadi rules in a mujtahad fih issue contrary to his own madhhab, either forgetfully or deliberately. Note that 'mujtahad fih' means an issue where valid ikhtilaf exists among early scholars.
The passage distinguishes between khilaf (invalid disagreement) and ikhtilaf (valid difference). Only the latter qualifies as mujtahad fih.
2
State the Positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if the qadi forgets his madhhab, the verdict is enforced. If deliberate, there are two narrations (one enforces, one does not). The Sahibayn hold that in both forgetful and deliberate cases, the verdict is not enforced.
The Sahibayn's view is also adopted by Malik, Shafi'i, and Hanbali schools.
3
Analyze the Reasoning (Talil) for Each Position
Abu Hanifa argues that in mujtahad fih matters, neither opinion is definitively correct or wrong, so the qadi's verdict is not certainly erroneous. The Sahibayn contend that the qadi's own belief considers the verdict wrong, and a person is treated according to his belief.
The Sahibayn give an analogy: a person whose ijtihad indicates one qibla but prays facing another – his prayer is invalid because he believes it wrong.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Relied-Upon Position)
Later Hanafi authorities like Allama Ibn al-Humam favour the Sahibayn's position. Thus, the fatwa is that the verdict is not enforced in either case, whether the qadi was forgetful or deliberate.
Earlier scholars like Sadr al-Shahid followed the narration that enforces even deliberate verdicts, but the later fatwa accepts the Sahibayn's view.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Practical Scenario
In a Hanafi court, if a Hanafi judge rules according to a non-Hanafi view in a mujtahad fih matter, the verdict will be overturned on appeal because the judge's own belief deems it wrong.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that litigants can challenge such verdicts successfully.

Source Text

كتاب الادب القاضي
اشرف الہدایہ جلد نہم
المجتهد فيه ان لايكون مخالفا لما ذكرنا و المراد بالسنة المشهورة منها و فيما اجتمع عليه الجمهور لا يعتبر مخالفة البعض و ذلك خلاف وليس باختلاف والمعتبر الاختلاف في الصدر الاول

ترجمہ اور قاضی نے کسی مجتہد فیہ مسئلہ میں اپنی رائے کے خلاف اپنا مذہب بھول کر فیصلہ دیدیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کو نافذ کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر عمداً ایسا کیا تو اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔ اور نافذ ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ حکم یقینی طور پر خطا نہیں ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں نافذ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس نے ایسی چیز کے ساتھ فیصلہ دیا ہے جو اس کے نزدیک خطا ہے اور اسی پر فتویٰ ہے۔

تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر کسی مجتہد فیہ مسئلہ میں قاضی نے اپنا مذ ہب بھول کر اپنی رائے کے خلاف حکم دیدیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک قاضی کا یہ حکم نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر جان بوجھ کر ایسا کیا تو اس بارے میں حضرت امام اعظم سے دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک روایت کے مطابق اس صورت میں بھی قاضی کا حکم نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اسی روایت کے مطابق صدر الشہید اور شیخ ظهیر الدین فتوی دیتے تھے۔ اور ایک روایت میں قاضی کا یہ حکم نافذ نہ ہو گا۔ اسی روایت پر شمس الائمہ اور جندی فتوی دیتے تھے ۔ نافذ ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قاضی نے اپنے مذہب کے خلاف جو حکم دیا ہے وہ قطعی طور پر غلط نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ قاضی کی رائے اگر چہ اس کے نزد یک بظاہر صواب ہے لیکن احتمال خطا کا بھی ہے اور اس کے علاوہ کی رائے اس کے نزدیک اگر چہ غلط ہے لیکن احتمال صواب کا بھی ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ دونوں میں سے کسی کی رائے یقینی طور پر خطا نہیں ہے۔ اور جب دونوں میں سے کسی کی رائے کو یقینی طور پر نہ خطا کہا جا سکتا ہے اور نہ درست کہا جا سکتا ہے تو قاضی کا حکم مجتہد فیہ صورت میں ہوا اور مجتہد فیہ صورت میں قاضی کا حکم بہر صورت نافذ ہوتا ہے خواہ اس کے مذہب کے خلاف ہو، خواہ موافق ہو اسلئے قاضی کا مذکورہ حکم اگر چہ اس کے مذہب کے خلاف ہے، نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اور نافذ نہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جب قاضی نے عمدا اپنے مذہب کے خلاف فیصلہ دیا ہے تو گویا اس کو اپنے دیئے ہوئے فیصلہ کے غلط اور فاسد ہونے کا گمان ہے اور ہر شخص کے حق میں چونکہ اس کے گمان کے مطابق معاملہ کیا جاتا ہے اسلئے قاضی کے گمان کے مطابق اس کے فیصلہ کو فاسد قرار دیکر اس کو نافذ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ جیسے کسی شخص پر قبلہ مشتبہ ہو گیا اور اس کی تحری کسی ایک جہت کی طرف واقع ہوئی مگر اس نے اس کے خلاف دوسری جہت کی طرف منہ کر کے نماز ادا کی تو اس کی نماز درست نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اسکے اعتقاد میں یہ جہت غلط ہے پس اسی طرح یہاں بھی قاضی کا فیصلہ جو اس کے مذہب کے خلاف ہے۔ اس کے اعتقاد میں غلط ہونے کی وجہ سے نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ قاضی اپنے مذہب کے خلاف بھول کر فیصلہ دے یا جان کر فیصلہ دے دونوں صورتوں میں اُس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہو گا۔ یہی مذہب امام مالک، امام شافعی اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ اور بقول علامہ ابن الہمام کا فتوی بھی اسی پر ہے۔ کیونکہ قاضی نے جو فیصلہ دیا ہے وہ اس کے نزدیک غلط اور خطا ہے اور آدمی سے چونکہ اس کے گمان کے مطابق معاملہ کیا جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے گمان کے مطابق اس کا یہ فیصلہ غلط اور خطا ہوگا اور غلط فیصلہ چونکہ نا قابل تنفیذ ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس فیصلہ کو نافذ کیا جائے گا۔
The Book of the Disciplines of the Judge. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume Nine. The mujtahad fih is that it not be contrary to what we mentioned. And what is meant by the Sunnah is the well-known one from it. And in what the majority have agreed upon, the opposition of a few is not considered. And that is khilaf, not ikhtilaf. And the ikhtilaf that is considered is from the first generation.

Translation: And if a judge in a mujtahad fih issue, having forgotten his own madhhab, gave a verdict contrary to his own opinion, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa it will be enforced. And if he did so deliberately, there are two narrations. And the reason for enforcement is that this ruling is not definitively erroneous. And according to the Sahibayn, in both cases it will not be enforced because he gave a ruling with something that is erroneous in his view, and upon this is the fatwa.

Explanation: Sahib Quduri said: If a judge in a mujtahad fih issue, having forgotten his own madhhab, gave a ruling contrary to his own opinion, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the judge's ruling will be enforced. And if he did so knowingly, there are two narrations from Imam A'zam. According to one narration, in this case too the judge's ruling will be enforced. According to this narration, Sadr al-Shahid and Sheikh Zahir al-Din used to give fatwa. And in one narration, the judge's ruling will not be enforced. According to this narration, Shams al-A'imma and al-Jandi used to give fatwa. The reason for enforcement: the judge's ruling contrary to his madhhab is not definitively wrong because the judge's opinion, though seemingly correct to him, has the possibility of error, and the other opinion, though seemingly wrong to him, has the possibility of correctness. Thus it is known that neither opinion is definitively erroneous or correct. When that is the case, the judge's ruling occurs in a mujtahad fih matter, and in a mujtahad fih matter the judge's ruling is enforced in any case, whether contrary to his madhhab or in agreement. Therefore, the aforementioned ruling, though contrary to his madhhab, will be enforced. And the reason for non-enforcement: when the judge deliberately gave a verdict contrary to his madhhab, he has a belief that his own verdict is wrong and invalid. And since every person is dealt with according to his belief, his verdict is deemed invalid according to his belief and will not be enforced. For example, if a person has doubt about the qibla and his ijtihad leads to one direction, but he prays facing another direction, his prayer is not valid because in his belief that direction is wrong. So similarly, here the judge's verdict contrary to his madhhab, due to being wrong in his belief, will not be enforced. The Sahibayn said: Whether the judge gives a verdict contrary to his madhhab by forgetfulness or knowingly, in both cases his verdict will not be enforced. This is also the madhhab of Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. And according to Allama Ibn al-Humam, the fatwa is upon this as well, because the judge's verdict is wrong and erroneous in his view, and since a person is dealt with according to his belief, his verdict will be wrong and erroneous according to his belief, and since a wrong verdict is unenforceable, this verdict will not be enforced.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling with proof and intra-madhhab dispute regarding the enforceability of a judge's verdict when he rules against his own madhhab in a mujtahad fih issue. The text begins by quoting from Quduri that if the judge forgetfully rules contrary to his own opinion, Imam Abu Hanifa says it is enforced. If deliberate, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one enforces, the other does not. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that in both cases the verdict is not enforced. The commentary explains the reasoning: For Abu Hanifa, since the matter is open to ijtihad, neither view is definitively correct or wrong; therefore the judge's ruling is valid even if contrary to his own preference. The Sahibayn argue that the judge's own belief considers the ruling wrong, and since a person is treated according to his belief (zan), the verdict is invalid. A analogy with prayer direction is given. The passage notes that Imam Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad agree with the Sahibayn. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to some is the Sahibayn's view, though earlier scholars like Sadr al-Shahid followed the enforcement narration. The key point is that in mujtahad fih matters, ijtihad error is probable, so the judge's ruling is not categorically null.

Key Terms
مجتهد فيه (mujtahad fih): A legal issue that is open to ijtihad, i.e., not settled by a definitive text or consensus, and where there is a valid difference of opinion among scholars of the first generation.
خلاف (khilaf): An opposition that is not based on valid evidence but on obstinacy or lack of evidence; not considered a legitimate difference of opinion.
اختلاف (ikhtilaf): A valid difference of opinion based on evidence, especially among the Companions and early scholars (Sadr al-Awwal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what happens if a Hanafi judge deliberately gives a verdict contrary to his own madhhab in a mujtahad fih issue?
A) The verdict is enforced because the matter is open to ijtihad.
B) The verdict is not enforced because the judge believes it is wrong.
C) The verdict is enforced only if the judge forgot his madhhab.
D) The verdict is always enforced regardless of intention.

Key Takeaway
In mujtahad fih matters, the mufta bihi Hanafi position is that a judge's verdict contrary to his own madhhab is not enforceable, because his own belief deems it erroneous.

Defining Mujtahad Fih and Valid Ikhtilaf
Defining mujtahad fih and distinguishing valid ikhtilaf from khilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mujtahad fih and distinguish valid ikhtilaf from invalid khilaf according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
An issue is mujtahad fih only if it is not settled by a decisive text and has valid ikhtilaf from the first generation.

This lesson unpacks the Hidayah's definition of mujtahad fih — a key concept for understanding the scope of judicial review and ijtihad. You will learn the criteria that make an issue open to ijtihad, and the crucial difference between ikhtilaf (valid scholarly difference) and khilaf (mere opposition). This distinction has direct consequences for the validity of judges' verdicts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sources that bar an issue from being mujtahad fih
The passage states that an issue that is clearly ruled by the Quran, well-known Sunnah, or consensus cannot be mujtahad fih. Identify each source and why it closes the door to ijtihad.
The example given is the prohibition of stepmother from Quran 4:22, which all Salaf agreed upon.
2
Define 'well-known Sunnah' (sunnah mashhurah)
The passage specifies the condition for a sunnah to be considered decisive: it must have become famous among the Companions and Followers and transmitted through a sound chain. Explain why this standard matters for nullifying a judge's verdict.
Hanafis give high authority to such sunnah, similar to mutawatir in some respects.
3
Define 'consensus' (ijma) as used here
The passage defines consensus as the agreement of the majority of early scholars (Salaf). Note that even if a few scholars disagreed, the majority view is binding; such minority opposition is considered khilaf, not ikhtilaf.
This is a particular Hanafi approach; other schools may require unanimity.
4
Distinguish ikhtilaf from khilaf
The passage gives two criteria: (1) In ikhtilaf the method differs but the objective is unified; in khilaf both method and objective differ. (2) Ikhtilaf is based on evidence, khilaf on obstinacy. Apply these to a hypothetical scenario.
The passage says khilaf is not considered in Islamic law, while ikhtilaf is.
5
Determine when ikhtilaf makes an issue mujtahad fih
Only ikhtilaf from the first generation (Companions and Followers) counts. Later differences between schools like Hanafis and Shafi'is do not automatically make an issue mujtahad fih if there was no ikhtilaf among the Salaf. Explain the consequence for a judge's verdict.
If a judge rules against the consensus of the first generation, a higher judge can nullify that verdict.

Source Text

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مجتہد فیہ وہ مسئلہ کہلاتا ہے جو کتاب اللہ ، سنت مشہورہ اور اجماع کے خلاف نہ ہو۔ اور خود اسپر کوئی اختلاف نہ ہو۔ جیسے ولا تنكحوا مانكح أباؤكم من النساء یعنی نکاح میں نہ لاؤ جن عورتوں کو نکاح میں لائے تمہارے باپ۔ اس آیت کی مراد پر تمام سلف کا اتفاق ہے کہ جس عورت کے ساتھ باپ نے نکاح کیا اور پھر اس کو طلاق دیدی تو عدت گزرنے کے بعد بیٹے کے ساتھ اس کا نکاح نا جائز ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ اس آیت سے سوتیلی ماں کی حرمت پر تمام اسلاف کا اتفاق ہے۔ اسی طرح باپ کی موطو ہ باندی کے ساتھ نکاح کے جواز کا حکم دیدیا تو وہ قاضی جس کے پاس اس کا مرافعہ کیا گیا اس حکم کو باطل کر دے گا۔ اور سنت سے مراد سنت مشہورہ ہے۔ یعنی جو سنت صحابہ اور تابعین میں شہرت کے درجہ کو پہنچی ہو اور ہم تک اس کی نقل صحیح اور مشہور سند کے ساتھ پہنچی ہو۔ پس اگر قاضی نے ایسی سنت مشہورہ کے خلاف فیصلہ دیا ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا اس فیصلہ کو باطل کر دے گا۔ اور اجماع سے مراد وہ ہے جس پر جمہور اسلاف یعنی اکثر اور اجل علما متفق ہوں یعنی جس امر پر اکثر اور جمہور علما نے اتفاق کیا اور قاضی نے اس کے خلاف فیصلہ دیا تو قاضی اعلیٰ جس کے پاس مرافعہ ہو وہ اس کو توڑ دے۔ کیونکہ یہ فیصلہ اجماع کے خلاف ہے۔ اگر کسی مسئلہ پر اکثر کا اتفاق ہو گیا اور بعض علما نے اس کی مخالفت کی تو ان بعض کی مخالفت معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ بعض کا مخالفت کرنا ، اختلاف نہیں کہلا تا بلکہ خلاف کہلاتا ہے اور شریعت اسلام میں اختلاف تو معتبر ہے۔ لیکن خلاف معتبر نہیں ہے۔ خلاف اور اختلاف میں فرق یہ ہے کہ خلاف میں طریقہ بھی مختلف ہوتا ہے۔ اور مقصود بھی مختلف ہوتا ہے۔ اور اختلاف میں طریقہ تو مختلف ہوتا ہے مگر مقصود متحد ہوتا ہے۔ دوسرا فرق یہ ہے کہ اختلاف کی بنیاد دلیل پر ہوتی ہے اور خلاف کی بنیاد عناد پر ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی خلاف کے لئے کوئی دلیل نہیں ہوتی۔

صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ کسی مسئلہ کے مجتہد فیہ ہونے کے واسطے وہ اختلاف معتبر ہے جو صدر اول میں ہو ۔ یعنی صحابہ اور تابعین میں ہو ۔ اور اُن کے بعد کے لوگوں کا اختلاف معتبر نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً احناف اور شوافع کے درمیان اگر کسی مسئلہ میں اختلاف ہو ۔ اور صدر اول کے حضرات میں اختلاف نہ ہو تو یہ مسئلہ مجتہد فیہ نہیں کہلائے گا۔ پس اس وجہ سے اگر کسی شافعی یا مالکی نے اپنی رائے پر صدر اول کے حضرات کی رائے کے خلاف فیصلہ دیا پھر قاضی اعلیٰ کے پاس اس مسئلہ کا مرافعہ کیا گیا۔ اور یہ حکم قاضی اعلیٰ کی رائے کے بھی خلاف ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ اس فیصلہ کو توڑ دے۔
Sahib Hidayah says: A mujtahad fih issue is called that which is not contrary to the Book of Allah, the well-known Sunnah, and consensus. And there is no ikhtilaf upon it itself. Like the verse: 'And do not marry those women whom your fathers married' - meaning do not marry the women whom your fathers married. All the Salaf agreed upon the meaning of this verse that the woman whom the father married and then divorced, after the waiting period it is impermissible for the son to marry her. Summary: All the Salaf agreed upon the prohibition of the stepmother. Similarly, if [a judge] ruled on the permissibility of marrying the father's muwatthah slave-girl, then the higher judge to whom the matter is referred will nullify that ruling. And by 'Sunnah' is meant the well-known Sunnah, i.e., the Sunnah that reached the level of fame among the Companions and Followers and reached us with a correct and well-known chain. So if a judge gives a verdict contrary to such a well-known Sunnah, the higher judge to whom the matter is referred will nullify that verdict. And by 'consensus' is meant that upon which the majority of the Salaf, i.e., most and eminent scholars, agreed. So if a judge gives a verdict contrary to that, the higher judge to whom the matter is referred will break it, because this verdict is contrary to consensus. If a consensus of the majority occurs on an issue and some scholars oppose it, then the opposition of those few is not considered. Because opposing from some is not called ikhtilaf but rather khilaf. In Islamic law, ikhtilaf is considered, but khilaf is not considered. The difference between khilaf and ikhtilaf: in khilaf, both the method and the objective are different. And in ikhtilaf, the method is different but the objective is unified. A second difference: ikhtilaf is based on evidence, while khilaf is based on obstinacy, i.e., there is no evidence for khilaf.

Sahib Hidayah said: For an issue to be mujtahad fih, the ikhtilaf that is considered is that which occurred in the first generation, i.e., among the Companions and Followers. The ikhtilaf of those after them is not considered. For example, if there is ikhtilaf between Hanafis and Shafi'is on an issue, and there is no ikhtilaf among the first generation, then this issue is not called mujtahad fih. Therefore, if a Shafi'i or Maliki gave a verdict based on his opinion contrary to the opinion of the first generation, then the higher judge to whom the matter is referred, and if this ruling is also contrary to the higher judge's opinion, the higher judge will break that verdict.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage defines 'mujtahad fih' (an issue open to ijtihad) according to the Hidayah. An issue is mujtahad fih if it is not settled by a clear text from Quran, a well-known (mashhurah) Sunnah, or consensus (ijma). The example given is the prohibition of marrying a stepmother based on Quran 4:22, which all Salaf agreed upon. If a judge ruled contrary to such a definitive text, the verdict is nullified. 'Well-known Sunnah' means a hadith that became famous among the Companions and transmitted by a sound chain. 'Consensus' here means the agreement of the majority of early scholars (Salaf). The passage makes a critical distinction between 'khilaf' (mere opposition without proof) and 'ikhtilaf' (valid difference based on evidence). Khilaf is not respected in law; ikhtilaf is. Furthermore, only the ikhtilaf of the first generation (Companions and Followers) counts for making an issue mujtahad fih. Later differences, like those between Hanafis and Shafi'is, do not automatically make an issue mujtahad fih if there was no ikhtilaf among the Salaf. This has practical consequences: a judge ruling against the Salaf's view can have his verdict overturned by a higher judge.

Key Terms
مجتهد فيه (mujtahad fih): A legal issue not settled by Quran, well-known Sunnah, or consensus, and which had ikhtilaf among the first generation (Salaf).
سنت مشہورہ (sunnah mashhurah): A hadith that became well-known among the Companions and Followers and transmitted with a sound, well-known chain.
خلاف (khilaf): Opposition based on obstinacy without valid evidence; not a legitimate difference of opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes khilaf from ikhtilaf?
A) In khilaf, the method is different but objective is the same; in ikhtilaf, both differ.
B) In khilaf, both method and objective differ and there is no evidence; in ikhtilaf, method differs but objective is unified and it is based on evidence.
C) Khilaf occurs among the Salaf; ikhtilaf occurs among later scholars.
D) Khilaf is allowed; ikhtilaf is not.

Key Takeaway
An issue is mujtahad fih only if it lacks a decisive text from Quran, well-known Sunnah, or consensus of the Salaf, and if valid ikhtilaf (based on evidence) existed among the first generation.

Effect of Qadi's Ruling on Zahir and Batin
Ruling on the extent of a judge's verdict.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the effect of a qadi's verdict on the inner religious status (batin) and identify the condition (sabab mu'ayyan) required.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling on tahrim/tahlil under a specific cause binds both zahir and batin according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a subtle point in Islamic judicial theory: does a qadi's verdict affect only the external, legal outcome, or does it also determine the true religious status before Allah? According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when the claim is based on a specific cause—like false testimony in a contract or dissolution—the judge's decision on prohibition or permissibility carries weight in both the apparent and inner realities. This is a distinctive Hanafi view that requires careful parsing of its condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its author
Locate the statement attributed to Abu Hanifa: the judge's ruling on tahrim or tahlil in the zahir is also effective in the batin.
The text uses ‘ind Abi Hanifa, showing this is his position.
2
Note the condition
The phrase ‘idha kanat al-da'wa bi sabab mu'ayyan' indicates the condition: the claim must be based on a specific cause.
A general claim without a specific cause does not trigger this effect.
3
Recognize the context
The passage references the issue of the judge's ruling in contracts and dissolutions based on false testimony (shahadat al-zur).
This links to earlier discussion in the book of Nikah.
4
Understand the implication
Under this view, the qadi's verdict has binding force not only externally but also religiously, meaning the parties must consider the matter as determined by the court in their conscience.
This contrasts with views that separate court rulings from inner religious duty.
5
Apply the distinction
If the condition is absent (no specific cause), the verdict affects only the zahir, leaving the batin unaffected.
This nuance is essential for proper application.

قال وكل شئ قضى به القاضى فى الظاهر بتحريمه فهو في الباطن كذلك عند ابي حنيفة و كذا اذا قضى باحلال وهذا اذا كانت الدعوى بسبب معين وهى مسألة قضاء القاضى في العقود والفسوخ بشهادة الزور و قد مرت في النكاح

ترجمہ اور ہر وہ چیز جس کے حرام ہونے کا ظاہر میں قاضی نے حکم دیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک باطن میں بھی ایسا ہی ہے۔ اور اسی طرح اگر قاضی نے کسی چیز کے حلال ہونے کا حکم دیا۔ اور یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جب دعوئی کسی سبب معین کیسا تھ ہو ۔ اور یہی جھوٹی گواہی پر عقود اور فسوخ میں قضائے قاضی کا مسئلہ ہے اور یہ کتاب النکاح میں گذر چکا۔

تشریح مسئلہ سے پہلے دو باتیں مقدمہ کے طور پر ذہن نشین فرما لیجیئے۔
He said: And everything which the judge ruled in the zahir as prohibited, it is likewise in the batin according to Abu Hanifa. And similarly if he ruled as permissible. And this is when the claim was based on a specific cause. And this is the issue of the judge's ruling in contracts and dissolutions based on false testimony, and it has passed in the book of Nikah.

Translation: And everything which the judge ruled in the zahir as prohibited, according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is likewise in the batin. And similarly if he ruled on something as permissible. And this ruling is when the claim was with a specific cause. And this is the issue of the judge's ruling in contracts and dissolutions based on false testimony, and it has passed in the book of Nikah.

Explanation: Before the issue, keep two introductory points in mind.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the base text (Al-Hidayah or similar) regarding the effect of a judge's verdict. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a judge rules that something is haram (prohibited) in the apparent sense (zahir), then that ruling also applies to the inner reality (batin). The same applies if he rules something as halal. However, this is conditioned on the claim being based on a specific cause (sabab mu'ayyan), such as contracts or dissolutions based on false testimony. This issue was previously discussed in the book of Nikah. The commentary (Sharh) indicates that two preliminary points need to be understood before delving into the details. This ruling shows that in certain cases, the qadi's verdict has binding effect not only on the external outcome but also on the religious status of the matter in the sight of Allah, according to Abu Hanifa. This is a unique Hanafi position; other schools may differentiate between zahir and batin in such cases.

Key Terms
ظاهر (zahir): The apparent, external aspect of a matter, as determined by legal procedure and evidence in court.
باطن (batin): The inner reality of a matter, as known to Allah, or the true religious status regardless of court proceedings.
سبب معين (sabab mu'ayyan): A specific cause or basis for the claim, such as a particular contract or dissolution, as opposed to a general claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when does a judge's ruling on tahrim or tahlil affect both zahir and batin?
A) In all cases without exception.
B) Only when the claim is based on a specific cause, such as false testimony.
C) Only when the judge is absolutely certain.
D) Only in cases of marriage contracts.

Key Takeaway
A judge's verdict regarding prohibition or permissibility of a specific transaction based on false testimony affects both the external and internal religious status, according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Definition of Mujtahid Fih and the Ikhtilaf–Khilaf Distinction
Definition of mujtahid fih and the ikhtilaf–khilaf distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mujtahid fih, list its three definitive boundaries, and distinguish ikhtilaf from khilaf to determine when a judge's verdict can be overturned.

Core Idea
A matter is mujtahid fih only if not settled by Quran, sunnah mashhurah, or early consensus, and valid ikhtilaf is from the salaf.

This passage from the Hidayah clarifies what makes a legal issue open to ijtihad. Not every disagreement counts—only ikhtilaf based on evidence among the early generations (salaf) qualifies. This distinction directly affects whether a judge's verdict can be overturned by a higher court. Let's unpack the definition and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three definitive sources
The passage states that a matter is NOT mujtahid fih if it contradicts the Quran, the well-known Sunnah (sunnah mashhurah), or the consensus (ijma) of the majority of early scholars. These three sources settle an issue definitively.
Sunnah mashhurah is a distinct Hanafi category – widely transmitted from Companions and Successors, stronger than ahad hadith.
2
Understand the example of the stepmother
The verse about not marrying women your fathers married is cited as a settled matter because all early scholars agree on its meaning. Thus, it is NOT mujtahid fih. A judge ruling contrary to it must be overturned.
The example shows that clear text + ijma makes an issue non-ijtihadi.
3
Grasp the temporal scope of valid ikhtilaf
Only disagreement among the Companions and Successors (salaf) makes a matter mujtahid fih. Later disagreements, such as between Hanafis and Shafi'is, do not qualify if the salaf were unanimous.
This is a signature Hanafi view: later ikhtilaf cannot create ijtihad territory where none existed.
4
Distinguish ikhtilaf from khilaf
Ikhtilaf is valid disagreement based on evidence, with the same objective but different methods. Khilaf is opposition without evidence, based on obstinacy, with different objectives. Only ikhtilaf is recognized in Islamic law.
The consequence: a verdict based on khilaf is invalid and must be overturned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الادب القاضی
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مجتہد فیہ وہ مسئلہ کہلاتا ہے جو کتاب اللہ ، سنت مشہورہ اور اجماع کے خلاف نہ ہو۔ اور خود اسپر کوئی اختلاف نہ ہو۔ جیسے ولا تنكحوا مانكح أباؤكم من النساء یعنی نکاح میں نہ لاؤ جن عورتوں کو نکاح میں لائے تمہارے باپ۔ اس آیت کی مراد پر تمام سلف کا اتفاق ہے کہ جس عورت کے ساتھ باپ نے نکاح کیا اور پھر اس کو طلاق دیدی تو عدت گزرنے کے بعد بیٹے کے ساتھ اس کا نکاح نا جائز ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ اس آیت سے سوتیلی ماں کی حرمت پر تمام اسلاف کا اتفاق ہے۔ اسی طرح باپ کی موطو ہ باندی کے ساتھ نکاح کے جواز کا حکم دیدیا تو وہ قاضی جس کے پاس اس کا مرافعہ کیا گیا اس حکم کو باطل کر دے گا۔ اور سنت سے مراد سنت مشہورہ ہے۔ یعنی جو سنت صحابہ اور تابعین میں شہرت کے درجہ کو پہنچی ہو اور ہم تک اس کی نقل صحیح اور مشہور سند کے ساتھ پہنچی ہو۔ پس اگر قاضی نے ایسی سنت مشہورہ کے خلاف فیصلہ دیا ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا اس فیصلہ کو باطل کر دے گا۔ اور اجماع سے مراد وہ ہے جس پر جمہور اسلاف یعنی اکثر اور اجل علما متفق ہوں یعنی جس امر پر اکثر اور جمہور علما نے اتفاق کیا اور قاضی نے اس کے خلاف فیصلہ دیا تو قاضی اعلیٰ جس کے پاس مرافعہ ہو وہ اس کو توڑ دے۔ کیونکہ یہ فیصلہ اجماع کے خلاف ہے۔ اگر کسی مسئلہ پر اکثر کا اتفاق ہو گیا اور بعض علما نے اس کی مخالفت کی تو ان بعض کی مخالفت معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ بعض کا مخالفت کرنا ، اختلاف نہیں کہلا تا بلکہ خلاف کہلاتا ہے اور شریعت اسلام میں اختلاف تو معتبر ہے۔ لیکن خلاف معتبر نہیں ہے۔ خلاف اور اختلاف میں فرق یہ ہے کہ خلاف میں طریقہ بھی مختلف ہوتا ہے۔ اور مقصود بھی مختلف ہوتا ہے۔ اور اختلاف میں طریقہ تو مختلف ہوتا ہے مگر مقصود متحد ہوتا ہے۔ دوسرا فرق یہ ہے کہ اختلاف کی بنیاد دلیل پر ہوتی ہے اور خلاف کی بنیاد عناد پر ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی خلاف کے لئے کوئی دلیل نہیں ہوتی۔ حب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ کسی مسئلہ کے مجتہد فیہ ہونے کے واسطے وہ اختلاف معتبر ہے جو صد را دل میں ہو ۔ یعنی صحابہ اور تابعین میں ہو ۔ اور اُن کے بعد کے لوگوں کا اختلاف معتبر نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً احناف اور شوافع کے درمیان اگر کسی مسئلہ میں اختلاف ہو ۔ اور صدر اول کے حضرات میں اختلاف نہ ہو تو یہ مسئلہ مجتہد فیہ نہیں کہلائے گا۔ پس اس وجہ سے اگر کسی شافعی یا مالکی نے اپنی رائے پر صدر اول کے حضرات کی رائے کے خلاف فیصلہ دیا پھر قاضی اعلیٰ کے پاس اس مسئلہ کا مرافعہ کیا گیا۔ اور یہ حکم قاضی اعلیٰ کی رائے کے بھی خلاف ہو تو قاضی اعلیٰ اس فیصلہ کو توڑ دے۔
The author of Hidayah says: A matter is called mujtahid fih which does not oppose the Book of Allah, the well-known Sunnah, and consensus, and there is no disagreement about it itself. For example, 'Do not marry those [women] whom your fathers married,' meaning do not take in marriage those women whom your fathers have married. All the early scholars agree on the meaning of this verse: that if a woman married a father and he divorced her, after her 'idda it is not permissible for the son to marry her. In summary, all early scholars agree on the prohibition of the stepmother from this verse. Similarly, if a judge ruled the permissibility of marrying a father's muwatwu'ah slave-girl, then the judge to whom the appeal is made will annul that ruling. And by Sunnah is meant the well-known Sunnah, i.e., the Sunnah that attained fame among the Companions and Successors and reached us through a sound and well-known chain. So if a judge gave a verdict contrary to such a well-known Sunnah, the higher judge to whom the appeal is made will annul that verdict. And by consensus is meant that on which the majority of early scholars, i.e., most and eminent scholars, agree. So if a matter is agreed upon by most and the majority of scholars and a judge gives a verdict against it, the higher judge to whom the appeal is made will break it. This verdict is against consensus. If on a matter the majority have agreed and some scholars opposed them, the opposition of those few is not considered. Because the opposition of a few is not called ikhtilaf but rather khilaf. In Islamic law, ikhtilaf is considered, but khilaf is not. The difference between khilaf and ikhtilaf is that in khilaf both the method and the objective are different. In ikhtilaf, the method is different but the objective is the same. Another difference: ikhtilaf is based on evidence, while khilaf is based on obstinacy. Thus, khilaf has no evidence. The author of Hidayah said: For a matter to be mujtahid fih, the valid ikhtilaf is that which occurred in the early period, i.e., among the Companions and Successors. The ikhtilaf of later people is not considered. For example, if there is a difference between Hanafis and Shafi'is on a matter, and the early scholars did not differ, then this matter is not called mujtahid fih. Therefore, if a Shafi'i or Maliki gave a verdict based on his own opinion contrary to the opinion of the early scholars, and then the matter was appealed to a higher judge, and this verdict also contradicts the opinion of the higher judge, then the higher judge will break that verdict.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah defines what constitutes a matter subject to ijtihad (mujtahid fih). It is a definition_ruling. The author begins by stating that a matter is mujtahid fih if it does not contradict the Quran, the well-known Sunnah, or consensus, and if there is no explicit disagreement about it among the early scholars. The example of the prohibition of marrying stepmothers from the Quran is given to show a matter that is not mujtahid fih because it is settled. The passage then clarifies that the Sunnah meant is the well-known, widely transmitted one (sunnah mashhurah), not single reports. Similarly, the consensus meant is that of the majority of early scholars. The author then distinguishes between ikhtilaf (valid disagreement based on evidence) and khilaf (invalid opposition without evidence). This distinction is crucial for determining when a judge's verdict can be overturned. According to Hidayah, only ikhtilaf among the early generations (as-salaf) counts; later disagreements do not make a matter mujtahid fih. Therefore, if a judge gives a verdict based on a later opinion contrary to the early consensus, the higher judge can overturn it.

Key Terms
مجتہد فیہ (mujtahid fih): A legal matter subject to ijtihad, not settled by decisive texts or consensus.
سنت مشہورہ (sunnah mashhurah): A well-known sunnah transmitted through many chains from the Companions and Successors.
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of the majority of early scholars.
اختلاف (ikhtilaf): Legitimate disagreement based on evidence.
خلاف (khilaf): Opposition without evidence, based on obstinacy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hidayah, which of the following makes a matter mujtahid fih?
A) When there is any disagreement among later scholars
B) When there is legitimate disagreement among the early generation (salaf) based on evidence
C) When the matter is explicitly stated in the Quran
D) When the matter is agreed upon by the majority of scholars at any time

Key Takeaway
Ikhtilaf is valid only when based on evidence among the salaf; anything else is khilaf and cannot make a matter mujtahid fih, allowing higher judges to overturn contrary verdicts.

Effect of Judge's Decree Based on False Testimony: Ownership Types and Enforcement
Ruling on effect of judge's decree based on false testimony, with preliminary concepts of ownership types and enforcement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between unrestricted and restricted ownership claims and state the Hanafi ruling on the external and internal effect of a judge's decree based on false testimony in each case.

Core Idea
A judge's decree based on false testimony is binding externally, but internally only for restricted claims according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a critical issue in qada: when a judge's decree is based on false testimony, does it alter the religious reality or only the social one? The answer hinges on the type of ownership claim. Understanding the distinction between nafadh zahiri (external enforcement) and nafadh batini (internal enforcement) is essential for grasping the limits of judicial authority in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ownership claims
First, recognize that ownership claims can be unrestricted (amlak murSala), where the cause of ownership is not mentioned, or restricted (amlak muqayyada), where the cause is specified (e.g., purchase, inheritance). This classification determines the ruling.
Unrestricted: 'This is mine' without cause. Restricted: 'I bought this' or 'I inherited this'.
2
Understand the two types of enforcement
A judge's decree can have external effect (nafadh zahiri) – binding among people – and internal effect (nafadh batini) – religiously binding between the individual and Allah. The text explains both.
External: the decree is executed socially. Internal: the decree changes what is permissible religiously.
3
Apply the ruling to unrestricted ownership
For unrestricted claims, a decree based on false testimony is effective only externally, not internally, by consensus. The example given: a person claims a slave-girl without cause, produces false witnesses; the decree gives him external ownership but he cannot have intercourse with her religiously.
Implication: the plaintiff may use the property externally but not internally.
4
Apply the ruling to restricted ownership
For restricted claims, according to Abu Hanifa and the first qawl of Abu Yusuf, the decree is effective both externally and internally. The example: a wife falsely claims talaq with false witnesses; the decree makes the marriage dissolved and the second husband lawful even religiously.
This is a key point of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school and with other schools.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute
Abu Yusuf has a second qawl disagreeing with Abu Hanifa; Imam Muhammad, Imam Malik, and Imam Shafi'i also differ. The text cuts off, but the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the second marriage is religiously valid.
The mufta bihi is not stated; likely Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text

تشریح مسئلہ سے پہلے دو باتیں مقدمہ کے طور پر ذہن نشین فرما لیجیئے۔

پہلی بات یہ کہ املاک کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔
ا۔ املاک مرسلہ۔
- املاک مقیده
املاک مرسلہ اُن املاک کو کہتے ہیں جن میں سب ملک مذکور نہ ہو۔ مثلاً ایک شخص نے کسی باندی یا گندم میں اپنی ملک کا دعوی کیا۔ اور مالک ہونے کا سبب ، شرا یا ارث وغیرہ ذکر نہیں کیا تو یہ ملک، مرسل اور مطلق کہلائے گی۔ اور املاک مقیدہ ان املاک کو کہتے ہیں جن میں سبب ملک مذکور ہو۔ مثلاً ایک شخص نے دعویٰ کیا کہ فلاں باندی کو میں نے خریدا ہے اس لئے وہ میری مملوکہ ہے یا مجھے کو وراثت میں ملی ہے اس لئے میں اس کا مالک ہوں تو یہ ملک مقیدہ کہلائے گی۔ دوسری بات یہ کہ نفاذ کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔
ا نفاذ ظاہری۔
-۲ نفاذ باطنی ۔
نفاذ ظاہری تو یہ ہے کہ حکم فیما بین الناس نافذ کر دیا جائے اور نفاذ باطنی فیما بینہ و بین اللہ نافذ کرنے کا نام ہے۔ مثلا گواہی کی بنیاد پر قاضی نے حکم دیا کہ آمنہ، خالد کی بیوی ہے تو اس کے ظاہر ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ عورت اپنے آپ کو خالد کے سپر د کر دے اور خالد اس کا نان نفقہ ادا کر دے۔ اور باطناً نافذ ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فیما بینہما و بین اللہ خالد کے لئے آمنہ سے وہی کرنا حلال ہو گیا اور آمنہ کے لئے اپنے اوپر خالد کو قدرت دینا حلال ہو گیا۔
املاک مرسلہ میں اگر قاضی نے جھوٹی گواہی پر حکم دیا تو قاضی کا یہ حکم بالا جماع باطناً نافذ نہیں ہوگا۔ البتہ ظاہر آنا فذ ہو جائے گا۔ مثلاً ایک شخص نے قاضی کی عدالت میں دعویٰ کیا کہ یہ باندی میری ہے میں اس کا مالک ہوں۔ لیکن سبپ ملک ذکر نہیں کیا کہ اس کو خریدا ہے یا میراث میں ملی ہے یا کس نے ہبہ کی ہے۔ پھر مدعی نے دو گواہ پیش کر دیئے قاضی نے گواہوں کی گواہی پر باندی کا حکم کر دیا تو یہ حکم ظاہر نافذ ہوگا ۔ یعنی مدعی اس کا مالک ہوگا اور اس پر نفقہ واجب ہوگا ۔ اور باندی پر خدمت کرنا واجب ہو گا مگر یہ حکم باطناً نافذ نہ ہوگا ۔ یعنی فیما بینہما و بین اللہ مدعی کے واسطے اس باندی کے ساتھ وطی کرنا حلال نہ ہوگا ۔ اور باندی پر قدرت دینا حلال نہ ہو گا۔ اور اگر جھوٹی گواہی کی بنیاد پر قاضی نے املاک مقیدہ کے بارے میں کوئی حکم دیا مثلاً ایک عورت نے اپنے شوہر پر دعویٰ کیا کہ اُس نے مجھ کو تین طلاقیں دی ہیں۔ اور اپنے دعوئی پر جھوٹے گواہ پیش کر دئیے۔ پس قاضی نے دونوں کے درمیان فرقت کا فیصلہ کر دیا اور عورت نے عدت پوری ہونے کے بعد دوسرے شوہر سے نکاح کر لیا۔ پھر قاضی کو گواہوں کا جھوٹا ہونا معلوم ہوا تو حضرت امام اعظم کے نزدیک قاضی کا یہ فیصلہ ظاہراً اور باطنا دونوں طرح نافذ ہو گا۔ یعنی شوہر اول کے لئے اس عورت کے ساتھ وطی کرنا حرام ہو گا ۔ اور شوہر اول پر اس کا نان نفقہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور شوہر ثانی کے لئے ظاہرا اور باطنا دونوں طرح حلال ہو جائے گی خواہ شوہر ثانی کو حقیقت حال کا علم ہو بایں طور کہ شوہر ثانی خود ایک جھوٹا گواہ ہو۔ یا حقیقت حال کا علم نہ ہو ۔ بایں طور کہ زوج ثانی کوئی اجنبی آدمی ہو ۔ یہی امام ابو یوسف کا قول اول ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف کا دوسرا قول اور امام محمد ، امام مالک، امام شافعی ، امام
Every thing regarding which the judge passes a decree in its outward aspect as forbidden is also forbidden inwardly according to Abu Hanifa, and similarly if he decrees it permissible. This is when the claim is based on a specific cause, and this is the issue of the judge's decree in contracts and annulments based on false testimony, and it has passed in the Book of Nikah. Translation: And every thing regarding which the judge passes a decree outwardly as forbidden is also forbidden inwardly according to Abu Hanifa. And similarly if he decrees something permissible. And this decree is when the claim is due to a specific cause. And this is the issue of the judge's decree in contracts and annulments based on false testimony, and it has passed in the Book of Nikah. Explanation: Before explaining the issue, keep two preliminary points in mind. First, there are two types of ownership: 1. Unrestricted ownership (amlak murSala) 2. Restricted ownership (amlak muqayyada). Unrestricted ownership means ownership in which the cause of ownership is not mentioned. For example, a person claims ownership of a slave-girl or wheat, but does not mention the cause, such as purchase or inheritance. This is called unrestricted and absolute ownership. Restricted ownership is where the cause of ownership is mentioned. For example, a person claims that he bought a certain slave-girl, so she is his property, or that he inherited her, so he is her owner. This is called restricted ownership. Second, there are two types of enforcement (nafadh): 1. External enforcement (zahiri) 2. Internal enforcement (batini). External enforcement is that the decree is executed among people. Internal enforcement is its execution between him and Allah. For example, on the basis of testimony, a judge passed a decree that Amina is Khalid's wife. The meaning of its becoming external is that the woman submits herself to Khalid and Khalid pays her maintenance. The meaning of internal enforcement is that between them and Allah, it becomes permissible for Khalid to have intercourse with Amina, and permissible for Amina to allow Khalid access to her. In unrestricted ownership, if the judge passes a decree based on false testimony, then this decree, by consensus, does not take effect internally; rather, it becomes effective only externally. For example, a person claims in court that this slave-girl is his, he is her owner, but does not mention the cause. Then the plaintiff produces two witnesses, and the judge, based on their testimony, decrees the slave-girl to him. This decree takes effect externally: the plaintiff becomes her owner, maintenance is obligatory on him, and the slave-girl must serve him. But this decree does not take effect internally: it is not permissible for the plaintiff to have intercourse with this slave-girl between him and Allah, nor is it permissible for the slave-girl to allow him access. And if on the basis of false testimony, the judge passes a decree regarding restricted ownership, for example, a wife claims that her husband gave her three divorces, and produces false witnesses. The judge decrees separation between them, and the woman marries another after completing her 'idda. Then the judge discovers the witnesses were false. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this decree takes effect both externally and internally: it becomes unlawful for the first husband to have intercourse with her, and he is not obliged to provide maintenance. And the second husband becomes lawful to her both externally and internally, whether or not the second husband knows the real situation (even if he himself was a false witness, or he is a stranger). This is the first qawl of Imam Abu Yusuf. The second qawl of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, Imam...
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Abu Hanifa regarding the effect of a judge's decree based on false testimony. It is a ruling_with_proof. The Arabic states that according to Abu Hanifa, if a judge decrees something haram outwardly, it is also haram inwardly, and similarly for halal, provided the claim was made with a specific cause (sabab mu'ayyan). The commentator then explains two preliminary concepts: types of ownership (amlak) and types of enforcement (nafadh). Amlak MurSala are claims without specifying the cause; Amlak Muqayyada specify the cause. Nafadh Zahiri is external legal effect; Nafadh Batini is internal religious effect. The key ruling is that for unrestricted ownership claims, a decree based on false testimony is effective only externally, not internally, by consensus. For restricted ownership claims (like talaq), according to Abu Hanifa and the first qawl of Abu Yusuf, the decree is effective both externally and internally. The text then begins to mention the second qawl of Abu Yusuf and the views of Imam Muhammad, Malik, and Shafi'i, but cuts off, so the full dispute is not available.

Key Terms
املاک مرسلہ (amlak murSala): Unrestricted ownership claims where the cause of ownership (purchase, inheritance, etc.) is not specified.
املاک مقیدہ (amlak muqayyada): Restricted ownership claims where the cause of ownership is mentioned.
نفاذ ظاہری (nafadh zahiri): External enforcement of a judicial decree, i.e., its legal effect among people.
نفاذ باطنی (nafadh batini): Internal enforcement of a judicial decree, i.e., its effect between the individual and Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the effect of a judge's decree based on false testimony in a case of unrestricted ownership (amlak murSala)?
A) The decree is effective both externally and internally
B) The decree is effective only externally, not internally
C) The decree has no effect at all
D) The decree is effective internally but not externally

Key Takeaway
A judge's decree based on false testimony is effective externally in all ownership claims, but internally only in restricted claims according to Abu Hanifa.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
10 min
Effect of False Testimony: Unrestricted vs Restricted Claims
Explains classification of claims and effect of false testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between unrestricted and restricted claims, explain the Hanafi position on the inward effectiveness of a judge's ruling based on false testimony, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling based on false testimony is outwardly effective in all claims, but inwardly effective only in restricted claims according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical issue in Islamic judicial procedure: what is the legal effect of a judge's ruling when it is based on false testimony? The answer depends on the type of claim involved. Claims are classified as unrestricted (mursal) or restricted (muqayyad), and the ruling's enforcement is divided into outward (zahiri) and inward (batini). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying Hanafi fiqh in court settings and for recognizing the limits of a judge's authority over reality before Allah.

Guided Path
1
Classify the claim as mursal or muqayyad
Identify whether the claimant mentioned the cause of ownership (e.g., purchase, inheritance). If no cause is mentioned, the claim is unrestricted (mursal); if a cause is specified, it is restricted (muqayyad).
In the examples, a bare claim of ownership without cause is mursal; a claim stating 'I bought this' is muqayyad.
2
Apply the consensus rule for mursal claims
By consensus of all schools, a judge's ruling based on false testimony in unrestricted claims is effective outwardly but not inwardly. This means worldly legal effects (e.g., ownership, maintenance) are enforced, but the reality before Allah remains unchanged (e.g., intercourse is not permissible).
Note the example: the claimant becomes owner outwardly but cannot have intercourse with the slave-girl.
3
Analyze the dispute for muqayyad claims
For restricted claims, there is a dispute. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (first opinion) hold that the ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly. The second opinion of Abu Yusuf, along with Muhammad, Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad, holds that it is effective outwardly only.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) appears in cases like a false divorce claim: the woman's second marriage is valid and intercourse halal under Abu Hanifa's view, but considered adultery under the opposing view.
4
Identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's first opinion: for restricted claims, the ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly. This is the view presented in Zahir al-Riwayah and is followed in fatwa.
Al-Marghinani and later authorities (e.g., Ibn Abidin) uphold this as the strongest view.

باطنا دونوں طرح نافذ ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے قول آخر پر اور امام محمد، امام مالک، امام شافعی اور امام احمد کے نزدیک ظاہر ا تو نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ مگر باطنا نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ اس کی مزید تفصیل اشرف الہدایہ جلد چہارم کے ۵۳ پر دیکھی جاسکتی ہے۔
The first point is that property claims are of two types: 1. Unrestricted claims (amlak mursala). 2. Restricted claims (amlak muqayyada). Unrestricted claims are those in which the cause of ownership is not mentioned. For example, a person claimed ownership of a slave-girl or wheat without mentioning the cause, such as purchase or inheritance. This claim is called mursal and absolute. Restricted claims are those in which the cause of ownership is mentioned. For example, a person claimed: 'I bought this slave-girl, therefore she is my property,' or 'I inherited her, therefore I am her owner.' This is called muqayyad claim. The second point is that enforcement is of two types: 1. Outward enforcement. 2. Inward enforcement. Outward enforcement means that the ruling is enforced among the people. Inward enforcement means enforcement between the parties and Allah. For example, based on testimony, the judge ruled that Amina is Khalid's wife. The outward effect is that the woman submits to Khalid and he provides for her maintenance. The inward effect is that, between them and Allah, intercourse becomes permissible for Khalid with Amina, and it becomes permissible for Amina to allow Khalid access. In unrestricted claims, if the judge gives a ruling based on false testimony, this ruling, by consensus, is not effective inwardly. However, it is effective outwardly. For example, a person claimed in the judge's court: 'This slave-girl is mine, I am her owner,' but he did not mention the cause of ownership—whether he bought her, inherited her, or was given her as a gift. Then the claimant produced two witnesses, and the judge ruled in his favor based on their testimony. This ruling is effective outwardly: the claimant becomes the owner and is obligated to provide maintenance, and the slave-girl is obligated to serve him. But the ruling is not effective inwardly: between the parties and Allah, it is not permissible for the claimant to have intercourse with the slave-girl, nor is it permissible for the slave-girl to allow him access. If the judge gives a ruling based on false testimony regarding restricted claims—for example, a woman claimed that the husband had divorced her three times, and she produced false witnesses; the judge then separated them, and after completing her waiting period, she married another man. Later, the judge discovered the witnesses were false. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly: intercourse with the first husband becomes prohibited, and maintenance is not obligatory upon him. For the second husband, she becomes permissible both outwardly and inwardly, whether the second husband knew the truth (e.g., he himself was a false witness) or did not know (e.g., he was a stranger). This is also the first opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf. Imam Abu Yusuf's second opinion, and the madhhab of Imam Muhammad, Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad, is that the judge's ruling is not effective inwardly: intercourse with the second husband is prohibited, and if he does engage, it is considered adultery. Similarly, if a man produced two false witnesses to marry a woman who denies the marriage, and the judge ruled the marriage valid, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa (based on Abu Yusuf's first opinion), the ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly: intercourse is permissible and the woman must submit. According to Abu Yusuf's second opinion, and the views of Imam Muhammad, Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad, the ruling is effective outwardly but not inwardly: intercourse is not permissible and submission is not allowed. The author of Hidayah states that the title of this issue is 'Qada al-Qadi fi al-Uqud wa al-Fusukh bi Shahadat al-Zur' (The Judge's Ruling in Contracts and Dissolutions Based on False Testimony). According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's first opinion, the ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly. According to Abu Yusuf's latter opinion and the views of Muhammad, Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad, it is effective outwardly but not inwardly. Further details can be seen in Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume 4, page 53.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the effect of a judge's ruling based on false testimony, presented in the context of Kitab al-Adab al-Qadi (The Judge's Conduct). The author first distinguishes between two types of property claims: unrestricted (mursala) where the cause of ownership is not mentioned, and restricted (muqayyada) where the cause is specified. Then he explains the two types of enforcement of a judgment: outward (zahiri) which affects worldly interactions, and inward (batini) which concerns the ruling's validity before Allah. By consensus (ijma), in unrestricted claims, a ruling based on false testimony is effective outwardly but not inwardly. The dispute arises in restricted claims. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf in his first opinion hold that the ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly, meaning that the legal consequences (like permissibility of intercourse) are realized even before Allah. The second opinion of Abu Yusuf, along with Imam Muhammad, Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad, maintains that the ruling is only effective outwardly; inwardly the original reality prevails, so acts like intercourse remain prohibited. The author of Al-Hidayah notes that this is the well-known issue and presents both positions without explicit tarjih, though in Hanafi fiqh, the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's first opinion is generally relied upon. The passage underscores an important principle: a judge's ruling changes only the outward legal status, not the inner reality before Allah, except in certain cases like restricted claims according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
املاک مرسلہ (amlak mursala): Claims where the cause of ownership (such as purchase or inheritance) is not mentioned by the claimant.
املاک مقیدہ (amlak muqayyada): Claims where the cause of ownership is explicitly mentioned by the claimant.
نفاذ ظاہری (nifadh zahiri): Outward enforcement of a judge's ruling, meaning it is implemented among people in terms of worldly legal effects.
نفاذ باطنی (nifadh batini): Inward enforcement of a judge's ruling, meaning the ruling changes the legal reality before Allah, making acts permissible or impermissible accordingly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In restricted claims (amlak muqayyada), what is the Hanafi mufta bihi position regarding the inward effectiveness of a judge's ruling based on false testimony?
A) The ruling is effective only outwardly, by consensus of all Hanafi scholars.
B) The ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's first opinion.
C) The ruling is effective inwardly only, according to Imam Muhammad.
D) The ruling is completely void both outwardly and inwardly.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, for restricted claims (amlak muqayyada), the relied-upon position is that a judge's ruling based on false testimony is effective both outwardly and inwardly, affecting the ruling before Allah.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
