تی سی صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اگر دو شخصوں نے کسی نزاعی مسئلہ میں ایک تیسرے آدمی کو حکم مقرر کیا اور اس کے فیصلہ پر راضی ہو گئے۔ تو یہ جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ دونوں کی ذات پر ولایت حاصل ہے۔ لہذا ان دونوں کا اپنے مسئلہ میں کسی تیسرے آدمی کو حکم بنا نا صحیح ہے اور جب حکم بنانا جائز ہے تو حکم کا فیصلہ بھی ان دونوں پر نافذ ہوگا۔ البتہ ان دونوں کے علاوہ پر نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اگر مشتری اور بائع کے درمیان اختلاف کی وجہ سے دونوں نے کسی تیسرے آدمی کو حکم مقرر کیا۔ پھر حکم کے فیصلہ کے مطابق مشتری نے اپنے بائع کو مبیع والپس کر دی تو بائع کے لئے اپنے بائع کی طرف واپس کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بائع ثانی اور مشتری جنہوں نے حکم مقرر کیا ہے۔ اُن پر تو حکم کا فیصلہ نافذ ہوگا۔ لیکن بائع اول پر جو ان دونوں کا غیر ہے اُس پر اس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ حکم وہی شخص ہو سکتا ہے جس میں قاضی اور حاکم بننے کی صلاحیت ہو۔ یعنی جس طرح قاضی کے لئے شہادت کا اہل ہونا شرط ہے اسی طرح علم کے واسطے بھی شہادت کا اہل ہونا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ حکم ان دونوں شخصوں کے درمیان جنھوں نے حکم مقرر کیا ہے بمنزلہ قاضی کے ہے۔ اور قاضی کے لئے چونکہ شہادت کا اہل اور قضاء کا اہل ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اس لئے حکم جو قاضی کے مرتبہ میں ہے اس کے واسطے بھی شہادت اور قضاء کا اہل ہونا شرط ہو گا۔ چنانچہ اگر دو شخصوں نے کسی عورت کو ایسے مسئلہ میں حکم مقرر کیا جو شہادت کے ساتھ بھی ثابت ہو جاتا ہے تو یہ جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ ایسے مسئلہ میں عورت شہادت کی اہل ہوتی ہے۔
یہ واضح رہے کہ جس طرح قاضی کے لئے اہلیت قضاء قاضی ہونے کے وقت سے لے کر فیصلہ کے وقت تک شرط ہے۔ اسی طرح حکم کے واسطے بھی حکم بننے کے وقت سے لے کر فیصلہ صادر کرنے کے وقت تک اہلیت قضاء کا موجود ہونا شرط ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر دو شخصوں نے غلام کوحکم مقرر کیا پھر وہ آزاد ہو گیا یا نا بالغ کوحکم مقرر کیا پھر وہ بالغ ہو گیا۔ یادمی کو حکم مقرر کیا پھر وہ مسلمان ہو گیا اور اس نے فیصلہ دیا تو اس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مذکورہ صورتوں میں فیصلہ کے وقت اگر چہ اہلیت قضاء موجود ہے۔ لیکن حکم مقرر کرتے وقت اہلیت قضاء موجود نہیں ہے۔
ولا يجوز تحكيم الكافر الخ - سے صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جب یہ بات مسلّم ہے کہ اہلیت قضاء اہلیت شہادت پر موقوف ہے۔ تو یہ بھی تسلیم کرنا پڑے گا ۔ کہ جس شخص میں شہادت کی اہلیت موجود نہ ہو اس کو نہ قاضی مقر ر کیا جا سکتا ہے ۔ اور نہ حکم مقرر کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ پس اسی وجہ سے کا فرکو ، غلام کو ذمی کو محدود فی القذف کو ، فاسق کو اور نابالغ کو حکم مقرر کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مذکورہ اشخاص میں چونکہ شہادت کی لیاقت موجود نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے مذکورہ اشخاص قاضی نہیں ہو سکتے اور جب قاضی نہیں ہو سکتے تو حکم بھی نہیں ہو سکتے ہیں۔ لیکن ذمّی کو حکم مقرر کرنا اُس وقت نا جائز ہے جب اس کو مسلمانوں نے حکم مقرر کیا ہو۔ اور اگر ذمیوں نے کسی ذمّی کو حکم مقرر کیا تو یہ جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ذمی ، مسلمانوں کے حق میں اگر چہ اہل شہادت میں سے نہیں ہے لیکن اہل ذمہ کے حق میں شہادت کا اہل ہوتا ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اگر فاسق کو حکم مقرر کر دیا گیا تو ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہونا چاہئے جیسے کتاب ادب القاضی کے شروع میں گذرا کہ فاسق کو قاضی نہ بنانا چاہئے لیکن اگر بنا دیا گیا تو جائز ہے۔ اور اس کا حکم قضاء نافذ ہوگا۔ اسی طرح اگر فاسق کو حکم مقرر کر دیا گیا تو بھی جائز ہونا چاہئے ۔
The book of the Adab al-Qadi (Etiquette of the Judge). Ashraf al-Hidayah volume 9. al-Qada: And it is not permissible to appoint as arbitrator: the disbeliever, the slave, the dhimmi, the one punished for false accusation of adultery (qadhf), the sinful person (fasiq), and the minor, due to the absence of capacity for judgment (ahliyyat al-qada) by analogy with capacity for testimony (ahliyyat al-shahada). And if a fasiq passes a ruling, it must be valid according to us, as passed in the matter of [the judge]. Translation: And when two people appointed a man as arbitrator, and he passed a ruling between them, and both were pleased with his ruling, it is permissible because they have authority over themselves; thus their appointment of an arbitrator is permissible, and the arbitrator's ruling is binding on them. And this ruling is when the arbitrator possesses the quality of a ruler because he is in the position of a judge between them. Therefore, capacity for judgment is a condition. And it is not permissible to appoint a disbeliever, slave, dhimmi, one punished for qadhf, fasiq, and minor as arbitrator, because, analogizing to the capacity for testimony, the capacity for judgment is absent. And if a fasiq is appointed as arbitrator, according to us it should be valid, as passed in the matter of the judge. Tī Sī Ṣāḥib Qudūrī said: If two people appointed a third person as arbitrator in a dispute and agreed to his ruling, it is permissible because they have authority over themselves. Therefore, their appointment of a third person in their matter is valid, and if the appointment is valid, the arbitrator's ruling will be binding on both of them. However, it will not be binding on anyone else. For example, if a buyer and seller had a dispute and appointed a third person as arbitrator, and according to the arbitrator's ruling, the buyer returned the sold item to his seller, it would not be permissible for that seller to return it to his own seller, because the ruling is binding on the second seller and the buyer who appointed him, but not on the first seller who is not among them. Ṣāḥib al-Hidāyah says: The arbitrator can only be a person who has the capacity to be a judge and ruler. Just as for a judge, being eligible for testimony is a condition, similarly for [the arbitrator] it is necessary to be eligible for testimony. Because the arbitrator between the two people who appointed him is in the position of a judge. And since for a judge it is necessary to be eligible for testimony and for judgment, therefore for the arbitrator, who is in the rank of a judge, being eligible for testimony and judgment is a condition. Thus, if two people appointed a woman as arbitrator in a matter that can be proven by testimony, it is permissible, because in such a matter a woman is eligible for testimony. It should be clear that just as for a judge, capacity for judgment is a condition from the time of his appointment until the time of his ruling, similarly for the arbitrator, the existence of capacity for judgment is a condition from the time of his appointment until the time he passes his ruling. Therefore, if two people appointed a slave as arbitrator and then he became free, or a minor and then he reached puberty, or a dhimmi and then he became Muslim, and then he passed a ruling, his ruling will not be enforced, because although at the time of the ruling capacity for judgment exists, at the time of appointment it did not exist. From 'and it is not permissible to appoint a disbeliever, etc.' – Ṣāḥib al-Hidāyah says: Since it is established that capacity for judgment depends on capacity for testimony, it must be accepted that a person who does not have capacity for testimony cannot be appointed as a judge nor as an arbitrator. Therefore, it is not permissible to appoint a disbeliever, slave, dhimmi, one punished for qadhf, fasiq, or minor as arbitrator, because these persons lack the capacity for testimony; thus they cannot be judges, and if they cannot be judges, they cannot be arbitrators. But appointing a dhimmi as arbitrator is impermissible only when Muslims appoint him. If dhimmis appoint a dhimmi, it is permissible, because although a dhimmi is not eligible for testimony in matters concerning Muslims, he is eligible in matters among dhimmis. Ṣāḥib al-Hidāyah said: If a fasiq is appointed as arbitrator, according to us it should be valid, as passed at the beginning of the book of Adab al-Qadi that a fasiq should not be made a judge, but if he is appointed, it is valid, and his judgment is enforceable. Similarly, if a fasiq is appointed as arbitrator, it should also be valid.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the conditions for the validity of arbitration (tahkim). The text first states the general principle: two parties can appoint a third person as arbitrator (muhakkam) to settle their dispute, and his ruling is binding on them because they have authority over their own affairs. However, the arbitrator must possess the same qualifications as a judge (qadi). Specifically, he must have capacity for judgment (ahliyyat al-qada), which is grounded in the capacity for testimony (ahliyyat al-shahada). Therefore, those disqualified from giving testimony are also disqualified from being arbitrators. The text lists seven categories: disbeliever (kafir), slave (abd), dhimmi (non-Muslim subject), one who has been punished for false accusation of adultery (mahrud fi al-qadhf), a sinful person (fasiq), and a minor (sabi). The reasoning is qiyas (analogy) to testimony: since these persons cannot be witnesses in court, they cannot be judges, and because an arbitrator is like a judge, they cannot be arbitrators either. An important exception is made for dhimmis: Muslims cannot appoint a dhimmi as arbitrator, but dhimmis can appoint one among themselves, because a dhimmi is eligible to testify in matters concerning dhimmis. Moreover, the text clarifies that the capacity for judgment must exist at both the time of appointment and the time of the ruling. If an ineligible person (e.g., a slave) is appointed and later becomes eligible (e.g., freed), his ruling is not valid because the condition was not fulfilled at appointment. Similarly, if a woman is appointed in a matter where her testimony is accepted (e.g., property disputes), it is permissible because she has partial eligibility. Finally, the text addresses the case of a fasiq (sinner): although it is not recommended to appoint a fasiq as a judge or arbitrator, if his appointment occurs, his ruling is valid and enforceable according to the Hanafi school. This is based on the principle that the fasiq's ruling, like that of a judge, is upheld despite his personal sinfulness. The passage thus establishes the Hanafi position on arbitrator eligibility with detailed conditions and exceptions.

Key Terms
تحكيم (taḥkīm): The act of appointing a third party (muhakkam) to settle a dispute by mutual consent of the parties; its ruling is binding on them.
محكم (muḥakkam): The person appointed as arbitrator; he must be eligible for judgment (ahliyyat al-qada) based on eligibility for testimony.
اهلية القضاء (ahliyyat al-qaḍā): Capacity to serve as a judge; includes being Muslim, free, mature, sane, and not a mahdud fi al-qadhf, among others.
اهلية الشهادة (ahliyyat al-shahāda): Legal capacity to give testimony in court; certain persons (e.g., disbelievers, slaves) lack this capacity.
محدود في القذف (maḥdūd fī al-qadhf): A person who has received the fixed punishment (hadd) for false accusation of adultery; loses capacity for testimony and thus for judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for determining who can be appointed as an arbitrator (muhakkam)?
A) The arbitrator must be a scholar of fiqh.
B) The arbitrator must be eligible to serve as a judge, based on capacity for testimony.
C) The arbitrator must be the most righteous person in the community.
D) The arbitrator must be appointed by the qadi.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an arbitrator's eligibility is derived from witness eligibility; only those who can serve as witnesses can serve as arbitrators, with specific exceptions for dhimmis and fasiqs.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Right of the Parties to Revoke Arbitration Before the Ruling
Ruling on revocation of arbitration before the ruling, with logical proof and qadi review.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on revocation of arbitration before a ruling and apply the conditions for bindingness of the arbitrator's decision.

Core Idea
Arbitration is consensual: each party can revoke before the ruling, but once given it binds unless contrary to the qadi's madhhab.

Arbitration (taḥkīm) is a common method of dispute resolution in Islamic law. How binding is the arbitrator's authority? Can a party withdraw before a decision? This lesson explores the Hanafi position, which emphasizes the consensual nature of the appointment and the logical consequences of revocation. We will also see how the qadi interacts with an arbitrator's ruling after it is issued.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the action being discussed: each party's right to revoke the arbitrator before a ruling. State the hukm: it is permissible (mubah).
Revocation is a unilateral right, not requiring the other party's consent.
2
Understand the legal nature of the arbitrator
Analyze the term 'muqallad' (delegate). The arbitrator's authority is derived solely from the parties' appointment. Without ongoing consent, he has no jurisdiction.
This is the core rationale for the permissibility of revocation.
3
Trace the consequence before vs. after the ruling
Before the ruling: revocation ends authority. After the ruling: the decision becomes binding on the parties because it was issued with proper authority.
The ruling is enforceable unless overturned by a qadi.
4
Examine the qadi's role
When the ruling is brought to a qadi, he checks if it aligns with his madhhab. If yes, he enforces; if no, he nullifies. The arbitrator's ruling is not binding on the qadi.
This shows the hierarchy between private arbitration and state judiciary.
5
Compare with other schools
Note that the right to revoke before the ruling is also accepted by al-Shafi'i, and one narration from Malik and Ahmad. Some earlier scholars consider the appointment irrevocable.
This highlights a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different views of the nature of the arbitration contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حکم بنانے والوں کو حکم سے رجوع کا اختیار ہے
ولكل واحد من المحكمين ان يرجع مالم يحكم عليهما لانه مقلد من جهتهما فلا يحكم الا برضاهما جميعاً واذا حكم لزمهما لصدور حكمه عن ولايه عليهما واذا رفع حكمه الى القاضى فوافق مذهبه امضاه لانه لا فائدة في نقضه ثم في إبرامه على ذلك الوجه و ان خالفه ابطله لان حكمه لا يلزمه لعدم التحكيم منه
ترجمہ اور حکم بنانے والے دونوں شخصوں میں سے ہر ایک کو حکم بنانے سے رجوع کا اختیار ہے جب تک کہ حکم نے ان پر حکم صادر نہ کیا ہو۔ اسلئے کہ اس کو ان دونوں کی طرف سے حکم مقرر کیا گیا ہے۔ لہذا وہ بغیر ان دونوں کی رضا مندی کے حکم صادر نہیں کر سکے گا۔ اور جب حکم نے حکم کر دیا تو ان دونوں پر لازم ہو گا۔ کیوں کہ ان دونوں پر ولایت حاصل ہو کر اس کا حکم صادر ہوا ہے۔ اور حکم کے حکم کا مرافعہ قاضی کے پاس کیا گیا اور وہ حکم اس کے مذہب کے موافق نکلا تو قاضی اس کو نافذ کرے گا۔ کیوں کہ اس کے حکم کو توڑ کر پھر اُسی طور پر مضبوط کرنے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر حکم کا حکم قاضی کے مذہب کے خلاف نکلا تو قاضی اس کو باطل کر دے گا۔ کیونکہ حکم کا حکم
قاضی پر لازم نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ قاضی کی طرف سے اس کو حکم نہیں بنایا گیا ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ حکم بنانے والے دونوں شخصوں میں سے ہر ایک حکم کے حکم کرنے سے پہلے پہلے حکم بنانے سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار ہے۔ یعنی حکم کے حکم کرنے سے پہلے پہلے دونوں میں سے ہر ایک یہ کہ سکتا ہے کہ اب آپ میرے حکم نہیں ہیں۔ یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔ اور امام مالک کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے۔ اور امام احمد سے ایک روایت یہی ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حکم کو انہیں دونوں کے اتفاق سے مقرر کیا گیا لہذا جب تک یہ دونوں اس کے حکم ہونے پر راضی رہیں گے اس وقت تک وہ حکم اور فیصلہ کرنے کا مجاز ہوگا ۔ اور جب دونوں میں سے کسی ایک نے عدم رضا کا اظہار کر دیا تو وہ ظلم کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہو گا۔ کیونکہ جس کا وجود دو چیزوں سے وابستہ ہوتا ہے اس کے موجود رہنے کے لئے دونوں چیزوں کا موجود ہونا ضروری ہے۔ لیکن اس کے معدوم ہونے کے لئے دونوں چیزوں کا معدوم ہونا ضروری نہیں ہوتا۔ بلکہ اگر دونوں چیزوں میں سے ایک چیز بھی معدوم ہوگئی تو وہ شئی معدوم ہو جاتی ہے۔ پس اسی وجہ سے کہا گیا ہے کہ حکم کے حکم کو باقی رہنے کے لئے دونوں شخصوں کا راضی رہنا ضروری ہے اور
The parties who appointed the arbitrator have the right to revoke the arbitration. And each of the two parties (who appointed the arbitrator) has the right to revoke (the arbitration) as long as he has not ruled upon them, because he is a delegate from them, so he cannot rule except with the consent of both of them. And when he rules, it becomes binding upon them because his ruling issues from his authority over them. And if his ruling is presented to the qadi, and it agrees with his (the qadi's) madhhab, he enforces it, because there is no benefit in overturning it and then re-establishing it in that manner. And if it contradicts his madhhab, he nullifies it, because his ruling is not binding upon him due to the absence of his appointment. Translation: And each of the two persons who appointed the arbitrator has the right to revoke the appointment before the arbitrator has issued a ruling on them, because he has been appointed by them. Therefore, he cannot issue a ruling without the consent of both of them. And when the arbitrator has ruled, it becomes binding on them, because his ruling issues from his authority over them. And if the arbitrator's ruling is presented to the qadi and it is in accordance with his madhhab, the qadi will enforce it, because there is no benefit in overturning it and then re-establishing it in that manner. And if the arbitrator's ruling contradicts the qadi's madhhab, the qadi will nullify it, because the arbitrator's ruling is not binding on the qadi, since the qadi did not appoint him. Explanation: Ṣāḥib Qudūrī said that each of the two parties who appointed the arbitrator has the right to revoke the appointment before the arbitrator rules. That is, before the arbitrator passes his ruling, each of them can say, 'You are no longer my arbitrator.' This is one saying of Imam al-Shafi'i, and one narration from Imam Malik, and one narration from Imam Ahmad. The evidence is that the arbitrator was appointed by the agreement of both; therefore, as long as both are satisfied with him being their arbitrator, he is authorized to rule and decide. And when one of them expresses dissatisfaction, he is no longer authorized to rule, because something whose existence depends on two things requires both to exist for its continuation, but for its cessation, it does not require both to cease; if one ceases, the thing ceases. Therefore, it is said that for the arbitrator's ruling to remain, the consent of both parties is necessary.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage discusses a key rule of arbitration in Hanafi fiqh: the right of the parties to revoke the arbitrator before a ruling is issued. The text begins with the Arabic matn: 'Each of the two parties has the right to revoke as long as he has not ruled upon them.' The reasoning is that the arbitrator is a delegate (muqallad) from them; his authority is derived solely from their consent. Therefore, as long as no ruling has been given, either party can withdraw consent, and the arbitrator loses jurisdiction. Once a ruling is given, it becomes binding on both parties because it is issued from the authority they granted. If the ruling is brought before a qadi, the qadi examines it: if it agrees with his own madhhab (Hanafi), he enforces it because there is no benefit in overturning and reissuing a correct ruling. If it contradicts his madhhab, he nullifies it because the arbitrator's ruling is not binding on the qadi (he did not appoint him). The commentary by Quduri and others explains that this right of revocation before the ruling is agreed upon by Imam Shafi'i, and a narration from Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. The logical proof (dalil aqli) is that the arbitrator's authority depends on the ongoing consent of both parties; consent of both is required for its existence, but withdrawal of one is sufficient to render it void. This rule ensures that arbitration remains consensual. After the ruling, however, the outcome is binding unless it violates the qadi's madhhab, in which case the qadi can nullify it. This shows the interplay between private arbitration and the judicial system: the arbitrator's decision is final for the parties but subject to review by the state qadi.

Key Terms
رجوع (rujūʿ): The act of one party revoking the arbitration appointment before the arbitrator issues a ruling.
مقلد (muqallad): The arbitrator is a 'delegate' appointed by the parties; he acts on their behalf and with their consent.
إمضاء (imḍāʾ): The qadi's enforcement of the arbitrator's ruling if it aligns with his madhhab.
إبطال (ibṭāl): The qadi's nullification of the arbitrator's ruling if it contradicts his madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition can a qadi enforce an arbitrator's ruling?
A) The arbitrator was a close relative of the qadi.
B) The arbitrator's ruling agrees with the qadi's own madhhab.
C) The parties appointed the arbitrator in writing.
D) The arbitrator issued the ruling in the qadi's court.

Key Takeaway
The arbitrator's authority is conditional on the ongoing consent of both parties; revocation before the ruling ends that authority instantly, and the qadi has discretion to enforce or nullify the ruling based on his madhhab.

Who Can Be Appointed as Arbitrator? Condition of Testimony Capacity
States disqualifications and exceptions for arbitrator appointment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the qualifications required for an arbitrator in Hanafi fiqh and apply the exception for a fasiq arbitrator.

Core Idea
An arbitrator must be qualified to testify; lacking that, appointment is invalid, but a fasiq's enforced ruling is upheld.

This passage from the Hidayah discusses who can serve as an arbitrator (hakam) and the legal effect of appointing someone unqualified. The general rule is that an arbitrator must have the same capacity as a witness (shahadah). However, the text also addresses two exceptions: a dhimmi among dhimmis and a fasiq whose appointment is valid if it actually occurs. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on the functionality of rulings over procedural perfection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The text states that those who lack 'capability of testimony' cannot be arbitrators because they cannot be judges. Identify the specific category of persons listed as disqualified.
The disqualifying factor is the absence of shahadah qualification.
2
Examine the exceptions
Two exceptions are provided: a dhimmi appointed by dhimmis (valid) and a fasiq if actually appointed (his ruling is effective). Note the reasoning behind each exception.
The dhimmi exception is based on mutual testimony among dhimmis; the fasiq exception follows the rule for a fasiq judge.
3
Connect the rulings on fasiq judge and fasiq arbitrator
The Hidayah author (Al-Marghinani) explicitly links the ruling for a fasiq arbitrator to the earlier ruling in Kitab Adab al-Qadi about a fasiq judge. Understand that the same logic applies: the appointment is discouraged but if it happens, it is valid and the rulings are enforced.
This shows the consistency of Hanafi methodology across chapters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقرر کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ پس اسی وجہ سے کا فرکو ، غلام کو ذمی کو محدود فی القذف کو ، فاسق کو اور نابالغ کو حکم مقرر کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مذکورہ اشخاص میں چونکہ شہادت کی لیاقت موجود نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے مذکورہ اشخاص قاضی نہیں ہو سکتے اور جب قاضی نہیں ہو سکتے تو حکم بھی نہیں ہو سکتے ہیں۔ لیکن ذمّی کو حکم مقرر کرنا اُس وقت نا جائز ہے جب اس کو مسلمانوں نے حکم مقرر کیا ہو۔ اور اگر ذمیوں نے کسی ذمّی کو حکم مقرر کیا تو یہ جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ذمی ، مسلمانوں کے حق میں اگر چہ اہل شہادت میں سے نہیں ہے لیکن اہل ذمہ کے حق میں شہادت کا اہل ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اگر فاسق کو حکم مقرر کر دیا گیا تو ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہونا چاہئے جیسے کتاب ادب القاضی کے شروع میں گذرا کہ فاسق کو قاضی نہ بنانا چاہئے لیکن اگر بنا دیا گیا تو جائز ہے۔ اور اس کا حکم قضاء نافذ ہوگا۔ اسی طرح اگر فاسق کو حکم مقرر کر دیا گیا تو بھی جائز ہونا چاہئے ۔
It can be appointed. So for this reason, appointing a disbeliever, a slave, a dhimmi, one who is hadd-limited for qadhf, a fasiq, and a minor as an arbitrator is not permissible. Because the mentioned persons do not possess the capability of testimony. For this reason, they cannot be judges, and when they cannot be judges, they also cannot be arbitrators. But appointing a dhimmi as an arbitrator is impermissible when Muslims have appointed him. And if dhimmis appointed a dhimmi as arbitrator, it will be permissible. Because a dhimmi, although not from among those eligible for testimony regarding Muslims, is eligible for testimony regarding the dhimmis. The author of Hidayah said: 'If a fasiq is appointed as an arbitrator, in our view it should be permissible, just as passed earlier in the beginning of Kitab Adab al-Qadi that a fasiq should not be made a judge, but if he is made, it is permissible. And his judicial ruling will be effective. Similarly, if a fasiq is appointed as an arbitrator, it should also be permissible.'
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage states the conditions for appointing an arbitrator (hakam) in Hanafi fiqh. The general principle is that an arbitrator must have the same qualifications as a witness (shahadah) because arbitration is a form of judgment that requires reliability. Therefore, those who are not qualified to testify cannot be arbitrators: a disbeliever (kafir), a slave (ghulam), a dhimmi (when appointing over Muslims), a person subject to hadd for false accusation (mahdud fi al-qadhf), a fasiq (open sinner), and a minor. However, there are exceptions: a dhimmi can serve as arbitrator among dhimmis because he is eligible for testimony among them. Also, following the ruling about a fasiq judge mentioned earlier in Kitab Adab al-Qadi, if a fasiq is actually appointed as an arbitrator, his rulings are enforceable and the appointment is considered valid, though it is recommended not to appoint him initially.

Key Terms
حَکَم (hakam): arbitrator appointed by disputing parties to resolve their conflict
شہادت (shahadah): legal testimony; capacity to testify in court
فاسق (fasiq): a person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking moral integrity

6 min
Parties' Right to Revoke Arbitrator Before Ruling
Discusses revocation, binding effect, and qadi review of arbitration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule regarding revocation of an arbitrator’s authority and explain the binding nature of his ruling after issuance, including the qadi’s role in review.

Core Idea
An arbitrator's authority depends on mutual consent; it ends when one party withdraws before a ruling, but becomes binding once the ruling is issued.

This lesson examines the legal framework of arbitration (tahkim) in Hanafi fiqh. The key issue is the balance between party autonomy and finality of decisions. The Hanafi school, supported by other leading Imams, holds that each party can revoke the arbitrator's mandate at any time before a ruling is given, but once the ruling is delivered, it becomes binding and cannot be revoked.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on revocation before ruling
Identify the rule: each party can revoke the arbitrator’s authority as long as no ruling has been issued. This is because the arbitrator is a delegate (muqallid) from both parties and his authority exists only by their consent.
The act of revocation is a unilateral withdrawal of consent.
2
Explain the rational basis for the rule
The commentator provides a logical argument: the existence of the arbitrator's authority requires both parties' consent; its termination requires only one party's withdrawal. This is analogous to any two-factor condition.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) used by the Hanafis.
3
Identify the post-ruling binding effect
Once the arbitrator issues a ruling, it becomes binding on both parties and cannot be revoked. The ruling has authority over them at the moment of issuance, similar to a qadi's ruling even if he is later dismissed.
This is agreed upon by Shafi’i, Maliki, and Hanbali narrations.
4
Describe the qadi’s role in reviewing the arbitrator's ruling
If the arbitrator's ruling is presented to a qadi, the qadi will enforce it if it agrees with his own madhhab. If it contradicts his madhhab, he will nullify it because the arbitrator’s ruling is not binding on the qadi (who did not appoint him).
Once the qadi enforces it, a later qadi cannot overturn it.
5
Note the practical implications and cross-madhhab agreement
The Hanafi position is supported by Imam Shafi’i (one qawl), Imam Malik (one narration), and Imam Ahmad (one narration). The practical effect: a party cannot withdraw after the ruling, and the arbitrator's decision is final subject to qadi review.
There is no fundamental ikhtilaf among the cited Imams on these points.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حکم بنانے والوں کو حکم سے رجوع کا اختیار ہے

ولكل واحد من المحكمين ان يرجع مالم يحكم عليهما لانه مقلد من جهتهما فلا يحكم الا برضاهما جميعاً واذا حكم لزمهما لصدور حكمه عن ولايه عليهما واذا رفع حكمه الى القاضى فوافق مذهبه امضاه لانه لا فائدة في نقضه ثم في إبرامه على ذلك الوجه و ان خالفه ابطله لان حكمه لا يلزمه لعدم التحكيم منه

ترجمہ اور حکم بنانے والے دونوں شخصوں میں سے ہر ایک کو حکم بنانے سے رجوع کا اختیار ہے جب تک کہ حکم نے ان پر حکم صادر نہ کیا ہو۔ اسلئے کہ اس کو ان دونوں کی طرف سے حکم مقرر کیا گیا ہے۔ لہذا وہ بغیر ان دونوں کی رضا مندی کے حکم صادر نہیں کر سکے گا۔ اور جب حکم نے حکم کر دیا تو ان دونوں پر لازم ہو گا۔ کیوں کہ ان دونوں پر ولایت حاصل ہو کر اس کا حکم صادر ہوا ہے۔ اور حکم کے حکم کا مرافعہ قاضی کے پاس کیا گیا اور وہ حکم اس کے مذہب کے موافق نکلا تو قاضی اس کو نافذ کرے گا۔ کیوں کہ اس کے حکم کو توڑ کر پھر اُسی طور پر مضبوط کرنے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر حکم کا حکم قاضی کے مذہب کے خلاف نکلا تو قاضی اس کو باطل کر دے گا۔ کیونکہ حکم کا حکم قاضی پر لازم نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ قاضی کی طرف سے اس کو حکم نہیں بنایا گیا ہے۔

تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ حکم بنانے والے دونوں شخصوں میں سے ہر ایک حکم کے حکم کرنے سے پہلے پہلے حکم بنانے سے رجوع کرنے کا اختیار ہے۔ یعنی حکم کے حکم کرنے سے پہلے پہلے دونوں میں سے ہر ایک یہ کہ سکتا ہے کہ اب آپ میرے حکم نہیں ہیں۔ یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔ اور امام مالک کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے۔ اور امام احمد سے ایک روایت یہی ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حکم کو انہیں دونوں کے اتفاق سے مقرر کیا گیا لہذا جب تک یہ دونوں اس کے حکم ہونے پر راضی رہیں گے اس وقت تک وہ حکم اور فیصلہ کرنے کا مجاز ہوگا ۔ اور جب دونوں میں سے کسی ایک نے عدم رضا کا اظہار کر دیا تو وہ ظلم کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہو گا۔ کیونکہ جس کا وجود دو چیزوں سے وابستہ ہوتا ہے اس کے موجود رہنے کے لئے دونوں چیزوں کا موجود ہونا ضروری ہے۔ لیکن اس کے معدوم ہونے کے لئے دونوں چیزوں کا معدوم ہونا ضروری نہیں ہوتا۔ بلکہ اگر دونوں چیزوں میں سے ایک چیز بھی معدوم ہوگئی تو وہ شئی معدوم ہو جاتی ہے۔ پس اسی وجہ سے کہا گیا ہے کہ حکم کے حکم کو باقی رہنے کے لئے دونوں شخصوں کا راضی رہنا ضروری ہے اور اس کے حکم ہونے کو ختم کرنے کے لئے ایک کا ناراض ہونا بھی کافی ہے۔ صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ اگر حکم نے کوئی حکم صادر کر دیا تو حکم کا یہ حکم لازم ہوگا ۔ اور فریقین میں سے کسی کو انحراف کا حق نہ ہوگا ۔ جیسے قاضی نے اگر کوئی فیصلہ کیا پھر سلطان نے اس کو معزول کر دیا تو قاضی کا یہ فیصلہ نافذ اور لازم ہوتا ہے۔ یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔ اور امام مالک اور امام احمد کا مذہب یہی ہے کیونکہ حکم نے جس وقت حکم دیا ہے اس وقت اس کو دونوں پر ولایت حاصل تھی۔ اور صاحب ولایت کا حکم چونکہ لازم ہوتا ہے اس لئے حکم کا مذکورہ حکم بھی لازم ہوگا ۔

صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر حکم کے حکم کا قاضی کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا اور یہ حکم قاضی کے مذہب کے موافق ہو تو قاضی حکم کے حکم کو نافذ کرے گا۔ کیونکہ حکم کے حکم کو توڑ کر پھر اسی طرح پر اس کو مضبوط کرنے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ یعنی اس میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے کہ قاضی پہلے حکم کے حکم کو توڑے اور پھر اپنی طرف سے وہی حکم صادر کرے۔ اور قاضی کی عدالت میں مرافعہ کرنے سے یہ فائدہ ہوگا کہ جب قاضی نے حکم کے حکم کو نافذ کر دیا پھر کسی ایسے قاضی کی عدالت میں مرافعہ ہوا جس کے مذہب کے یہ حکم موافق نہیں ہے تو یہ دوسرا قاضی اس کو توڑنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ سابق میں گذر چکا کہ اگر کسی مسئلہ مجتہد فیہ کو ایک قاضی نے نافذ کر دیا تو دوسرا قاضی جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے اس کو توڑنے کا مجاز نہیں ہوتا۔ اور اگر حکم کا حکم اس قاضی کے مذہب کے مخالف ہے جس کی عدالت میں مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے تو قاضی حکم کے حکم کو باطل کر دے۔ کیونکہ حکم کا حکم قاضی پر لازم نہیں ہے۔ اور قاضی پر حکم کے حکم کا لازم نہ ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ قاضی کی طرف سے اس کو حکم بنانا نہیں پایا گیا۔ اور یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی ہے کہ حکم کا حکم اس پر لازم ہوتا ہے جس نے اس کو حکم بنایا ہو۔ اس کے علاوہ پر لازم نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے حکم کا یہ حکم قاضی پر لازم نہ ہو گا۔
Each of the two arbitrators has the right to revoke as long as he has not ruled against them, because he is a delegate from their side, so he only rules with the consent of both. When he rules, it becomes binding on them because his ruling is issued with authority over them. If his ruling is referred to the qadi and it agrees with his madhhab, he enforces it because there is no benefit in revoking it and then confirming it in that manner. And if it contradicts his madhhab, he invalidates it because his ruling is not binding on him due to the lack of arbitration from him. ... (full translation of the Urdu commentary follows in the original).
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage covers three aspects of arbitration (tahkim). First, the right of revocation: each party can revoke the arbitrator's authority before he issues a ruling. This is because the arbitrator's authority is derived from their mutual consent. If one party withdraws consent, the authority ends. This is agreed by Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Imam Malik and Ahmad. Second, once the arbitrator issues a ruling, it becomes binding on both parties and cannot be revoked, similar to a qadi's ruling even if he is later dismissed. Third, when the arbitrator's ruling is presented to a qadi: if it agrees with the qadi's own madhhab, he enforces it to avoid futility. If it disagrees, he nullifies it because the arbitrator's ruling is not binding on the qadi (the qadi did not appoint him). However, if the qadi enforces it, then a later qadi of a different madhhab cannot overturn it because it has been upheld by a valid court decision. The commentary also notes that arbitration is permissible in all ijtihad matters like talaq and nikah, but fatwa is not given on this to prevent common people from overstepping.

Key Terms
تحکیم (tahkim): arbitration; the process of appointing a private arbitrator to resolve a dispute
رجوع (ruju'): revocation; the act of withdrawing consent from the arbitrator
مقلد (muqallid): delegate; the arbitrator is a delegate of the parties, not a qadi

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can a party revoke the arbitrator's authority?
A) At any time before or after the ruling
B) Only before the ruling
C) Only after the ruling
D) Never, once the arbitrator is appointed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an arbitrator's authority is revocable unilaterally before the ruling, but the ruling becomes binding and final once issued, subject only to a qadi's review if it contradicts his madhhab.

Arbitration Prohibited in Hudud and Qisas
Prohibition of arbitration in hudud and qisas with rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of arbitration in hudud and qisas, explain the rationale based on lack of authority over blood, and apply the ruling to related cases including mistaken killing.

Core Idea
Arbitration in hudud and qisas is prohibited because parties have no authority over their own blood.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a fundamental limit on arbitration (tahkim) in Islamic law: it is not permitted in cases involving fixed punishments (hudud) or retributive justice (qisas). The core reason is that the parties, whether victims or their heirs, have no legal authority over the blood of the accused—these are rights of Allah or the community. Understanding this principle is crucial for distinguishing which disputes can be resolved through private arbitration and which must be decided by a qadi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the opening statement: arbitration is not permissible in hudud and qisas. Recognize that this is a prohibition.
Hudud are fixed punishments; qisas is retaliatory justice for killing/injury.
2
Trace the rationale
Find the reason given: 'because they have no authority over their own blood.' Understand that parties cannot authorize what they do not own.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli): blood cannot be made permissible by consent.
3
Examine the inference for other matters
Note that specifying hudud and qisas implies arbitration is allowed in other ijtihad matters (e.g., divorce, marriage). Understand the caveat: fatwa is not given on this permissibility to prevent common people's audacity.
This is a key practical restriction despite logical permissibility.
4
Analyze the case of mistaken killing
Consider the example: if an arbitrator rules diyah on the 'aqilah or the killer, his ruling is not enforced if it contradicts the textual rule. Identify why the qadi rejects it.
The 'aqilah is liable in accidental killing; the qadi's opinion and text prevail.
5
Note the exception for confession
Recognize that if the killing is proven by the killer's own confession, the 'aqilah does not pay, and the arbitrator's ruling against the killer's wealth may stand.
Confession changes liability: 'aqilah not responsible for confession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حدود و قصاص میں تحکیم جائز نہیں

ولا يجوز التحكيم فى الحدود والقصاص لانه لا ولاية لهما على دمهما ولهذا لا يملكان الا باحة فلا يستباح برضاهما قالوا و تخصيص الحدود والقصاص يدل على جواز التحكيم في سائر المجتهدات كالطلاق والنكاح وغيرهما وهو صحيح الا انه لا يفتى به ويقال يحتاج الى حكم المولى دفعاً لتجاسر العوام فيه وان حكماه في دم خطأ فقضى بالدية على العاقلة لم ينفذ حكمه لانه لا ولاية له عليهم اذ لا تحكيم من جهتهم ولو حكم على القاتل بالدية فى ماله رده القاضى ويقضى بالدية على العاقلة لانه مخالف لرأيه ومخالف للنص ايضاً الا اذا ثبت القتل باقراره لان العاقلة لا تعقله

ترجمہ اور حدود و قصاص میں حکم بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں کی ولایت اپنے خون پر نہیں ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے چونکہ دونوں خون مبارح کرنے کے مالک نہیں ہیں۔ تو ان کی رضامندی سے بھی خون مباح نہ ہو گا۔ مشائخ نے کہا کہ حدود قصاص کی تخصیص کرنا تمام مجاہدات ، طلاق ، نکاح وغیرہ میں حکم بنانے کے جواز پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ اور یہی صحیح ہے مگر یہ کہ اس پر فتویٰ نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ اور کہدیا جائے گا کہ اس میں قاضی کے حکم کی ضرورت ہے تا کہ اس میں عوام کی دلیری دور ہو۔ اور اگر دو آدمیوں نے قتل خطا میں اس کو حکم بنایا۔ پس
Arbitration is not permissible in hudud and qisas because they have no authority over their own blood, and therefore they do not possess the right to permit it, so the blood is not made permissible by their consent. They said: specifying hudud and qisas indicates the permissibility of arbitration in all other ijtihad matters like divorce, marriage, etc., and this is correct, except that fatwa is not given on it, and it is said that the ruler's judgment is needed to prevent the audacity of common people in it. And if they appointed him as arbitrator in a case of mistaken killing and he ruled for diyah on the 'aqilah, his ruling is not executed because he has no authority over them since there is no arbitration from their side. And if he ruled for diyah from the killer's own wealth, the qadi rejects it and rules for diyah on the 'aqilah because it contradicts his opinion and also contradicts the text, unless the killing is proven by the killer's confession because the 'aqilah do not pay for a confession. And if two men appointed him as arbitrator in mistaken killing... then
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage establishes that arbitration (tahkim) is not valid in cases of hudud (fixed corporal punishments) and qisas (retributive justice) because the parties have no authority over their own blood—they cannot pardon or permit such punishments. Their consent is irrelevant because these are rights of Allah or the community. The mashayikh note that by specifying these two categories, it implies arbitration is valid in all other matters where ijtihad is possible, such as divorce, marriage, etc. However, they caution that fatwa is not given on this permissibility to prevent common people from overstepping, requiring them to seek the qadi's ruling instead. The passage then discusses a specific case: if two parties appoint an arbitrator in a case of mistaken killing (qatl khata') and he rules that the 'aqilah (tribal group) must pay diyah, his ruling is not enforced because the 'aqilah were not parties to the arbitration. If he rules that the killer must pay diyah from his own wealth, the qadi rejects it and rules against the 'aqilah because it contradicts his own opinion and the textual ruling. An exception is made if the killer confesses, because then the 'aqilah are not liable for a confession. The text ends abruptly with a new case about two men appointing an arbitrator in mistaken killing.

Key Terms
حدود (hudud): fixed corporal punishments for crimes like theft, zina, etc.
قصاص (qisas): retributive justice for intentional killing or injury
دية (diyah): blood money paid to the victim's family
تحكيم (tahkim): arbitration, appointment of a private judge by disputing parties

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is arbitration not allowed in hudud and qisas according to this passage?
A) Because the parties are not qualified to be arbitrators
B) Because the parties have no authority over their own blood
C) Because the qadi must always decide these cases
D) Because these cases require a jury

Key Takeaway
Arbitration is invalid in hudud and qisas because the parties have no authority over blood; for other matters, it is theoretically permissible but fatwa discourages it to prevent misuse.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
The Binding Effect of an Arbitrator’s Ruling and Its Enforcement by a Qadi
Explains the binding nature of a hakam's ruling and its enforcement by a qadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the binding effect of a hakam's ruling on the parties and identify when a qadi must enforce or nullify the ruling based on madhhab compatibility.

Core Idea
A hakam’s ruling binds the parties; a qadi enforces it only if it agrees with his madhhab.

In Hanafi fiqh, an arbitrator (hakam) appointed by disputing parties has binding authority over them. But what happens when that ruling is brought before a state-appointed judge (qadi)? This lesson, based on the text of al-Quduri and its commentary, clarifies the scope of the hakam’s ruling and the qadi’s duty to either enforce it or nullify it depending on whether it aligns with the qadi’s own madhhab. The passage also highlights the agreement of other major imams on the binding nature of the hakam’s decision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and authority of the hakam
Recognize that a hakam is appointed by the disputing parties and, at the time of ruling, has authority over them. This authority is the basis for the binding nature of his decision.
The hakam is not a state-appointed qadi; his authority comes from the parties' agreement.
2
Understand the analogy with a qadi's ruling
The passage compares the hakam's ruling to a qadi's ruling that remains binding even after the qadi is dismissed. This analogy reinforces the idea that the hakam's ruling cannot be revoked by the parties.
The dismissal of the qadi does not nullify his past rulings; similarly, the end of the hakam's appointment does not affect his already-issued ruling.
3
Distinguish binding effect on parties vs. on a qadi
The hakam's ruling is binding on the parties who appointed him, but it is not automatically binding on any qadi. A qadi who did not appoint the hakam is not obligated to accept the ruling.
This distinction is crucial: the ruling binds the parties, but the qadi's enforcement depends on his own madhhab.
4
Apply the rule: qadi's enforcement based on madhhab
If the ruling is referred to a qadi, he enforces it if it matches his madhhab; if it contradicts his madhhab, he nullifies it. The passage explains why: there is no benefit in breaking and reissuing the same ruling, and the qadi is not bound by a ruling from a hakam he did not appoint.
Once a qadi enforces it, no other qadi can overturn it, even if they disagree with the madhhab.
5
Note the benefit of referral
The benefit of referring the hakam's ruling to a qadi is to secure finality: after the qadi enforces it, it cannot be challenged in another court on matters of ijtihad.
This prevents endless litigation and gives the ruling stability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ اگر حکم نے کوئی حکم صادر کر دیا تو حکم کا یہ حکم لازم ہوگا ۔ اور فریقین میں سے کسی کو انحراف کا حق نہ ہوگا ۔ جیسے قاضی نے اگر کوئی فیصلہ کیا پھر سلطان نے اس کو معزول کر دیا تو قاضی کا یہ فیصلہ نافذ اور لازم ہوتا ہے۔ یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔ اور امام مالک اور امام احمد کا مذہب یہی ہے کیونکہ حکم نے جس وقت حکم دیا ہے اس وقت اس کو دونوں پر ولایت حاصل تھی۔ اور صاحب ولایت کا حکم چونکہ لازم ہوتا ہے اس لئے حکم کا مذکورہ حکم بھی لازم ہوگا ۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر حکم کے ظلم کا قاضی کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا اور یہ حکم قاضی کے مذہب کے موافق ہو تو قاضی حکم کے حکم کو نافذ کرے گا۔ کیونکہ حکم کے حکم کو توڑ کر پھر اسی طرح پر اس کو مضبوط کرنے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ یعنی اس میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے کہ قاضی پہلے حکم کے حکم کو توڑے اور پھر اپنی طرف سے وہی حکم صادر کرے۔ اور قاضی کی عدالت میں مرافعہ کرنے سے یہ فائدہ ہوگا کہ جب قاضی نے حکم کے حکم کو نافذ کر دیا پھر کسی ایسے قاضی کی عدالت میں مرافعہ ہوا جس کے مذہب کے یہ حکم موافق نہیں ہے تو یہ دوسرا قاضی اس کو توڑنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ سابق میں گذر چکا کہ اگر کسی مسئلہ مجتہد فیہ کو ایک قاضی نے نافذ کر دیا تو دوسرا قاضی جس کے پاس مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے اس کو توڑنے کا مجاز نہیں ہوتا۔ اور اگر حکم کا حکم اس قاضی کے مذہب کے مخالف ہے جس کی عدالت میں مرافعہ کیا گیا ہے تو قاضی حکم کے حکم کو باطل کر دے۔ کیونکہ حکم کا حکم قاضی پر لازم نہیں ہے۔ اور قاضی پر حکم کے حکم کا لازم نہ ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ قاضی کی طرف سے اس کو حکم بنانا نہیں پایا گیا۔ اور یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی ہے کہ حکم کا حکم اس پر لازم ہوتا ہے جس نے اس کو حکم بنایا ہو۔ اس کے علاوہ پر لازم نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے حکم کا یہ حکم قاضی پر لازم نہ ہو گا۔
Sahib al-Quduri says: If a hakam issues a ruling, then that ruling of the hakam is binding. And neither of the two parties has the right to deviate from it. Just as if a qadi makes a decision, then the sultan dismisses him, the qadi's decision is still effective and binding. This is also one saying of Imam al-Shafi'i, and the madhhab of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad is the same, because when the hakam gave the ruling, he had authority over both parties at that time. And since the ruling of one with authority is binding, therefore the mentioned ruling of the hakam will also be binding. Sahib al-Quduri states: If the hakam's oppression is referred to a qadi, and this ruling is in accordance with the qadi's madhhab, then the qadi will enforce the hakam's ruling. Because there is no benefit in breaking the hakam's ruling and then strengthening it in the same way — that is, there is no benefit in the qadi first breaking the hakam's ruling and then issuing the same ruling from himself. And the benefit of referring to the qadi's court is that when the qadi enforces the hakam's ruling, then if it is later referred to the court of another qadi whose madhhab does not agree with this ruling, that second qadi will not be permitted to break it. Because it has passed earlier that if a qadi enforces a ruling in a matter of ijtihad, another qadi to whom it is referred is not permitted to break it. And if the hakam's ruling is contrary to the madhhab of the qadi in whose court it is referred, then the qadi will nullify the hakam's ruling. Because the hakam's ruling is not binding upon the qadi. And the reason the hakam's ruling is not binding upon the qadi is that the qadi did not appoint him as hakam. And this matter has passed earlier: the hakam's ruling is binding upon the one who appointed him as hakam, and is not binding upon others. Therefore, this ruling of the hakam will not be binding upon the qadi.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Sahib al-Quduri, expanded by the commentator. It addresses the effect of an arbitrator's (hakam's) ruling when it is brought before a qadi. The passage first establishes that a hakam's ruling is binding on the parties who appointed him, using the analogy of a qadi's ruling remaining binding even after dismissal. This is supported by the fact that at the time of ruling, the hakam had authority (wilaya) over the parties. Then it discusses two scenarios when the ruling is referred to a qadi: (1) If the ruling agrees with the qadi's madhhab, the qadi enforces it directly without reissuing it, because breaking and remaking the same ruling is pointless. (2) If the ruling disagrees with the qadi's madhhab, the qadi nullifies it because the hakam's ruling is not binding on the qadi who did not appoint him. The passage also notes that once a qadi enforces a ruling, it cannot be overturned by another qadi in matters of ijtihad.

Key Terms
حَکَم (ḥakam): An arbitrator appointed by the parties to settle a dispute; not a state-appointed qadi.
مَرَافَعَة (murāfaʿah): Referring a case to a qadi for review or enforcement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hakam's ruling is brought before a qadi whose madhhab disagrees with it, what should the qadi do?
A) Enforce the ruling as long as it is valid
B) Nullify the ruling because it is not binding on him
C) Refer the case to another qadi
D) Issue a new ruling from himself

Key Takeaway
A hakam's ruling binds the parties; a qadi enforces it only if it matches his madhhab, otherwise nullifies it.

Prohibition of Arbitration in Hudud and Qisas
States the ruling and discusses different madhhab positions on tahkim in hudud and qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the impermissibility of arbitration (tahkim) in hudud and qisas, identify the key proof (dalil), and evaluate the opposing views of al-Sarakhsi and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
You cannot arbitrate over your own life – lack of authority over blood makes consent meaningless in hudud and qisas.

Arbitration (tahkim) is a common tool for dispute resolution, but in Islamic criminal law, its scope is limited. This lesson examines why the Hanafi school, following Imam al-Khassaf, prohibits arbitration in cases involving fixed punishments (hudud) and retaliation (qisas). We will analyze the legal reasoning, the evidence from lack of authority over one's blood, and the practical implications of the dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: Tahkim is not permissible in hudud (rights of Allah) and qisas (rights of the individual over blood).
The passage opens with this ruling directly.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (al-Sarakhsi allows it in qadhf and qisas) and the Shafi'i position (only in property matters).
Other schools: Malik and Ahmad also have positions.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand al-Sarakhsi's argument: the right belongs to the individual (heirs), so they can delegate. Al-Shafi'i argues these matters require caution and a qadi's ruling.
The passage mentions these proofs in the commentary.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is based on lack of wilaya over one's blood; rights of Allah cannot be delegated.
Also, the hakam's ruling creates shubha (doubt), which waives hudud.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: a hakam's ruling in hudud/qisas is unenforceable; in other matters it is valid but fatwa discourages it to prevent chaos.
The passage explicitly says 'fatwa is not given on it'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حدود و قصاص میں تحکیم جائز نہیں
ولا يجوز التحكيم فى الحدود والقصاص لانه لا ولاية لهما على دمهما ولهذا لا يملكان الا باحة فلا يستباح برضاهما قالوا و تخصيص الحدود والقصاص يدل على جواز التحكيم في سائر المجتهدات كالطلاق والنكاح وغيرهما وهو صحيح الا انه لا يفتى به ويقال يحتاج الى حكم المولى دفعاً لتجاسر العوام فيه وان حكماه في دم خطأ فقضى بالدية على العاقلة لم ينفذ حكمه لانه لا ولاية له عليهم اذ لا تحكيم من جهتهم ولو حكم على القاتل بالدية فى ماله رده القاضى ويقضى بالدية على العاقلة لانه مخالف لرأيه ومخالف للنص ايضاً الا اذا ثبت القتل باقراره لان العاقلة لا تعقله

ترجمہ اور حدود و قصاص میں حکم بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں کی ولایت اپنے خون پر نہیں ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے چونکہ دونوں خون مبارح کرنے کے مالک نہیں ہیں۔ تو ان کی رضامندی سے بھی خون مباح نہ ہو گا۔ مشائخ نے کہا کہ حدود قصاص کی تخصیص کرنا تمام مجاہدات ، طلاق ، نکاح وغیرہ میں حکم بنانے کے جواز پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ اور یہی صحیح ہے مگر یہ کہ اس پر فتویٰ نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ اور کہدیا جائے گا کہ اس میں قاضی کے حکم کی ضرورت ہے تا کہ اس میں عوام کی دلیری دور ہو۔ اور اگر دو آدمیوں نے قتل خطا میں اس کو حکم بنایا۔ پس

اس نے عاقلہ پر دیت کا فیصلہ دیا تو اس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ عاقلہ پر اس کی ولایت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کی طرف سے حکم بنانا نہیں پایا گیا۔ اور اگر حکم نے قاتل پر اس کے ذاتی مال میں دیت کا حکم دیا تو قاضی اس کو رد کر دے گا۔ اور عاقلہ پر دیت کا حکم دے گا کیونکہ یہ قاضی کی رائے کے خلاف ہے۔ اور نص کے بھی خلاف ہے مگر جب قاتل کے اقرار سے قتل ثابت ہوا ہو کیونکہ عاقلہ اس دیت کو برداشت نہیں کریں گے۔

تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ حدود و قصاص میں حکم بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہمارے علمائے احناف میں یہ مذہب امام خصاف کا ہے۔ اس کو شیخ ابوالحسن قدوری اور صاحب ہدایہ نے اختیار کیا ہے۔ لیکن یہاں حدود سے وہ حدود مراد ہیں جو خالصہ اللہ جل شانہ کا حق ہیں جیسے حد زنا اور حد شرب خمر شمس الائمہ سرخسی نے کہا کہ حد قذف اور قصاص میں حکم بنانا جائز ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اموال اور اموال کے ہم معنی چیزوں میں حکم بنانا جائز ہے۔ لیکن ان کے علاوہ میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس کے قائل امام مالک ہیں۔ حتی کہ حد، لعان، قصاص، قذف ، نسب، ولاء چونکہ نہ مال ہیں اور نہ مال کے ہم معنی ہیں ۔ اس لئے ان میں حکم بنانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ تمام چیزیں چونکہ احتیاط پربنی ہیں اس لئے ان میں فیصلہ صادر کرنے کے لئے قاضی متعین ہوگا۔ حکم کا فیصلہ کافی نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب حکم کا فیصلہ کافی نہیں ہے تو ان میں حکم بنانا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ شمس الائمہ سرخسی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حد قذف اور قصاص کے وصول کرنے کا حق چونکہ مقذوف علیہ اور اولیاء مقتول کو ہے۔ یعنی حد قذف اور قصاص یہ دونوں حقوق العباد میں سے ہیں اس لئے قاذف اور مقذوف علیہ اور قاتل اور اولیاء مقتول کو حکم مقرر کرنے کا حق بھی حاصل ہوگا۔ اور امام خصاف کے مذہب یعنی حدود و قصاص میں حکم مقرر کرنے کے عدمِ جواز پر دلیل یہ ہے کہ حکم مقرر کرنے والوں کو اپنی جان اور خون پر کوئی ولایت حاصل نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ کسی کو اپنا خون مباح کرنے کا اختیار نہیں دیا گیا۔ پس جب کسی کو اپنی جان اور خون پر ولایت حاصل نہیں ہے اور اپنا خون مباح کرنے کا اختیار نہیں دیا گیا تو ان کی رضامندی سے ان کا خون مباح نہ ہو گا۔ اور جب رضامندی کے باوجود اپنا خون مباح نہیں ہوا تو قصاص (خون بہانے کے لئے ) کسی کو حکم مقرر کرنا بھی جائز اور مباح نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب، عنایہ نے فرمایا کہ صاحب ہدایہ کی بیان کردہ یہ دلیل قصاص میں حکم مقرر کرنے کے عدم جواز پر تو ہو سکتی ہے لیکن حدود میں حکم مقرر کرنے کے عدم جواز پر نہیں ہوسکتی۔ اس لئے بعض علماء نے دلیل پیش کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ حکم کا حکم چونکہ حکم مقرر کر نے والوں کے علاوہ کے حق میں حجت نہیں ہوتا اس لئے حکم کے حکم میں شبہ ہو گا۔ اور چونکہ حدود و قصاص کو شبہات کے ساتھ وصول نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ اس لئے حکم کے حکم سے حدود و قصاص کو وصول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور جب حکم کے حکم سے حدود و قصاص کو وصول نہیں کیا جا سکتا تو حدود و قصاص میں حکم مقرر کرنا بھی ناجائز ہوگا۔

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مشائخ متاخرین نے فرمایا کہ شیخ ابوالحسن قدوری کا حدود و قصاص کی تخصیص کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ حدود و قصاص کے علاوہ دوسرے تمام مسائل ( طلاق، نکاح وغیرہ) میں حکم مقرر کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور یہی صحیح ہے۔ لیکن اس کا فتویٰ نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ بلکہ یہ کہہ دیا جائے گا کہ اس میں قاضی کے حکم کی ضرورت ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر حکم بنانے کے جواز کا فتویٰ دے دیا گیا تو
Arbitration is not permissible in hudud and qisas. Because they have no authority over their blood, and therefore they do not have ownership of making it permissible. So their blood cannot be made lawful by their consent. They (the scholars) said: Specifying hudud and qisas indicates the permissibility of arbitration in all other matters of ijtihad, such as divorce, marriage, etc. And this is correct, except that fatwa is not given on it, and it will be said: It needs the ruling of the qadi to repel the audacity of the common people in it. If two people appointed him as hakam in a case of erroneous killing, and he ruled that the diyah is upon the 'aqilah, his ruling is not executed because he has no authority over them, as there is no appointment from their side. And if he ruled that the killer pays diyah from his own wealth, the qadi rejects it and gives judgment that diyah is upon the 'aqilah, because it contradicts his opinion and also contradicts the text, except if the killing is established by the killer's confession, because the 'aqilah do not bear it. ... [Translation continues]
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of arbitration (tahkim) in hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). The passage opens with a clear ruling from the Arabic text: tahkim is not allowed in hudud and qisas. The reason is that individuals have no authority (wilaya) over their own lives or blood; thus they cannot agree to make their blood permissible. The commentary first presents the Hanafi position as adopted by Imam al-Khassaf, al-Quduri, and the author of al-Hidayah: tahkim is impermissible in hudud (specifically those that are pure rights of Allah, like zina and drinking) and in qisas. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi differed, allowing tahkim in qadhf (false accusation of zina) and qisas because these are rights of the individual. Imam al-Shafi'i allowed tahkim only in matters of property and what is analogous to property, excluding hudud, li'an, qisas, qadhf, nasab, and wala'. The passage then gives the proofs: al-Shafi'i argues these matters require caution and thus only a state-appointed qadi suffices; al-Sarakhsi argues that the right to demand qisas belongs to the victim's heirs, so they can appoint a hakam; al-Khassaf argues lack of wilaya over one's blood. The text also notes that although the correct view is that tahkim is permissible in non-hudud matters, fatwa is not given on this to prevent misuse, and it is said that a qadi's ruling is needed. Finally, it discusses two cases involving diyah (blood money) for erroneous killing: if the hakam rules against the 'aqilah (tribal guarantors), it is invalid because he lacks authority over them; if he rules against the killer personally, the qadi rejects it and imposes diyah on the 'aqilah, unless the killer confessed, in which case the 'aqilah are not liable.

Key Terms
تَحْكِيم (taḥkīm): Appointing a third party (hakam) to settle a dispute; arbitration.
وِلَايَة (wilāyah): Legal authority to act on behalf of another; here, authority over one's own blood or life.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is arbitration (tahkim) not permissible in hudud and qisas according to the Hanafi position presented in this passage?
A) Because these matters require a qadi appointed by the state
B) Because the parties have no legal authority over their own blood or life
C) Because the hakam cannot be trusted in such serious matters
D) Because the texts explicitly forbid it without exception

Key Takeaway
Tahkim is invalid in hudud and qisas because individuals lack legal authority over their blood, and consent cannot override divine rights.

Arbitration in Hudud and Qisas: A Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tahkim in hudud and qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on private arbitration in hudud, qisas, and other matters, and distinguish the views of Imam al-Khasaf and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi.

Core Idea
Private arbitration is impermissible in hudud and qisas because individuals have no authority over life and blood, yet it is valid in other matters, though fatwa is withheld.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines the contentious issue of private arbitration (tahkim) in Islamic law. It begins with a specific case involving accidental killing and the 'aqila, then moves to the general principle: may parties appoint a private arbitrator to resolve hudud, qisas, or other disputes? The text navigates intra-Hanafi disagreement and cross-madhhab differences, ultimately prescribing a nuanced position that balances permissibility with practical caution.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the introductory scenario with 'aqila
Understand why an arbitrator's ruling against the 'aqila is unenforceable — they did not consent to arbitration. This sets the stage for discussing the limits of arbitration.
The 'aqila is a group of male relatives who pay diyat in accidental killings.
2
Identify the main dispute: is arbitration permissible in hudud and qisas?
State the relied-upon Hanafi position (Imam al-Khasaf) that it is not, and the opposing view of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi that it is for qadhf and qisas.
Hudud here are pure rights of Allah (e.g., zina, drinking).
3
Trace the proofs for each position
Examine the three main arguments: Khasaf's (no authority over life), Sarakhsi's (individual right to execute), and the Shafi'i/Maliki proof (caution requires a judge).
Also note the shubha argument: arbitrator's ruling is ambiguous for third parties.
4
Understand the final ruling and its practical application
Learn that later scholars accept permissibility in non-hudud/qisas matters (e.g., divorce) but instruct muftis not to give fatwa on it to prevent abuse.
This is an application of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means to evil).

اشرف البدایہ جلد - شمیم عوام دلیر اور جری ہو جائیں گے۔ اور ہر شخص اپنی منشاء کے مطابق حکم مقرر کر کے فیصلہ حاصل کرنے کی کوشش کرے گا۔ مثلا کسی نے ایک بارگی تین طلاقیں دیں حتی کہ ہمارے نزدیک یہ عورت بغیر حلالہ کے جائز نہیں رہی لیکن اگر ان کو حکم مقرر کرنے کے جائز ہونے کا فتوی معلوم ہو تو عورت و مردل کر ایک شافعی المذہب یا غیر مقلد کو اس معاملہ میں حکم مقرر کر لیں گے اور وہ ایک طلاق واقع ہونے کا حکم دے گا۔ اسی طرح جس شخص کو جس مسئلہ میں ضرورت پیش آئے گی وہ ایسے شخص کو تلاش کرے گا۔ جس کے نزدیک وہ بات جائز ہو۔ پس اس کو حکم بنا کر جواز حاصل کرے گا اگر چہ اس سے پہلے اس کو حرام تصور کرتا ہو۔ اس لئے مشائخ نے کہا کہ حکم بنانا اگر چہ جائز ہے لیکن اس کا فتوی نہ دیا جائے۔
313 The Book of the Etiquette of the Judge. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Volume 9: If he (the arbitrator) gave a verdict of blood money on the 'aqila, his verdict will not be enforceable, because he has no authority over the 'aqila, since they did not appoint him. If the arbitrator gave a verdict of blood money on the killer from his own wealth, the judge will reject it and order the 'aqila to pay, because it contradicts the judge's view and the text, unless the killing was proven by the killer's confession, because the 'aqila will not bear that blood money. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that arbitration is not permissible in hudud and qisas. Among our Hanafi scholars, this is the madhhab of Imam al-Khasaf, adopted by Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri and Sahib al-Hidayah. But here hudud refer to those that are pure rights of Allah, like hadd of zina and hadd of drinking wine. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said that arbitration is permissible in hadd of qadhf and qisas. Imam al-Shafi'i said that arbitration is permissible in property and things analogous to property, but not in others, and Imam Malik holds this view. Hence, hadd, li'an, qisas, qadhf, nasab, wala' are not property nor analogous to property, so arbitration is not permissible in them. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that all these matters are based on caution, so a specific judge is needed to issue a ruling; the arbitrator's decision is not sufficient. When not sufficient, arbitration is not permissible. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi's proof is that the right to execute hadd of qadhf and qisas belongs to the person slandered and the heirs of the slain; these are rights of individuals, so the slanderer and the slain's heirs have the right to appoint an arbitrator. Imam al-Khasaf's proof for non-permissibility is that people have no authority over their own life and blood, as no one is allowed to make their own blood permissible. Since they have no authority, their consent does not permit bloodshed. If consent does not permit bloodshed, then appointing an arbitrator for qisas is also not permissible. Sahib al-'Inaya said that this proof of Sahib al-Hidayah applies to non-permissibility in qisas but not in hudud. Some scholars presented another proof: the arbitrator's ruling is not binding on others, so it contains ambiguity (shubha). Hudud and qisas cannot be executed with ambiguity, so arbitration is not valid for them. Sahib al-Hidayah says that the later scholars said that Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri's specification of hudud and qisas indicates that arbitration is permissible in all other matters (like divorce, marriage, etc.). This is correct, but a fatwa will not be given; rather it will be said that the judge's ruling is needed. Because if a fatwa of permissibility is given, then the common people would become bold and everyone would seek arbitration according to his desire. For example, someone gave three divorces in one sitting, so according to us the woman is not lawful without halala. But if they know of a fatwa of permissibility, they would appoint a Shafi'i or non-muqallid arbitrator who would rule that only one divorce occurred. Similarly, whenever someone faces a need, he will search for someone who considers it permissible, and by appointing him as arbitrator, he will obtain permissibility even if he previously considered it forbidden. Hence the scholars said: Arbitration is permissible, but a fatwa is not given on it.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya, a commentary on al-Hidaya, discusses the ruling on private arbitration (tahkim) in different types of cases. It begins with a specific scenario: if two parties in a case of qatl khata (accidental killing) appoint an arbitrator, and the arbitrator rules that the 'aqila (the killer's clan responsible for paying blood money) must pay the diyat, that ruling is not enforceable because the 'aqila did not agree to arbitration. The arbitrator has no authority over them. If instead the arbitrator rules against the killer personally, the judge can override this and order the 'aqila to pay, as the arbitrator's ruling contradicts both the judge's view and the hadith text. An exception is if the killing was proven by the killer's own confession, in which case the 'aqila does not bear the diyat. The commentary then explains the general principles. According to al-Quduri, arbitration is not permissible in matters of hudud (fixed corporal punishments) and qisas (retaliation). This is the view of Imam al-Khasaf, adopted by al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidaya. Here, hudud refers only to those that are purely Allah's rights, like zina and drinking. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi distinguished: arbitration is permissible in hadd al-qadhf (false accusation) and qisas because these involve personal rights. The text also presents the views of Shafi'i and Maliki schools, which restrict arbitration to property matters. The core of the dispute is whether the parties have authority over the subject matter. For hudud that are pure rights of Allah, no one has authority to waive them, so arbitration is invalid. For qisas and qadhf, Sarakhsi argues that since the right belongs to the individual, they can appoint an arbitrator. Khasaf's counterargument is that no one has authority over their own life or blood, so even in qisas, arbitration is not valid. Another argument is that the arbitrator's ruling contains shubha (ambiguity) because it does not bind third parties, and hudud/qisas cannot be executed with shubha. The later scholars (masha'ikh muta'akhkhirin) then clarify that al-Quduri's restriction to hudud and qisas implies that arbitration is valid in all other matters, such as divorce and marriage. However, despite this permissibility, a fatwa should not be given to the public, as it would lead to widespread manipulation of rulings to suit personal desires. This is a classic example of the Hanafi fiqh principle of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means to evil), where a valid act is discouraged in practice due to its potential for misuse.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): In this context, a private arbitrator appointed by disputing parties to resolve a case outside the official court.
حدود (hudud): Fixed corporal punishments prescribed by Allah, such as for zina and drinking. In this passage, it excludes hadd al-qadhf according to some.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional killing or injury, a right of the victim or their heirs.
عاقلہ ('aqila): The group of male agnatic relatives (or tribe) who are collectively responsible for paying diyat in cases of accidental killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view in this passage, in which cases is private arbitration (tahkim) not permissible?
A) All property disputes
B) Hudud and qisas
C) Marriage and divorce
D) Only financial transactions

Key Takeaway
Private arbitration is impermissible in hudud and qisas, valid in other matters, but fatwa is withheld to prevent abuse.

Diyat on 'Aqlah and the Hakam's Ruling in Accidental Killing
Ruling on diyat liability and hakam's authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that diyat for accidental killing is on the 'aqlah, explain the exception for confession (iqrar), and evaluate whether a hakam's ruling against the 'aqlah is enforceable.

Core Idea
Diyat in accidental killing is on the clan ('aqlah), not the killer's own wealth, unless proven by confession.

In cases of accidental killing (qatl khata), Hanafi fiqh places the blood-money (diyah) on the 'aqlah—the killer's male relatives—not on the killer personally. This lesson examines the hadith evidence for this rule and its limits: if the killer confesses, liability shifts to him. It also addresses a practical problem: when parties appoint an arbitrator (hakam), can he rule that diyat is on the 'aqlah? The passage answers no, because the 'aqlah did not appoint him.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Accidental killing (qatl khata). What is the hukm? Diyat is wajib on the 'aqlah by default.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Mughira ibn Shu'ba is cited: the Prophet placed the ghurrah (compensation for a fetus) on the 'asabah ('aqlah) of the woman who caused the miscarriage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of placing the payment on the 'asabah indicates the legal principle that diyat in accidental killing is on the 'aqlah, not the killer's personal wealth.
4
Note the exception
If the killing is proven by the killer's confession (iqrar), then the liability shifts to the killer personally. The 'aqlah is not liable in that case.
5
Apply to the hakam's ruling
If a hakam rules that diyat is on the 'aqlah, that ruling is invalid because the 'aqlah did not appoint him. If the hakam rules that the killer pays from personal wealth, the qadi rejects it and rules on the 'aqlah instead, because the ruling contradicts the hadith and the qadi's madhhab.

Book of the Etiquette of the Judge. Ashraf al-Bidaya volume. The common people will become bold and daring. And every person will try to appoint an arbitrator according to his own wish to obtain a judgment. For example, someone gave three divorces at once, so according to us this woman is not permissible without halalah, but if they know the fatwa of permissibility of appointing an arbitrator, then the man and woman will appoint a Shafi'i or a non-muqallid as arbitrator in this matter, and he will rule that one divorce occurred. Similarly, whoever has a need in any issue will seek such a person for whom that matter is permissible. Then he will obtain permissibility by making him arbitrator, even if he previously considered it haram. Therefore, the mashayikh said that appointing an arbitrator is permissible, but fatwa should not be given on it. The author of Hidayah said: If two people appointed someone as arbitrator in a case of accidental killing, and the arbitrator ruled that the diyat is on the 'aqlah (helping clan), then this ruling of the arbitrator will not be enforced. Because the 'aqlah did not appoint him from their side, so the arbitrator has no authority over the 'aqlah. And when the arbitrator has no authority over the 'aqlah, his ruling will not be binding on them. And if the arbitrator ruled that the killer must pay diyat from his personal wealth, the qadi will reject this ruling and rule that the diyat is on the 'aqlah, because the arbitrator's ruling is against both the qadi's madhhab and the text of the hadith. The hadith is: From al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: Two wives [of a man] were [under one roof?]; one struck the other with a stone or a tent-peg, and she miscarried. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ruled for the fetus a ghurrah (a slave or slave-girl) and placed it on the 'asabah (male relatives, i.e., the 'aqlah) of the woman. Hadrat Mughirah says: two women were co-wives; one struck the other with a stone or a tent-peg, causing her to miscarry. The Prophet ruled that for the abortion a ghurrah – a slave or slave-girl – be given as blood-money, and placed it on the 'asabah ( 'aqlah) of the woman (the killer). Originally this incident was about the two wives of 'Amr ibn Malik. Then the Prophet told the relatives of the one who killed the fetus: 'Stand up and pay his blood-money (diyah).' From these two hadiths it is understood that diyat is obligatory on the 'aqlah, not on the killer's personal wealth. But if the killing is proven by the killer's confession, then in such a case it is permissible to rule that diyat is on the killer's personal wealth, because in that case diyat is not obligatory on the 'aqlah, but rather on the killer.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage discusses the liability for diyat in accidental killing (qatl khata). The author begins by warning against the practice of people appointing arbitrators (hakam) who will give rulings according to their own madhhab, which can lead to abuse. For example, if a man divorces his wife three times at once, according to the Hanafi school this woman becomes permanently haram without halalah. But if they appoint a Shafi'i or non-muqallid as hakam, he may rule that only one divorce occurred, thereby allowing remarriage without halalah. The author then states that the senior scholars (mashayikh) said that while appointing a hakam is permissible, one should not give a fatwa (i.e., encourage it). The text then focuses on a specific case: two people appointed a hakam in a case of accidental killing, and the hakam ruled that the diyat is on the 'aqlah (the clan). The author says this ruling is not enforceable because the 'aqlah did not appoint the hakam, so he has no authority over them. If the hakam ruled that the diyat is on the killer's personal wealth, the qadi would reject that and instead rule that it is on the 'aqlah, because the hakam's ruling contradicts both the qadi's madhhab and the explicit text of hadith. The hadith from Mughira ibn Shu'ba is cited: two co-wives, one threw a stone or tent-peg at the other, causing miscarriage. The Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled that a ghurrah (a slave) is due for the fetus and placed it on the 'aqlah of the woman (the killer). The author explains that this hadith and another similar hadith show that diyat is on the 'aqlah, not the killer's personal wealth. However, if the killing is proven by the killer's confession (iqrar), then the diyat is on the killer personally, because in that case the 'aqlah is not liable. This distinction is important for the hakam's ruling.

Key Terms
عاقلہ ('āqila): The clan or group of male relatives (asabah) who are liable to pay diyat on behalf of a killer in cases of accidental killing.
حکم (ḥakam): An arbitrator appointed by the parties to a dispute to give a binding ruling.
دیت (diyah): Blood-money paid as compensation for killing or injury, especially in accidental cases.
اقرار (iqrār): Confession, admission of liability by the accused.
قتل خطا (qatl khaṭā): Accidental killing, where the killer had no intent to kill.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a case of accidental killing, if the killer confesses (iqrar), who is liable for the diyat?
A) The 'aqlah (clan) exclusively
B) The killer from his personal wealth
C) Both the killer and the 'aqlah equally
D) The state treasury

Key Takeaway
Diyat in accidental killing is on the 'aqlah unless proven by the killer's confession; a hakam's ruling against the 'aqlah is unenforceable because they did not appoint him.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate

The Hakam's Authority to Hear Evidence, Rule on Nukul, and Accept Iqrar
Expansion of the hakam's procedural powers in arbitration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three permissible actions of a hakam during arbitration and distinguish between reports about facts (which are accepted) and reports about the judgment itself (which are not).

Core Idea
A hakam may hear evidence, rule on oath refusal, and accept confession; his report of a fact is trusted, but his report of the judgment is not because his authority ends.

In Hanafi fiqh, an arbitrator (hakam) appointed by two litigants has specific judicial powers. This passage from al-Quduri clarifies that the hakam may hear evidence, rule on the defendant's refusal to swear (nukul), and accept a confession (iqrar). It also draws a critical procedural distinction: if the hakam reports a fact that occurred during the arbitration, such as a confession or witness verification, his word is accepted as long as his authority continues; but if he reports that he has already given a judgment, his statement is not accepted because his authority ended with the judgment. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the rules of arbitration correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three permissible actions
List the three actions the hakam is permitted to do: hear bayyinah, rule on nukul, and accept iqrar. Base your list on the first line of the passage.
2
Understand the legal basis
The passage states that these actions are permissible because they are 'in accordance with Shari'ah'. Reflect on why this is sufficient: the hakam is authorized to do anything that aligns with Shari'ah, so these specific actions fall within his authority.
3
Distinguish between fact reports and judgment reports
The passage contrasts two situations: (a) the hakam reports a fact like iqrar or witness verification while the parties still hold him as arbitrator; (b) the hakam reports that he has already given judgment. Note the different rulings on accepting his statement in each case.
4
Apply the ruling to the distinction
Determine why the hakam's report of a fact is accepted (his wilayah continues) while his report of the judgment is not (wilayah ends with the judgment). Confirm this by the analogy with a qadi after removal.
5
Summarise the practical consequence
If the hakam says 'The defendant confessed before me' and then the defendant denies, the qadi accepts the hakam's word. But if the hakam says 'I gave judgment' and the losing party denies, his word is not accepted; the case must be reheard or other evidence provided.
